TOM The Adventures of Tom Sawyer
TOM 
TOM 				  by
TOM 
TOM 		Mark Twain (Samuel Langhorne Clemens)
TOM 
TOM Preface
TOM 
TOM MOST of the adventures recorded in this book really occurred; one or two
TOM were experiences of my own, the rest those of boys who were schoolmates
TOM of mine. Huck Finn is drawn from life; Tom Sawyer also, but not from an
TOM individual -- he is a combination of the characteristics of three boys
TOM whom I knew, and therefore belongs to the composite order of
TOM architecture.
TOM 
TOM The odd superstitions touched upon were all prevalent among children and
TOM slaves in the West at the period of this story -- that is to say, thirty
TOM or forty years ago.
TOM 
TOM Although my book is intended mainly for the entertainment of boys and
TOM girls, I hope it will not be shunned by men and women on that account,
TOM for part of my plan has been to try to pleasantly remind adults of what
TOM they once were themselves, and of how they felt and thought and talked,
TOM and what queer enterprises they sometimes engaged in.
TOM 
TOM THE AUTHOR.
TOM 
TOM HARTFORD, 1876.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter I
TOM 
TOM ``TOM!''
TOM 
TOM No answer.
TOM 
TOM ``TOM!''
TOM 
TOM No answer.
TOM 
TOM ``What's gone with that boy, I wonder? You TOM!''
TOM 
TOM No answer.
TOM 
TOM The old lady pulled her spectacles down and looked over them about the
TOM room; then she put them up and looked out under them. She seldom or
TOM never looked THROUGH them for so small a thing as a boy; they were her
TOM state pair, the pride of her heart, and were built for ``style,'' not
TOM service -- she could have seen through a pair of stove-lids just as
TOM well. She looked perplexed for a moment, and then said, not fiercely,
TOM but still loud enough for the furniture to hear:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I lay if I get hold of you I'll --''
TOM 
TOM She did not finish, for by this time she was bending down and punching
TOM under the bed with the broom, and so she needed breath to punctuate the
TOM punches with. She resurrected nothing but the cat.
TOM 
TOM ``I never did see the beat of that boy!''
TOM 
TOM She went to the open door and stood in it and looked out among the
TOM tomato vines and ``jimpson'' weeds that constituted the garden. No Tom.
TOM So she lifted up her voice at an angle calculated for distance and
TOM shouted:
TOM 
TOM ``Y-o-u-u TOM!''
TOM 
TOM There was a slight noise behind her and she turned just in time to seize
TOM a small boy by the slack of his roundabout and arrest his flight.
TOM 
TOM ``There! I might 'a' thought of that closet. What you been doing in
TOM there?''
TOM 
TOM ``Nothing.''
TOM 
TOM ``Nothing! Look at your hands. And look at your mouth. What IS that
TOM truck?''
TOM 
TOM ``I don't know, aunt.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I know. It's jam -- that's what it is. Forty times I've said if
TOM you didn't let that jam alone I'd skin you. Hand me that switch.''
TOM 
TOM The switch hovered in the air -- the peril was desperate --
TOM 
TOM ``My! Look behind you, aunt!''
TOM 
TOM The old lady whirled round, and snatched her skirts out of danger. The
TOM lad fled on the instant, scrambled up the high board-fence, and
TOM disappeared over it.
TOM 
TOM His aunt Polly stood surprised a moment, and then broke into a gentle
TOM laugh.
TOM 
TOM ``Hang the boy, can't I never learn anything? Ain't he played me tricks
TOM enough like that for me to be looking out for him by this time? But old
TOM fools is the biggest fools there is. Can't learn an old dog new tricks,
TOM as the saying is. But my goodness, he never plays them alike, two days,
TOM and how is a body to know what's coming? He 'pears to know just how long
TOM he can torment me before I get my dander up, and he knows if he can make
TOM out to put me off for a minute or make me laugh, it's all down again and
TOM I can't hit him a lick. I ain't doing my duty by that boy, and that's
TOM the Lord's truth, goodness knows. Spare the rod and spile the child, as
TOM the Good Book says. I'm a laying up sin and suffering for us both, I
TOM know. He's full of the Old Scratch, but laws-a-me! he's my own dead
TOM sister's boy, poor thing, and I ain't got the heart to lash him,
TOM somehow. Every time I let him off, my conscience does hurt me so, and
TOM every time I hit him my old heart most breaks. Well-a-well, man that is
TOM born of woman is of few days and full of trouble, as the Scripture says,
TOM and I reckon it's so. He'll play hookey this evening, * and [*
TOM Southwestern for ``afternoon''] I'll just be obleeged to make him work,
TOM to-morrow, to punish him. It's mighty hard to make him work Saturdays,
TOM when all the boys is having holiday, but he hates work more than he
TOM hates anything else, and I've GOT to do some of my duty by him, or I'll
TOM be the ruination of the child.''
TOM 
TOM Tom did play hookey, and he had a very good time. He got back home
TOM barely in season to help Jim, the small colored boy, saw next-day's wood
TOM and split the kindlings before supper -- at least he was there in time
TOM to tell his adventures to Jim while Jim did three-fourths of the work.
TOM Tom's younger brother (or rather half-brother) Sid was already through
TOM with his part of the work (picking up chips), for he was a quiet boy,
TOM and had no adventurous, troublesome ways.
TOM 
TOM While Tom was eating his supper, and stealing sugar as opportunity
TOM offered, Aunt Polly asked him questions that were full of guile, and
TOM very deep -- for she wanted to trap him into damaging revealments. Like
TOM many other simple-hearted souls, it was her pet vanity to believe she
TOM was endowed with a talent for dark and mysterious diplomacy, and she
TOM loved to contemplate her most transparent devices as marvels of low
TOM cunning. Said she:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, it was middling warm in school, warn't it?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes'm.''
TOM 
TOM ``Powerful warm, warn't it?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes'm.''
TOM 
TOM ``Didn't you want to go in a-swimming, Tom?''
TOM 
TOM A bit of a scare shot through Tom -- a touch of uncomfortable suspicion.
TOM He searched Aunt Polly's face, but it told him nothing. So he said:
TOM 
TOM ``No'm -- well, not very much.''
TOM 
TOM The old lady reached out her hand and felt Tom's shirt, and said:
TOM 
TOM ``But you ain't too warm now, though.'' And it flattered her to reflect
TOM that she had discovered that the shirt was dry without anybody knowing
TOM that that was what she had in her mind. But in spite of her, Tom knew
TOM where the wind lay, now. So he forestalled what might be the next move:
TOM 
TOM ``Some of us pumped on our heads -- mine's damp yet. See?''
TOM 
TOM Aunt Polly was vexed to think she had overlooked that bit of
TOM circumstantial evidence, and missed a trick. Then she had a new
TOM inspiration:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, you didn't have to undo your shirt collar where I sewed it, to
TOM pump on your head, did you? Unbutton your jacket!''
TOM 
TOM The trouble vanished out of Tom's face. He opened his jacket. His shirt
TOM collar was securely sewed.
TOM 
TOM ``Bother! Well, go 'long with you. I'd made sure you'd played hookey and
TOM been a-swimming. But I forgive ye, Tom. I reckon you're a kind of a
TOM singed cat, as the saying is -- better'n you look. THIS time.''
TOM 
TOM She was half sorry her sagacity had miscarried, and half glad that Tom
TOM had stumbled into obedient conduct for once.
TOM 
TOM But Sidney said:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, now, if I didn't think you sewed his collar with white thread,
TOM but it's black.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, I did sew it with white! Tom!''
TOM 
TOM But Tom did not wait for the rest. As he went out at the door he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Siddy, I'll lick you for that.''
TOM 
TOM In a safe place Tom examined two large needles which were thrust into
TOM the lapels of his jacket, and had thread bound about them -- one needle
TOM carried white thread and the other black. He said:
TOM 
TOM ``She'd never noticed if it hadn't been for Sid. Confound it! sometimes
TOM she sews it with white, and sometimes she sews it with black. I wish to
TOM geeminy she'd stick to one or t'other -- I can't keep the run of 'em.
TOM But I bet you I'll lam Sid for that. I'll learn him!''
TOM 
TOM He was not the Model Boy of the village. He knew the model boy very well
TOM though -- and loathed him.
TOM 
TOM Within two minutes, or even less, he had forgotten all his troubles. Not
TOM because his troubles were one whit less heavy and bitter to him than a
TOM man's are to a man, but because a new and powerful interest bore them
TOM down and drove them out of his mind for the time -- just as men's
TOM misfortunes are forgotten in the excitement of new enterprises. This new
TOM interest was a valued novelty in whistling, which he had just acquired
TOM from a negro, and he was suffering to practise it undisturbed. It
TOM consisted in a peculiar bird-like turn, a sort of liquid warble,
TOM produced by touching the tongue to the roof of the mouth at short
TOM intervals in the midst of the music -- the reader probably remembers how
TOM to do it, if he has ever been a boy. Diligence and attention soon gave
TOM him the knack of it, and he strode down the street with his mouth full
TOM of harmony and his soul full of gratitude. He felt much as an astronomer
TOM feels who has discovered a new planet -- no doubt, as far as strong,
TOM deep, unalloyed pleasure is concerned, the advantage was with the boy,
TOM not the astronomer.
TOM 
TOM The summer evenings were long. It was not dark, yet. Presently Tom
TOM checked his whistle. A stranger was before him -- a boy a shade larger
TOM than himself. A new-comer of any age or either sex was an impressive
TOM curiosity in the poor little shabby village of St. Petersburg. This boy
TOM was well dressed, too -- well dressed on a week-day. This was simply
TOM astounding. His cap was a dainty thing, his close-buttoned blue cloth
TOM roundabout was new and natty, and so were his pantaloons. He had shoes
TOM on -- and it was only Friday. He even wore a necktie, a bright bit of
TOM ribbon. He had a citified air about him that ate into Tom's vitals. The
TOM more Tom stared at the splendid marvel, the higher he turned up his nose
TOM at his finery and the shabbier and shabbier his own outfit seemed to him
TOM to grow. Neither boy spoke. If one moved, the other moved -- but only
TOM sidewise, in a circle; they kept face to face and eye to eye all the
TOM time. Finally Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``I can lick you!''
TOM 
TOM ``I'd like to see you try it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I can do it.''
TOM 
TOM ``No you can't, either.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes I can.''
TOM 
TOM ``No you can't.''
TOM 
TOM ``I can.''
TOM 
TOM ``You can't.''
TOM 
TOM ``Can!''
TOM 
TOM ``Can't!''
TOM 
TOM An uncomfortable pause. Then Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``What's your name?''
TOM 
TOM ``'Tisn't any of your business, maybe.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well I 'low I'll MAKE it my business.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well why don't you?''
TOM 
TOM ``If you say much, I will.''
TOM 
TOM ``Much -- much -- MUCH. There now.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, you think you're mighty smart, DON'T you? I could lick you with
TOM one hand tied behind me, if I wanted to.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well why don't you DO it? You SAY you can do it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well I WILL, if you fool with me.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh yes -- I've seen whole families in the same fix.''
TOM 
TOM ``Smarty! You think you're SOME, now, DON'T you? Oh, what a hat!''
TOM 
TOM ``You can lump that hat if you don't like it. I dare you to knock it off
TOM -- and anybody that'll take a dare will suck eggs.''
TOM 
TOM ``You're a liar!''
TOM 
TOM ``You're another.''
TOM 
TOM ``You're a fighting liar and dasn't take it up.''
TOM 
TOM ``Aw -- take a walk!''
TOM 
TOM ``Say -- if you give me much more of your sass I'll take and bounce a
TOM rock off'n your head.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, of COURSE you will.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well I WILL.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well why don't you DO it then? What do you keep SAYING you will for?
TOM Why don't you DO it? It's because you're afraid.''
TOM 
TOM ``I AIN'T afraid.''
TOM 
TOM ``You are.''
TOM 
TOM ``I ain't.''
TOM 
TOM ``You are.''
TOM 
TOM Another pause, and more eying and sidling around each other. Presently
TOM they were shoulder to shoulder. Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Get away from here!''
TOM 
TOM ``Go away yourself!''
TOM 
TOM ``I won't.''
TOM 
TOM ``I won't either.''
TOM 
TOM So they stood, each with a foot placed at an angle as a brace, and both
TOM shoving with might and main, and glowering at each other with hate. But
TOM neither could get an advantage. After struggling till both were hot and
TOM flushed, each relaxed his strain with watchful caution, and Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``You're a coward and a pup. I'll tell my big brother on you, and he can
TOM thrash you with his little finger, and I'll make him do it, too.''
TOM 
TOM ``What do I care for your big brother? I've got a brother that's bigger
TOM than he is -- and what's more, he can throw him over that fence, too.''
TOM [Both brothers were imaginary.]
TOM 
TOM ``That's a lie.''
TOM 
TOM ``YOUR saying so don't make it so.''
TOM 
TOM Tom drew a line in the dust with his big toe, and said:
TOM 
TOM ``I dare you to step over that, and I'll lick you till you can't stand
TOM up. Anybody that'll take a dare will steal sheep.''
TOM 
TOM The new boy stepped over promptly, and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Now you said you'd do it, now let's see you do it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Don't you crowd me now; you better look out.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, you SAID you'd do it -- why don't you do it?''
TOM 
TOM ``By jingo! for two cents I WILL do it.''
TOM 
TOM The new boy took two broad coppers out of his pocket and held them out
TOM with derision. Tom struck them to the ground. In an instant both boys
TOM were rolling and tumbling in the dirt, gripped together like cats; and
TOM for the space of a minute they tugged and tore at each other's hair and
TOM clothes, punched and scratched each other's nose, and covered themselves
TOM with dust and glory. Presently the confusion took form, and through the
TOM fog of battle Tom appeared, seated astride the new boy, and pounding him
TOM with his fists. ``Holler 'nuff!'' said he.
TOM 
TOM The boy only struggled to free himself. He was crying -- mainly from
TOM rage.
TOM 
TOM ``Holler 'nuff!'' -- and the pounding went on.
TOM 
TOM At last the stranger got out a smothered ``'Nuff!'' and Tom let him up
TOM and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Now that'll learn you. Better look out who you're fooling with next
TOM time.''
TOM 
TOM The new boy went off brushing the dust from his clothes, sobbing,
TOM snuffling, and occasionally looking back and shaking his head and
TOM threatening what he would do to Tom the ``next time he caught him out.''
TOM To which Tom responded with jeers, and started off in high feather, and
TOM as soon as his back was turned the new boy snatched up a stone, threw it
TOM and hit him between the shoulders and then turned tail and ran like an
TOM antelope. Tom chased the traitor home, and thus found out where he
TOM lived. He then held a position at the gate for some time, daring the
TOM enemy to come outside, but the enemy only made faces at him through the
TOM window and declined. At last the enemy's mother appeared, and called Tom
TOM a bad, vicious, vulgar child, and ordered him away. So he went away; but
TOM he said he ``'lowed'' to ``lay'' for that boy.
TOM 
TOM He got home pretty late that night, and when he climbed cautiously in at
TOM the window, he uncovered an ambuscade, in the person of his aunt; and
TOM when she saw the state his clothes were in her resolution to turn his
TOM Saturday holiday into captivity at hard labor became adamantine in its
TOM firmness.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter II
TOM 
TOM SATURDAY morning was come, and all the summer world was bright and
TOM fresh, and brimming with life. There was a song in every heart; and if
TOM the heart was young the music issued at the lips. There was cheer in
TOM every face and a spring in every step. The locust-trees were in bloom
TOM and the fragrance of the blossoms filled the air. Cardiff Hill, beyond
TOM the village and above it, was green with vegetation and it lay just far
TOM enough away to seem a Delectable Land, dreamy, reposeful, and inviting.
TOM 
TOM Tom appeared on the sidewalk with a bucket of whitewash and a
TOM long-handled brush. He surveyed the fence, and all gladness left him and
TOM a deep melancholy settled down upon his spirit. Thirty yards of board
TOM fence nine feet high. Life to him seemed hollow, and existence but a
TOM burden. Sighing, he dipped his brush and passed it along the topmost
TOM plank; repeated the operation; did it again; compared the insignificant
TOM whitewashed streak with the far-reaching continent of unwhitewashed
TOM fence, and sat down on a tree-box discouraged. Jim came skipping out at
TOM the gate with a tin pail, and singing Buffalo Gals. Bringing water from
TOM the town pump had always been hateful work in Tom's eyes, before, but
TOM now it did not strike him so. He remembered that there was company at
TOM the pump. White, mulatto, and negro boys and girls were always there
TOM waiting their turns, resting, trading playthings, quarrelling, fighting,
TOM skylarking. And he remembered that although the pump was only a hundred
TOM and fifty yards off, Jim never got back with a bucket of water under an
TOM hour -- and even then somebody generally had to go after him. Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Say, Jim, I'll fetch the water if you'll whitewash some.''
TOM 
TOM Jim shook his head and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Can't, Mars Tom. Ole missis, she tole me I got to go an' git dis water
TOM an' not stop foolin' roun' wid anybody. She say she spec' Mars Tom gwine
TOM to ax me to whitewash, an' so she tole me go 'long an' 'tend to my own
TOM business -- she 'lowed SHE'D 'tend to de whitewashin'.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, never you mind what she said, Jim. That's the way she always
TOM talks. Gimme the bucket -- I won't be gone only a a minute. SHE won't
TOM ever know.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, I dasn't, Mars Tom. Ole missis she'd take an' tar de head off'n
TOM me. 'Deed she would.''
TOM 
TOM ``SHE! She never licks anybody -- whacks 'em over the head with her
TOM thimble -- and who cares for that, I'd like to know. She talks awful,
TOM but talk don't hurt -- anyways it don't if she don't cry. Jim, I'll give
TOM you a marvel. I'll give you a white alley!''
TOM 
TOM Jim began to waver.
TOM 
TOM ``White alley, Jim! And it's a bully taw.''
TOM 
TOM ``My! Dat's a mighty gay marvel, I tell you! But Mars Tom I's powerful
TOM 'fraid ole missis --''
TOM 
TOM ``And besides, if you will I'll show you my sore toe.''
TOM 
TOM Jim was only human -- this attraction was too much for him. He put down
TOM his pail, took the white alley, and bent over the toe with absorbing
TOM interest while the bandage was being unwound. In another moment he was
TOM flying down the street with his pail and a tingling rear, Tom was
TOM whitewashing with vigor, and Aunt Polly was retiring from the field with
TOM a slipper in her hand and triumph in her eye.
TOM But Tom's energy did not last. He began to think of the fun he had
TOM planned for this day, and his sorrows multiplied. Soon the free boys
TOM would come tripping along on all sorts of delicious expeditions, and
TOM they would make a world of fun of him for having to work -- the very
TOM thought of it burnt him like fire. He got out his worldly wealth and
TOM examined it -- bits of toys, marbles, and trash; enough to buy an
TOM exchange of WORK, maybe, but not half enough to buy so much as half an
TOM hour of pure freedom. So he returned his straitened means to his pocket,
TOM and gave up the idea of trying to buy the boys. At this dark and
TOM hopeless moment an inspiration burst upon him! Nothing less than a
TOM great, magnificent inspiration.
TOM 
TOM He took up his brush and went tranquilly to work. Ben Rogers hove in
TOM sight presently -- the very boy, of all boys, whose ridicule he had been
TOM dreading. Ben's gait was the hop-skip-and-jump -- proof enough that his
TOM heart was light and his anticipations high. He was eating an apple, and
TOM giving a long, melodious whoop, at intervals, followed by a deep-toned
TOM ding-dong-dong, ding-dong-dong, for he was personating a steamboat. As
TOM he drew near, he slackened speed, took the middle of the street, leaned
TOM far over to star-board and rounded to ponderously and with laborious
TOM pomp and circumstance -- for he was personating the Big Missouri, and
TOM considered himself to be drawing nine feet of water. He was boat and
TOM captain and engine-bells combined, so he had to imagine himself standing
TOM on his own hurricane-deck giving the orders and executing them:
TOM 
TOM ``Stop her, sir! Ting-a-ling-ling!'' The headway ran almost out, and he
TOM drew up slowly toward the sidewalk.
TOM 
TOM ``Ship up to back! Ting-a-ling-ling!'' His arms straightened and
TOM stiffened down his sides.
TOM 
TOM ``Set her back on the stabboard! Ting-a-ling-ling! Chow! ch-chow-wow!
TOM Chow!'' His right hand, meantime, describing stately circles -- for it
TOM was representing a forty-foot wheel.
TOM 
TOM ``Let her go back on the labboard! Ting-a-ling-ling!
TOM Chow-ch-chow-chow!'' The left hand began to describe circles.
TOM 
TOM ``Stop the stabboard! Ting-a-ling-ling! Stop the labboard! Come ahead on
TOM the stabboard! Stop her! Let your outside turn over slow!
TOM Ting-a-ling-ling! Chow-ow-ow! Get out that head-line! LIVELY now! Come
TOM -- out with your spring-line -- what're you about there! Take a turn
TOM round that stump with the bight of it! Stand by that stage, now -- let
TOM her go! Done with the engines, sir! Ting-a-ling-ling! SH'T! S'H'T!
TOM SH'T!'' (trying the gauge-cocks).
TOM 
TOM Tom went on whitewashing -- paid no attention to the steamboat. Ben
TOM stared a moment and then said: ``Hi-YI! YOU'RE up a stump, ain't you!''
TOM 
TOM No answer. Tom surveyed his last touch with the eye of an artist, then
TOM he gave his brush another gentle sweep and surveyed the result, as
TOM before. Ben ranged up alongside of him. Tom's mouth watered for the
TOM apple, but he stuck to his work. Ben said:
TOM 
TOM ``Hello, old chap, you got to work, hey?''
TOM 
TOM Tom wheeled suddenly and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Why, it's you, Ben! I warn't noticing.''
TOM 
TOM ``Say -- I'm going in a-swimming, I am. Don't you wish you could? But of
TOM course you'd druther WORK -- wouldn't you? Course you would!''
TOM 
TOM Tom contemplated the boy a bit, and said:
TOM 
TOM ``What do you call work?''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, ain't THAT work?''
TOM 
TOM Tom resumed his whitewashing, and answered carelessly:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, maybe it is, and maybe it ain't. All I know, is, it suits Tom
TOM Sawyer.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh come, now, you don't mean to let on that you LIKE it?''
TOM 
TOM The brush continued to move.
TOM 
TOM ``Like it? Well, I don't see why I oughtn't to like it. Does a boy get a
TOM chance to whitewash a fence every day?''
TOM 
TOM That put the thing in a new light. Ben stopped nibbling his apple. Tom
TOM swept his brush daintily back and forth -- stepped back to note the
TOM effect -- added a touch here and there -- criticised the effect again --
TOM Ben watching every move and getting more and more interested, more and
TOM more absorbed. Presently he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Say, Tom, let ME whitewash a little.''
TOM 
TOM Tom considered, was about to consent; but he altered his mind:
TOM 
TOM ``No -- no -- I reckon it wouldn't hardly do, Ben. You see, Aunt Polly's
TOM awful particular about this fence -- right here on the street, you know
TOM -- but if it was the back fence I wouldn't mind and SHE wouldn't. Yes,
TOM she's awful particular about this fence; it's got to be done very
TOM careful; I reckon there ain't one boy in a thousand, maybe two thousand,
TOM that can do it the way it's got to be done.''
TOM 
TOM ``No -- is that so? Oh come, now -- lemme just try. Only just a little
TOM -- I'd let YOU, if you was me, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``Ben, I'd like to, honest injun; but Aunt Polly -- well, Jim wanted to
TOM do it, but she wouldn't let him; Sid wanted to do it, and she wouldn't
TOM let Sid. Now don't you see how I'm fixed? If you was to tackle this
TOM fence and anything was to happen to it --''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, shucks, I'll be just as careful. Now lemme try. Say -- I'll give
TOM you the core of my apple.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, here -- No, Ben, now don't. I'm afeard --''
TOM 
TOM ``I'll give you ALL of it!''
TOM 
TOM Tom gave up the brush with reluctance in his face, but alacrity in his
TOM heart. And while the late steamer Big Missouri worked and sweated in the
TOM sun, the retired artist sat on a barrel in the shade close by, dangled
TOM his legs, munched his apple, and planned the slaughter of more
TOM innocents. There was no lack of material; boys happened along every
TOM little while; they came to jeer, but remained to whitewash. By the time
TOM Ben was fagged out, Tom had traded the next chance to Billy Fisher for a
TOM kite, in good repair; and when he played out, Johnny Miller bought in
TOM for a dead rat and a string to swing it with -- and so on, and so on,
TOM hour after hour. And when the middle of the afternoon came, from being a
TOM poor poverty-stricken boy in the morning, Tom was literally rolling in
TOM wealth. He had besides the things before mentioned, twelve marbles, part
TOM of a jews-harp, a piece of blue bottle-glass to look through, a spool
TOM cannon, a key that wouldn't unlock anything, a fragment of chalk, a
TOM glass stopper of a decanter, a tin soldier, a couple of tadpoles, six
TOM fire-crackers, a kitten with only one eye, a brass door-knob, a
TOM dog-collar -- but no dog -- the handle of a knife, four pieces of
TOM orange-peel, and a dilapidated old window sash.
TOM 
TOM He had had a nice, good, idle time all the while -- plenty of company --
TOM and the fence had three coats of whitewash on it! If he hadn't run out
TOM of whitewash he would have bankrupted every boy in the village.
TOM 
TOM Tom said to himself that it was not such a hollow world, after all. He
TOM had discovered a great law of human action, without knowing it --
TOM namely, that in order to make a man or a boy covet a thing, it is only
TOM necessary to make the thing difficult to attain. If he had been a great
TOM and wise philosopher, like the writer of this book, he would now have
TOM comprehended that Work consists of whatever a body is OBLIGED to do, and
TOM that Play consists of whatever a body is not obliged to do. And this
TOM would help him to understand why constructing artificial flowers or
TOM performing on a tread-mill is work, while rolling ten-pins or climbing
TOM Mont Blanc is only amusement. There are wealthy gentlemen in England who
TOM drive four-horse passenger-coaches twenty or thirty miles on a daily
TOM line, in the summer, because the privilege costs them considerable
TOM money; but if they were offered wages for the service, that would turn
TOM it into work and then they would resign.
TOM 
TOM The boy mused awhile over the substantial change which had taken place
TOM in his worldly circumstances, and then wended toward headquarters to
TOM report.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter III
TOM 
TOM TOM presented himself before Aunt Polly, who was sitting by an open
TOM window in a pleasant rearward apartment, which was bedroom,
TOM breakfast-room, dining-room, and library, combined. The balmy summer
TOM air, the restful quiet, the odor of the flowers, and the drowsing murmur
TOM of the bees had had their effect, and she was nodding over her knitting
TOM -- for she had no company but the cat, and it was asleep in her lap. Her
TOM spectacles were propped up on her gray head for safety. She had thought
TOM that of course Tom had deserted long ago, and she wondered at seeing him
TOM place himself in her power again in this intrepid way. He said: ``Mayn't
TOM I go and play now, aunt?''
TOM 
TOM ``What, a'ready? How much have you done?''
TOM 
TOM ``It's all done, aunt.''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, don't lie to me -- I can't bear it.''
TOM 
TOM ``I ain't, aunt; it IS all done.''
TOM 
TOM Aunt Polly placed small trust in such evidence. She went out to see for
TOM herself; and she would have been content to find twenty per cent. of
TOM Tom's statement true. When she found the entire fence whitewashed, and
TOM not only whitewashed but elaborately coated and recoated, and even a
TOM streak added to the ground, her astonishment was almost unspeakable. She
TOM said:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I never! There's no getting round it, you can work when you're a
TOM mind to, Tom.'' And then she diluted the compliment by adding, ``But
TOM it's powerful seldom you're a mind to, I'm bound to say. Well, go 'long
TOM and play; but mind you get back some time in a week, or I'll tan you.''
TOM 
TOM She was so overcome by the splendor of his achievement that she took him
TOM into the closet and selected a choice apple and delivered it to him,
TOM along with an improving lecture upon the added value and flavor a treat
TOM took to itself when it came without sin through virtuous effort. And
TOM while she closed with a happy Scriptural flourish, he ``hooked'' a
TOM doughnut.
TOM 
TOM Then he skipped out, and saw Sid just starting up the outside stairway
TOM that led to the back rooms on the second floor. Clods were handy and the
TOM air was full of them in a twinkling. They raged around Sid like a
TOM hail-storm; and before Aunt Polly could collect her surprised faculties
TOM and sally to the rescue, six or seven clods had taken personal effect,
TOM and Tom was over the fence and gone. There was a gate, but as a general
TOM thing he was too crowded for time to make use of it. His soul was at
TOM peace, now that he had settled with Sid for calling attention to his
TOM black thread and getting him into trouble.
TOM 
TOM Tom skirted the block, and came round into a muddy alley that led by the
TOM back of his aunt's cow-stable. He presently got safely beyond the reach
TOM of capture and punishment, and hastened toward the public square of the
TOM village, where two ``military'' companies of boys had met for conflict,
TOM according to previous appointment. Tom was General of one of these
TOM armies, Joe Harper (a bosom friend) General of the other. These two
TOM great commanders did not condescend to fight in person -- that being
TOM better suited to the still smaller fry -- but sat together on an
TOM eminence and conducted the field operations by orders delivered through
TOM aides-de-camp. Tom's army won a great victory, after a long and
TOM hard-fought battle. Then the dead were counted, prisoners exchanged, the
TOM terms of the next disagreement agreed upon, and the day for the
TOM necessary battle appointed; after which the armies fell into line and
TOM marched away, and Tom turned homeward alone.
TOM 
TOM As he was passing by the house where Jeff Thatcher lived, he saw a new
TOM girl in the garden -- a lovely little blue-eyed creature with yellow
TOM hair plaited into two long-tails, white summer frock and embroidered
TOM pantalettes. The fresh-crowned hero fell without firing a shot. A
TOM certain Amy Lawrence vanished out of his heart and left not even a
TOM memory of herself behind. He had thought he loved her to distraction; he
TOM had regarded his passion as adoration; and behold it was only a poor
TOM little evanescent partiality. He had been months winning her; she had
TOM confessed hardly a week ago; he had been the happiest and the proudest
TOM boy in the world only seven short days, and here in one instant of time
TOM she had gone out of his heart like a casual stranger whose visit is
TOM done.
TOM 
TOM He worshipped this new angel with furtive eye, till he saw that she had
TOM discovered him; then he pretended he did not know she was present, and
TOM began to ``show off'' in all sorts of absurd boyish ways, in order to
TOM win her admiration. He kept up this grotesque foolishness for some time;
TOM but by-and-by, while he was in the midst of some dangerous gymnastic
TOM performances, he glanced aside and saw that the little girl was wending
TOM her way toward the house. Tom came up to the fence and leaned on it,
TOM grieving, and hoping she would tarry yet awhile longer. She halted a
TOM moment on the steps and then moved toward the door. Tom heaved a great
TOM sigh as she put her foot on the threshold. But his face lit up, right
TOM away, for she tossed a pansy over the fence a moment before she
TOM disappeared.
TOM 
TOM The boy ran around and stopped within a foot or two of the flower, and
TOM then shaded his eyes with his hand and began to look down street as if
TOM he had discovered something of interest going on in that direction.
TOM Presently he picked up a straw and began trying to balance it on his
TOM nose, with his head tilted far back; and as he moved from side to side,
TOM in his efforts, he edged nearer and nearer toward the pansy; finally his
TOM bare foot rested upon it, his pliant toes closed upon it, and he hopped
TOM away with the treasure and disappeared round the corner. But only for a
TOM minute -- only while he could button the flower inside his jacket, next
TOM his heart -- or next his stomach, possibly, for he was not much posted
TOM in anatomy, and not hypercritical, anyway.
TOM 
TOM He returned, now, and hung about the fence till nightfall, ``showing
TOM off,'' as before; but the girl never exhibited herself again, though Tom
TOM comforted himself a little with the hope that she had been near some
TOM window, meantime, and been aware of his attentions. Finally he strode
TOM home reluctantly, with his poor head full of visions.
TOM 
TOM All through supper his spirits were so high that his aunt wondered
TOM ``what had got into the child.'' He took a good scolding about clodding
TOM Sid, and did not seem to mind it in the least. He tried to steal sugar
TOM under his aunt's very nose, and got his knuckles rapped for it. He said:
TOM 
TOM ``Aunt, you don't whack Sid when he takes it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, Sid don't torment a body the way you do. You'd be always into
TOM that sugar if I warn't watching you.''
TOM 
TOM Presently she stepped into the kitchen, and Sid, happy in his immunity,
TOM reached for the sugar-bowl -- a sort of glorying over Tom which was
TOM wellnigh unbearable. But Sid's fingers slipped and the bowl dropped and
TOM broke. Tom was in ecstasies. In such ecstasies that he even controlled
TOM his tongue and was silent. He said to himself that he would not speak a
TOM word, even when his aunt came in, but would sit perfectly still till she
TOM asked who did the mischief; and then he would tell, and there would be
TOM nothing so good in the world as to see that pet model ``catch it.'' He
TOM was so brimful of exultation that he could hardly hold himself when the
TOM old lady came back and stood above the wreck discharging lightnings of
TOM wrath from over her spectacles. He said to himself, ``Now it's coming!''
TOM And the next instant he was sprawling on the floor! The potent palm was
TOM uplifted to strike again when Tom cried out:
TOM 
TOM ``Hold on, now, what 'er you belting ME for? -- Sid broke it!''
TOM 
TOM Aunt Polly paused, perplexed, and Tom looked for healing pity. But when
TOM she got her tongue again, she only said:
TOM 
TOM ``Umf! Well, you didn't get a lick amiss, I reckon. You been into some
TOM other audacious mischief when I wasn't around, like enough.''
TOM 
TOM Then her conscience reproached her, and she yearned to say something
TOM kind and loving; but she judged that this would be construed into a
TOM confession that she had been in the wrong, and discipline forbade that.
TOM So she kept silence, and went about her affairs with a troubled heart.
TOM Tom sulked in a corner and exalted his woes. He knew that in her heart
TOM his aunt was on her knees to him, and he was morosely gratified by the
TOM consciousness of it. He would hang out no signals, he would take notice
TOM of none. He knew that a yearning glance fell upon him, now and then,
TOM through a film of tears, but he refused recognition of it. He pictured
TOM himself lying sick unto death and his aunt bending over him beseeching
TOM one little forgiving word, but he would turn his face to the wall, and
TOM die with that word unsaid. Ah, how would she feel then? And he pictured
TOM himself brought home from the river, dead, with his curls all wet, and
TOM his sore heart at rest. How she would throw herself upon him, and how
TOM her tears would fall like rain, and her lips pray God to give her back
TOM her boy and she would never, never abuse him any more! But he would lie
TOM there cold and white and make no sign -- a poor little sufferer, whose
TOM griefs were at an end. He so worked upon his feelings with the pathos of
TOM these dreams, that he had to keep swallowing, he was so like to choke;
TOM and his eyes swam in a blur of water, which overflowed when he winked,
TOM and ran down and trickled from the end of his nose. And such a luxury to
TOM him was this petting of his sorrows, that he could not bear to have any
TOM worldly cheeriness or any grating delight intrude upon it; it was too
TOM sacred for such contact; and so, presently, when his cousin Mary danced
TOM in, all alive with the joy of seeing home again after an age-long visit
TOM of one week to the country, he got up and moved in clouds and darkness
TOM out at one door as she brought song and sunshine in at the other.
TOM 
TOM He wandered far from the accustomed haunts of boys, and sought desolate
TOM places that were in harmony with his spirit. A log raft in the river
TOM invited him, and he seated himself on its outer edge and contemplated
TOM the dreary vastness of the stream, wishing, the while, that he could
TOM only be drowned, all at once and unconsciously, without undergoing the
TOM uncomfortable routine devised by nature. Then he thought of his flower.
TOM He got it out, rumpled and wilted, and it mightily increased his dismal
TOM felicity. He wondered if she would pity him if she knew? Would she cry,
TOM and wish that she had a right to put her arms around his neck and
TOM comfort him? Or would she turn coldly away like all the hollow world?
TOM This picture brought such an agony of pleasurable suffering that he
TOM worked it over and over again in his mind and set it up in new and
TOM varied lights, till he wore it threadbare. At last he rose up sighing
TOM and departed in the darkness.
TOM 
TOM About half-past nine or ten o'clock he came along the deserted street to
TOM where the Adored Unknown lived; he paused a moment; no sound fell upon
TOM his listening ear; a candle was casting a dull glow upon the curtain of
TOM a second-story window. Was the sacred presence there? He climbed the
TOM fence, threaded his stealthy way through the plants, till he stood under
TOM that window; he looked up at it long, and with emotion; then he laid him
TOM down on the ground under it, disposing himself upon his back, with his
TOM hands clasped upon his breast and holding his poor wilted flower. And
TOM thus he would die -- out in the cold world, with no shelter over his
TOM homeless head, no friendly hand to wipe the death-damps from his brow,
TOM no loving face to bend pityingly over him when the great agony came. And
TOM thus SHE would see him when she looked out upon the glad morning, and
TOM oh! would she drop one little tear upon his poor, lifeless form, would
TOM she heave one little sigh to see a bright young life so rudely blighted,
TOM so untimely cut down?
TOM 
TOM The window went up, a maid-servant's discordant voice profaned the holy
TOM calm, and a deluge of water drenched the prone martyr's remains!
TOM 
TOM The strangling hero sprang up with a relieving snort. There was a whiz
TOM as of a missile in the air, mingled with the murmur of a curse, a sound
TOM as of shivering glass followed, and a small, vague form went over the
TOM fence and shot away in the gloom.
TOM 
TOM Not long after, as Tom, all undressed for bed, was surveying his
TOM drenched garments by the light of a tallow dip, Sid woke up; but if he
TOM had any dim idea of making any ``references to allusions,'' he thought
TOM better of it and held his peace, for there was danger in Tom's eye.
TOM 
TOM Tom turned in without the added vexation of prayers, and Sid made mental
TOM note of the omission.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter IV
TOM 
TOM THE sun rose upon a tranquil world, and beamed down upon the peaceful
TOM village like a benediction. Breakfast over, Aunt Polly had family
TOM worship: it began with a prayer built from the ground up of solid
TOM courses of Scriptural quotations, welded together with a thin mortar of
TOM originality; and from the summit of this she delivered a grim chapter of
TOM the Mosaic Law, as from Sinai.
TOM 
TOM Then Tom girded up his loins, so to speak, and went to work to ``get his
TOM verses.'' Sid had learned his lesson days before. Tom bent all his
TOM energies to the memorizing of five verses, and he chose part of the
TOM Sermon on the Mount, because he could find no verses that were shorter.
TOM At the end of half an hour Tom had a vague general idea of his lesson,
TOM but no more, for his mind was traversing the whole field of human
TOM thought, and his hands were busy with distracting recreations. Mary took
TOM his book to hear him recite, and he tried to find his way through the
TOM fog:
TOM 
TOM ``Blessed are the -- a -- a --''
TOM 
TOM ``Poor'' --
TOM 
TOM ``Yes -- poor; blessed are the poor -- a -- a --''
TOM 
TOM ``In spirit --''
TOM 
TOM ``In spirit; blessed are the poor in spirit, for they -- they --''
TOM 
TOM ``THEIRS --''
TOM 
TOM ``For THEIRS. Blessed are the poor in spirit, for theirs is the kingdom
TOM of heaven. Blessed are they that mourn, for they -- they --''
TOM 
TOM ``Sh --''
TOM 
TOM ``For they -- a --''
TOM 
TOM ``S, H, A --''
TOM 
TOM ``For they S, H -- Oh, I don't know what it is!''
TOM 
TOM ``SHALL!''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, SHALL! for they shall -- for they shall -- a -- a -- shall mourn
TOM -- a-- a -- blessed are they that shall -- they that -- a -- they that
TOM shall mourn, for they shall -- a -- shall WHAT? Why don't you tell me,
TOM Mary? -- what do you want to be so mean for?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, Tom, you poor thick-headed thing, I'm not teasing you. I wouldn't
TOM do that. You must go and learn it again. Don't you be discouraged, Tom,
TOM you'll manage it -- and if you do, I'll give you something ever so nice.
TOM There, now, that's a good boy.''
TOM 
TOM ``All right! What is it, Mary, tell me what it is.''
TOM 
TOM ``Never you mind, Tom. You know if I say it's nice, it is nice.''
TOM 
TOM ``You bet you that's so, Mary. All right, I'll tackle it again.''
TOM 
TOM And he did ``tackle it again'' -- and under the double pressure of
TOM curiosity and prospective gain he did it with such spirit that he
TOM accomplished a shining success. Mary gave him a brand-new ``Barlow''
TOM knife worth twelve and a half cents; and the convulsion of delight that
TOM swept his system shook him to his foundations. True, the knife would not
TOM cut anything, but it was a ``sure-enough'' Barlow, and there was
TOM inconceivable grandeur in that -- though where the Western boys ever got
TOM the idea that such a weapon could possibly be counterfeited to its
TOM injury is an imposing mystery and will always remain so, perhaps. Tom
TOM contrived to scarify the cupboard with it, and was arranging to begin on
TOM the bureau, when he was called off to dress for Sunday-school.
TOM 
TOM Mary gave him a tin basin of water and a piece of soap, and he went
TOM outside the door and set the basin on a little bench there; then he
TOM dipped the soap in the water and laid it down; turned up his sleeves;
TOM poured out the water on the ground, gently, and then entered the kitchen
TOM and began to wipe his face diligently on the towel behind the door. But
TOM Mary removed the towel and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Now ain't you ashamed, Tom. You mustn't be so bad. Water won't hurt
TOM you.''
TOM 
TOM Tom was a trifle disconcerted. The basin was refilled, and this time he
TOM stood over it a little while, gathering resolution; took in a big breath
TOM and began. When he entered the kitchen presently, with both eyes shut
TOM and groping for the towel with his hands, an honorable testimony of suds
TOM and water was dripping from his face. But when he emerged from the
TOM towel, he was not yet satisfactory, for the clean territory stopped
TOM short at his chin and his jaws, like a mask; below and beyond this line
TOM there was a dark expanse of unirrigated soil that spread downward in
TOM front and backward around his neck. Mary took him in hand, and when she
TOM was done with him he was a man and a brother, without distinction of
TOM color, and his saturated hair was neatly brushed, and its short curls
TOM wrought into a dainty and symmetrical general effect. [He privately
TOM smoothed out the curls, with labor and difficulty, and plastered his
TOM hair close down to his head; for he held curls to be effeminate, and his
TOM own filled his life with bitterness.] Then Mary got out a suit of his
TOM clothing that had been used only on Sundays during two years -- they
TOM were simply called his ``other clothes'' -- and so by that we know the
TOM size of his wardrobe. The girl ``put him to rights'' after he had
TOM dressed himself; she buttoned his neat roundabout up to his chin, turned
TOM his vast shirt collar down over his shoulders, brushed him off and
TOM crowned him with his speckled straw hat. He now looked exceedingly
TOM improved and uncomfortable. He was fully as uncomfortable as he looked;
TOM for there was a restraint about whole clothes and cleanliness that
TOM galled him. He hoped that Mary would forget his shoes, but the hope was
TOM blighted; she coated them thoroughly with tallow, as was the custom, and
TOM brought them out. He lost his temper and said he was always being made
TOM to do everything he didn't want to do. But Mary said, persuasively:
TOM 
TOM ``Please, Tom -- that's a good boy.''
TOM 
TOM So he got into the shoes snarling. Mary was soon ready, and the three
TOM children set out for Sunday-school -- a place that Tom hated with his
TOM whole heart; but Sid and Mary were fond of it.
TOM 
TOM Sabbath-school hours were from nine to half-past ten; and then church
TOM service. Two of the children always remained for the sermon voluntarily,
TOM and the other always remained too -- for stronger reasons. The church's
TOM high-backed, uncushioned pews would seat about three hundred persons;
TOM the edifice was but a small, plain affair, with a sort of pine board
TOM tree-box on top of it for a steeple. At the door Tom dropped back a step
TOM and accosted a Sunday-dressed comrade:
TOM 
TOM ``Say, Billy, got a yaller ticket?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes.''
TOM 
TOM ``What'll you take for her?''
TOM 
TOM ``What'll you give?''
TOM 
TOM ``Piece of lickrish and a fish-hook.''
TOM 
TOM ``Less see 'em.''
TOM 
TOM Tom exhibited. They were satisfactory, and the property changed hands.
TOM Then Tom traded a couple of white alleys for three red tickets, and some
TOM small trifle or other for a couple of blue ones. He waylaid other boys
TOM as they came, and went on buying tickets of various colors ten or
TOM fifteen minutes longer. He entered the church, now, with a swarm of
TOM clean and noisy boys and girls, proceeded to his seat and started a
TOM quarrel with the first boy that came handy. The teacher, a grave,
TOM elderly man, interfered; then turned his back a moment and Tom pulled a
TOM boy's hair in the next bench, and was absorbed in his book when the boy
TOM turned around; stuck a pin in another boy, presently, in order to hear
TOM him say ``Ouch!'' and got a new reprimand from his teacher. Tom's whole
TOM class were of a pattern -- restless, noisy, and troublesome. When they
TOM came to recite their lessons, not one of them knew his verses perfectly,
TOM but had to be prompted all along. However, they worried through, and
TOM each got his reward -- in small blue tickets, each with a passage of
TOM Scripture on it; each blue ticket was pay for two verses of the
TOM recitation. Ten blue tickets equalled a red one, and could be exchanged
TOM for it; ten red tickets equalled a yellow one; for ten yellow tickets
TOM the superintendent gave a very plainly bound Bible (worth forty cents in
TOM those easy times) to the pupil. How many of my readers would have the
TOM industry and application to memorize two thousand verses, even for a
TOM Dore Bible? And yet Mary had acquired two Bibles in this way -- it was
TOM the patient work of two years -- and a boy of German parentage had won
TOM four or five. He once recited three thousand verses without stopping;
TOM but the strain upon his mental faculties was too great, and he was
TOM little better than an idiot from that day forth -- a grievous misfortune
TOM for the school, for on great occasions, before company, the
TOM superintendent (as Tom expressed it) had always made this boy come out
TOM and ``spread himself.'' Only the older pupils managed to keep their
TOM tickets and stick to their tedious work long enough to get a Bible, and
TOM so the delivery of one of these prizes was a rare and noteworthy
TOM circumstance; the successful pupil was so great and conspicuous for that
TOM day that on the spot every scholar's heart was fired with a fresh
TOM ambition that often lasted a couple of weeks. It is possible that Tom's
TOM mental stomach had never really hungered for one of those prizes, but
TOM unquestionably his entire being had for many a day longed for the glory
TOM and the eclat that came with it.
TOM 
TOM In due course the superintendent stood up in front of the pulpit, with a
TOM closed hymn-book in his hand and his forefinger inserted between its
TOM leaves, and commanded attention. When a Sunday-school superintendent
TOM makes his customary little speech, a hymn-book in the hand is as
TOM necessary as is the inevitable sheet of music in the hand of a singer
TOM who stands forward on the platform and sings a solo at a concert --
TOM though why, is a mystery: for neither the hymn-book nor the sheet of
TOM music is ever referred to by the sufferer. This superintendent was a
TOM slim creature of thirty-five, with a sandy goatee and short sandy hair;
TOM he wore a stiff standing-collar whose upper edge almost reached his ears
TOM and whose sharp points curved forward abreast the corners of his mouth
TOM -- a fence that compelled a straight lookout ahead, and a turning of the
TOM whole body when a side view was required; his chin was propped on a
TOM spreading cravat which was as broad and as long as a bank-note, and had
TOM fringed ends; his boot toes were turned sharply up, in the fashion of
TOM the day, like sleigh-runners -- an effect patiently and laboriously
TOM produced by the young men by sitting with their toes pressed against a
TOM wall for hours together. Mr. Walters was very earnest of mien, and very
TOM sincere and honest at heart; and he held sacred things and places in
TOM such reverence, and so separated them from worldly matters, that
TOM unconsciously to himself his Sunday-school voice had acquired a peculiar
TOM intonation which was wholly absent on week-days. He began after this
TOM fashion:
TOM 
TOM ``Now, children, I want you all to sit up just as straight and pretty as
TOM you can and give me all your attention for a minute or two. There --
TOM that is it. That is the way good little boys and girls should do. I see
TOM one little girl who is looking out of the window -- I am afraid she
TOM thinks I am out there somewhere -- perhaps up in one of the trees making
TOM a speech to the little birds. [Applausive titter.] I want to tell you
TOM how good it makes me feel to see so many bright, clean little faces
TOM assembled in a place like this, learning to do right and be good.'' And
TOM so forth and so on. It is not necessary to set down the rest of the
TOM oration. It was of a pattern which does not vary, and so it is familiar
TOM to us all.
TOM 
TOM The latter third of the speech was marred by the resumption of fights
TOM and other recreations among certain of the bad boys, and by fidgetings
TOM and whisperings that extended far and wide, washing even to the bases of
TOM isolated and incorruptible rocks like Sid and Mary. But now every sound
TOM ceased suddenly, with the subsidence of Mr. Walters' voice, and the
TOM conclusion of the speech was received with a burst of silent gratitude.
TOM 
TOM A good part of the whispering had been occasioned by an event which was
TOM more or less rare -- the entrance of visitors: lawyer Thatcher,
TOM accompanied by a very feeble and aged man; a fine, portly, middle-aged
TOM gentleman with iron-gray hair; and a dignified lady who was doubtless
TOM the latter's wife. The lady was leading a child. Tom had been restless
TOM and full of chafings and repinings; conscience-smitten, too -- he could
TOM not meet Amy Lawrence's eye, he could not brook her loving gaze. But
TOM when he saw this small new-comer his soul was all ablaze with bliss in a
TOM moment. The next moment he was ``showing off'' with all his might --
TOM cuffing boys, pulling hair, making faces -- in a word, using every art
TOM that seemed likely to fascinate a girl and win her applause. His
TOM exaltation had but one alloy -- the memory of his humiliation in this
TOM angel's garden -- and that record in sand was fast washing out, under
TOM the waves of happiness that were sweeping over it now.
TOM 
TOM The visitors were given the highest seat of honor, and as soon as Mr.
TOM Walters' speech was finished, he introduced them to the school. The
TOM middle-aged man turned out to be a prodigious personage -- no less a one
TOM than the county judge -- altogether the most august creation these
TOM children had ever looked upon -- and they wondered what kind of material
TOM he was made of -- and they half wanted to hear him roar, and were half
TOM afraid he might, too. He was from Constantinople, twelve miles away --
TOM so he had travelled, and seen the world -- these very eyes had looked
TOM upon the county court-house -- which was said to have a tin roof. The
TOM awe which these reflections inspired was attested by the impressive
TOM silence and the ranks of staring eyes. This was the great Judge
TOM Thatcher, brother of their own lawyer. Jeff Thatcher immediately went
TOM forward, to be familiar with the great man and be envied by the school.
TOM It would have been music to his soul to hear the whisperings:
TOM 
TOM ``Look at him, Jim! He's a going up there. Say -- look! he's a going to
TOM shake hands with him -- he IS shaking hands with him! By jings, don't
TOM you wish you was Jeff?''
TOM 
TOM Mr. Walters fell to ``showing off,'' with all sorts of official
TOM bustlings and activities, giving orders, delivering judgments,
TOM discharging directions here, there, everywhere that he could find a
TOM target. The librarian ``showed off'' -- running hither and thither with
TOM his arms full of books and making a deal of the splutter and fuss that
TOM insect authority delights in. The young lady teachers ``showed off'' --
TOM bending sweetly over pupils that were lately being boxed, lifting pretty
TOM warning fingers at bad little boys and patting good ones lovingly. The
TOM young gentlemen teachers ``showed off'' with small scoldings and other
TOM little displays of authority and fine attention to discipline -- and
TOM most of the teachers, of both sexes, found business up at the library,
TOM by the pulpit; and it was business that frequently had to be done over
TOM again two or three times (with much seeming vexation). The little girls
TOM ``showed off'' in various ways, and the little boys ``showed off'' with
TOM such diligence that the air was thick with paper wads and the murmur of
TOM scufflings. And above it all the great man sat and beamed a majestic
TOM judicial smile upon all the house, and warmed himself in the sun of his
TOM own grandeur -- for he was ``showing off,'' too.
TOM 
TOM There was only one thing wanting to make Mr. Walters' ecstasy complete,
TOM and that was a chance to deliver a Bible-prize and exhibit a prodigy.
TOM Several pupils had a few yellow tickets, but none had enough -- he had
TOM been around among the star pupils inquiring. He would have given worlds,
TOM now, to have that German lad back again with a sound mind.
TOM 
TOM And now at this moment, when hope was dead, Tom Sawyer came forward with
TOM nine yellow tickets, nine red tickets, and ten blue ones, and demanded a
TOM Bible. This was a thunderbolt out of a clear sky. Walters was not
TOM expecting an application from this source for the next ten years. But
TOM there was no getting around it -- here were the certified checks, and
TOM they were good for their face. Tom was therefore elevated to a place
TOM with the Judge and the other elect, and the great news was announced
TOM from head-quarters. It was the most stunning surprise of the decade, and
TOM so profound was the sensation that it lifted the new hero up to the
TOM judicial one's altitude, and the school had two marvels to gaze upon in
TOM place of one. The boys were all eaten up with envy -- but those that
TOM suffered the bitterest pangs were those who perceived too late that they
TOM themselves had contributed to this hated splendor by trading tickets to
TOM Tom for the wealth he had amassed in selling whitewashing privileges.
TOM These despised themselves, as being the dupes of a wily fraud, a
TOM guileful snake in the grass.
TOM 
TOM The prize was delivered to Tom with as much effusion as the
TOM superintendent could pump up under the circumstances; but it lacked
TOM somewhat of the true gush, for the poor fellow's instinct taught him
TOM that there was a mystery here that could not well bear the light,
TOM perhaps; it was simply preposterous that this boy had warehoused two
TOM thousand sheaves of Scriptural wisdom on his premises -- a dozen would
TOM strain his capacity, without a doubt.
TOM 
TOM Amy Lawrence was proud and glad, and she tried to make Tom see it in her
TOM face -- but he wouldn't look. She wondered; then she was just a grain
TOM troubled; next a dim suspicion came and went -- came again; she watched;
TOM a furtive glance told her worlds -- and then her heart broke, and she
TOM was jealous, and angry, and the tears came and she hated everybody. Tom
TOM most of all (she thought).
TOM 
TOM Tom was introduced to the Judge; but his tongue was tied, his breath
TOM would hardly come, his heart quaked -- partly because of the awful
TOM greatness of the man, but mainly because he was her parent. He would
TOM have liked to fall down and worship him, if it were in the dark. The
TOM Judge put his hand on Tom's head and called him a fine little man, and
TOM asked him what his name was. The boy stammered, gasped, and got it out:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, no, not Tom -- it is --''
TOM 
TOM ``Thomas.''
TOM 
TOM ``Ah, that's it. I thought there was more to it, maybe. That's very
TOM well. But you've another one I daresay, and you'll tell it to me, won't
TOM you?''
TOM 
TOM ``Tell the gentleman your other name, Thomas,'' said Walters, ``and say
TOM sir. You mustn't forget your manners.''
TOM 
TOM ``Thomas Sawyer -- sir.''
TOM 
TOM ``That's it! That's a good boy. Fine boy. Fine, manly little fellow. Two
TOM thousand verses is a great many -- very, very great many. And you never
TOM can be sorry for the trouble you took to learn them; for knowledge is
TOM worth more than anything there is in the world; it's what makes great
TOM men and good men; you'll be a great man and a good man yourself, some
TOM day, Thomas, and then you'll look back and say, It's all owing to the
TOM precious Sunday-school privileges of my boyhood -- it's all owing to my
TOM dear teachers that taught me to learn -- it's all owing to the good
TOM superintendent, who encouraged me, and watched over me, and gave me a
TOM beautiful Bible -- a splendid elegant Bible -- to keep and have it all
TOM for my own, always -- it's all owing to right bringing up! That is what
TOM you will say, Thomas -- and you wouldn't take any money for those two
TOM thousand verses -- no indeed you wouldn't. And now you wouldn't mind
TOM telling me and this lady some of the things you've learned -- no, I know
TOM you wouldn't -- for we are proud of little boys that learn. Now, no
TOM doubt you know the names of all the twelve disciples. Won't you tell us
TOM the names of the first two that were appointed?''
TOM 
TOM Tom was tugging at a button-hole and looking sheepish. He blushed, now,
TOM and his eyes fell. Mr. Walters' heart sank within him. He said to
TOM himself, it is not possible that the boy can answer the simplest
TOM question -- why DID the Judge ask him? Yet he felt obliged to speak up
TOM and say:
TOM 
TOM ``Answer the gentleman, Thomas -- don't be afraid.''
TOM 
TOM Tom still hung fire.
TOM 
TOM ``Now I know you'll tell me,'' said the lady. ``The names of the first
TOM two disciples were --''
TOM 
TOM ``DAVID AND GOLIAH!''
TOM 
TOM Let us draw the curtain of charity over the rest of the scene.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter V
TOM 
TOM ABOUT half-past ten the cracked bell of the small church began to ring,
TOM and presently the people began to gather for the morning sermon. The
TOM Sunday-school children distributed themselves about the house and
TOM occupied pews with their parents, so as to be under supervision. Aunt
TOM Polly came, and Tom and Sid and Mary sat with her -- Tom being placed
TOM next the aisle, in order that he might be as far away from the open
TOM window and the seductive outside summer scenes as possible. The crowd
TOM filed up the aisles: the aged and needy postmaster, who had seen better
TOM days; the mayor and his wife -- for they had a mayor there, among other
TOM unnecessaries; the justice of the peace; the widow Douglass, fair,
TOM smart, and forty, a generous, good-hearted soul and well-to-do, her hill
TOM mansion the only palace in the town, and the most hospitable and much
TOM the most lavish in the matter of festivities that St. Petersburg could
TOM boast; the bent and venerable Major and Mrs. Ward; lawyer Riverson, the
TOM new notable from a distance; next the belle of the village, followed by
TOM a troop of lawn-clad and ribbon-decked young heart-breakers; then all
TOM the young clerks in town in a body -- for they had stood in the
TOM vestibule sucking their cane-heads, a circling wall of oiled and
TOM simpering admirers, till the last girl had run their gantlet; and last
TOM of all came the Model Boy, Willie Mufferson, taking as heedful care of
TOM his mother as if she were cut glass. He always brought his mother to
TOM church, and was the pride of all the matrons. The boys all hated him, he
TOM was so good. And besides, he had been ``thrown up to them'' so much. His
TOM white handkerchief was hanging out of his pocket behind, as usual on
TOM Sundays -- accidentally. Tom had no handkerchief, and he looked upon
TOM boys who had as snobs.
TOM 
TOM The congregation being fully assembled, now, the bell rang once more, to
TOM warn laggards and stragglers, and then a solemn hush fell upon the
TOM church which was only broken by the tittering and whispering of the
TOM choir in the gallery. The choir always tittered and whispered all
TOM through service. There was once a church choir that was not ill-bred,
TOM but I have forgotten where it was, now. It was a great many years ago,
TOM and I can scarcely remember anything about it, but I think it was in
TOM some foreign country.
TOM 
TOM The minister gave out the hymn, and read it through with a relish, in a
TOM peculiar style which was much admired in that part of the country. His
TOM voice began on a medium key and climbed steadily up till it reached a
TOM certain point, where it bore with strong emphasis upon the topmost word
TOM and then plunged down as if from a spring-board:
TOM 
TOM Shall I be car-ri-ed toe the skies, on flow'ry BEDS of ease, Whilst
TOM others fight to win the prize, and sail thro' BLOOD y seas?
TOM 
TOM He was regarded as a wonderful reader. At church ``sociables'' he was
TOM always called upon to read poetry; and when he was through, the ladies
TOM would lift up their hands and let them fall helplessly in their laps,
TOM and ``wall'' their eyes, and shake their heads, as much as to say,
TOM ``Words cannot express it; it is too beautiful, TOO beautiful for this
TOM mortal earth.''
TOM 
TOM After the hymn had been sung, the Rev. Mr. Sprague turned himself into a
TOM bulletin-board, and read off ``notices'' of meetings and societies and
TOM things till it seemed that the list would stretch out to the crack of
TOM doom -- a queer custom which is still kept up in America, even in
TOM cities, away here in this age of abundant newspapers. Often, the less
TOM there is to justify a traditional custom, the harder it is to get rid of
TOM it.
TOM 
TOM And now the minister prayed. A good, generous prayer it was, and went
TOM into details: it pleaded for the church, and the little children of the
TOM church; for the other churches of the village; for the village itself;
TOM for the county; for the State; for the State officers; for the United
TOM States; for the churches of the United States; for Congress; for the
TOM President; for the officers of the Government; for poor sailors, tossed
TOM by stormy seas; for the oppressed millions groaning under the heel of
TOM European monarchies and Oriental despotisms; for such as have the light
TOM and the good tidings, and yet have not eyes to see nor ears to hear
TOM withal; for the heathen in the far islands of the sea; and closed with a
TOM supplication that the words he was about to speak might find grace and
TOM favor, and be as seed sown in fertile ground, yielding in time a
TOM grateful harvest of good. Amen.
TOM 
TOM There was a rustling of dresses, and the standing congregation sat down.
TOM The boy whose history this book relates did not enjoy the prayer, he
TOM only endured it -- if he even did that much. He was restive all through
TOM it; he kept tally of the details of the prayer, unconsciously -- for he
TOM was not listening, but he knew the ground of old, and the clergyman's
TOM regular route over it -- and when a little trifle of new matter was
TOM interlarded, his ear detected it and his whole nature resented it; he
TOM considered additions unfair, and scoundrelly. In the midst of the prayer
TOM a fly had lit on the back of the pew in front of him and tortured his
TOM spirit by calmly rubbing its hands together, embracing its head with its
TOM arms, and polishing it so vigorously that it seemed to almost part
TOM company with the body, and the slender thread of a neck was exposed to
TOM view; scraping its wings with its hind legs and smoothing them to its
TOM body as if they had been coat-tails; going through its whole toilet as
TOM tranquilly as if it knew it was perfectly safe. As indeed it was; for as
TOM sorely as Tom's hands itched to grab for it they did not dare -- he
TOM believed his soul would be instantly destroyed if he did such a thing
TOM while the prayer was going on. But with the closing sentence his hand
TOM began to curve and steal forward; and the instant the ``Amen'' was out
TOM the fly was a prisoner of war. His aunt detected the act and made him
TOM let it go.
TOM 
TOM The minister gave out his text and droned along monotonously through an
TOM argument that was so prosy that many a head by and by began to nod --
TOM and yet it was an argument that dealt in limitless fire and brimstone
TOM and thinned the predestined elect down to a company so small as to be
TOM hardly worth the saving. Tom counted the pages of the sermon; after
TOM church he always knew how many pages there had been, but he seldom knew
TOM anything else about the discourse. However, this time he was really
TOM interested for a little while. The minister made a grand and moving
TOM picture of the assembling together of the world's hosts at the
TOM millennium when the lion and the lamb should lie down together and a
TOM little child should lead them. But the pathos, the lesson, the moral of
TOM the great spectacle were lost upon the boy; he only thought of the
TOM conspicuousness of the principal character before the on-looking
TOM nations; his face lit with the thought, and he said to himself that he
TOM wished he could be that child, if it was a tame lion.
TOM 
TOM Now he lapsed into suffering again, as the dry argument was resumed.
TOM Presently he bethought him of a treasure he had and got it out. It was a
TOM large black beetle with formidable jaws -- a ``pinchbug,'' he called it.
TOM It was in a percussion-cap box. The first thing the beetle did was to
TOM take him by the finger. A natural fillip followed, the beetle went
TOM floundering into the aisle and lit on its back, and the hurt finger went
TOM into the boy's mouth. The beetle lay there working its helpless legs,
TOM unable to turn over. Tom eyed it, and longed for it; but it was safe out
TOM of his reach. Other people uninterested in the sermon found relief in
TOM the beetle, and they eyed it too. Presently a vagrant poodle dog came
TOM idling along, sad at heart, lazy with the summer softness and the quiet,
TOM weary of captivity, sighing for change. He spied the beetle; the
TOM drooping tail lifted and wagged. He surveyed the prize; walked around
TOM it; smelt at it from a safe distance; walked around it again; grew
TOM bolder, and took a closer smell; then lifted his lip and made a gingerly
TOM snatch at it, just missing it; made another, and another; began to enjoy
TOM the diversion; subsided to his stomach with the beetle between his paws,
TOM and continued his experiments; grew weary at last, and then indifferent
TOM and absent-minded. His head nodded, and little by little his chin
TOM descended and touched the enemy, who seized it. There was a sharp yelp,
TOM a flirt of the poodle's head, and the beetle fell a couple of yards
TOM away, and lit on its back once more. The neighboring spectators shook
TOM with a gentle inward joy, several faces went behind fans and
TOM handkerchiefs, and Tom was entirely happy. The dog looked foolish, and
TOM probably felt so; but there was resentment in his heart, too, and a
TOM craving for revenge. So he went to the beetle and began a wary attack on
TOM it again; jumping at it from every point of a circle, lighting with his
TOM fore-paws within an inch of the creature, making even closer snatches at
TOM it with his teeth, and jerking his head till his ears flapped again. But
TOM he grew tired once more, after a while; tried to amuse himself with a
TOM fly but found no relief; followed an ant around, with his nose close to
TOM the floor, and quickly wearied of that; yawned, sighed, forgot the
TOM beetle entirely, and sat down on it. Then there was a wild yelp of agony
TOM and the poodle went sailing up the aisle; the yelps continued, and so
TOM did the dog; he crossed the house in front of the altar; he flew down
TOM the other aisle; he crossed before the doors; he clamored up the
TOM home-stretch; his anguish grew with his progress, till presently he was
TOM but a woolly comet moving in its orbit with the gleam and the speed of
TOM light. At last the frantic sufferer sheered from its course, and sprang
TOM into its master's lap; he flung it out of the window, and the voice of
TOM distress quickly thinned away and died in the distance.
TOM 
TOM By this time the whole church was red-faced and suffocating with
TOM suppressed laughter, and the sermon had come to a dead standstill. The
TOM discourse was resumed presently, but it went lame and halting, all
TOM possibility of impressiveness being at an end; for even the gravest
TOM sentiments were constantly being received with a smothered burst of
TOM unholy mirth, under cover of some remote pew-back, as if the poor parson
TOM had said a rarely facetious thing. It was a genuine relief to the whole
TOM congregation when the ordeal was over and the benediction pronounced.
TOM 
TOM Tom Sawyer went home quite cheerful, thinking to himself that there was
TOM some satisfaction about divine service when there was a bit of variety
TOM in it. He had but one marring thought; he was willing that the dog
TOM should play with his pinchbug, but he did not think it was upright in
TOM him to carry it off.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter VI
TOM 
TOM MONDAY morning found Tom Sawyer miserable. Monday morning always found
TOM him so -- because it began another week's slow suffering in school. He
TOM generally began that day with wishing he had had no intervening holiday,
TOM it made the going into captivity and fetters again so much more odious.
TOM 
TOM Tom lay thinking. Presently it occurred to him that he wished he was
TOM sick; then he could stay home from school. Here was a vague possibility.
TOM He canvassed his system. No ailment was found, and he investigated
TOM again. This time he thought he could detect colicky symptoms, and he
TOM began to encourage them with considerable hope. But they soon grew
TOM feeble, and presently died wholly away. He reflected further. Suddenly
TOM he discovered something. One of his upper front teeth was loose. This
TOM was lucky; he was about to begin to groan, as a ``starter,'' as he
TOM called it, when it occurred to him that if he came into court with that
TOM argument, his aunt would pull it out, and that would hurt. So he thought
TOM he would hold the tooth in reserve for the present, and seek further.
TOM Nothing offered for some little time, and then he remembered hearing the
TOM doctor tell about a certain thing that laid up a patient for two or
TOM three weeks and threatened to make him lose a finger. So the boy eagerly
TOM drew his sore toe from under the sheet and held it up for inspection.
TOM But now he did not know the necessary symptoms. However, it seemed well
TOM worth while to chance it, so he fell to groaning with considerable
TOM spirit.
TOM 
TOM But Sid slept on unconscious.
TOM 
TOM Tom groaned louder, and fancied that he began to feel pain in the toe.
TOM 
TOM No result from Sid.
TOM 
TOM Tom was panting with his exertions by this time. He took a rest and then
TOM swelled himself up and fetched a succession of admirable groans.
TOM 
TOM Sid snored on.
TOM 
TOM Tom was aggravated. He said, ``Sid, Sid!'' and shook him. This course
TOM worked well, and Tom began to groan again. Sid yawned, stretched, then
TOM brought himself up on his elbow with a snort, and began to stare at Tom.
TOM Tom went on groaning. Sid said:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom! Say, Tom!'' [No response.] ``Here, Tom! TOM! What is the matter,
TOM Tom?'' And he shook him and looked in his face anxiously.
TOM 
TOM Tom moaned out:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, don't, Sid. Don't joggle me.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, what's the matter, Tom? I must call auntie.''
TOM 
TOM ``No -- never mind. It'll be over by and by, maybe. Don't call
TOM anybody.''
TOM 
TOM ``But I must! DON'T groan so, Tom, it's awful. How long you been this
TOM way?''
TOM 
TOM ``Hours. Ouch! Oh, don't stir so, Sid, you'll kill me.''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, why didn't you wake me sooner ? Oh, Tom, DON'T! It makes my flesh
TOM crawl to hear you. Tom, what is the matter?''
TOM 
TOM ``I forgive you everything, Sid. [Groan.] Everything you've ever done to
TOM me. When I'm gone --''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, Tom, you ain't dying, are you? Don't, Tom -- oh, don't. Maybe --''
TOM 
TOM ``I forgive everybody, Sid. [Groan.] Tell 'em so, Sid. And Sid, you give
TOM my window-sash and my cat with one eye to that new girl that's come to
TOM town, and tell her --''
TOM 
TOM But Sid had snatched his clothes and gone. Tom was suffering in reality,
TOM now, so handsomely was his imagination working, and so his groans had
TOM gathered quite a genuine tone.
TOM 
TOM Sid flew down-stairs and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, Aunt Polly, come! Tom's dying!''
TOM 
TOM ``Dying!''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes'm. Don't wait -- come quick!''
TOM 
TOM ``Rubbage! I don't believe it!''
TOM 
TOM But she fled up-stairs, nevertheless, with Sid and Mary at her heels.
TOM And her face grew white, too, and her lip trembled. When she reached the
TOM bed-side she gasped out:
TOM 
TOM ``You, Tom! Tom, what's the matter with you?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, auntie, I'm --''
TOM 
TOM ``What's the matter with you -- what is the matter with you, child?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, auntie, my sore toe's mortified!''
TOM 
TOM The old lady sank down into a chair and laughed a little, then cried a
TOM little, then did both together. This restored her and she said:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, what a turn you did give me. Now you shut up that nonsense and
TOM climb out of this.''
TOM 
TOM The groans ceased and the pain vanished from the toe. The boy felt a
TOM little foolish, and he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Aunt Polly, it SEEMED mortified, and it hurt so I never minded my
TOM tooth at all.''
TOM 
TOM ``Your tooth, indeed! What's the matter with your tooth?''
TOM 
TOM ``One of them's loose, and it aches perfectly awful.''
TOM 
TOM ``There, there, now, don't begin that groaning again. Open your mouth.
TOM Well -- your tooth IS loose, but you're not going to die about that.
TOM Mary, get me a silk thread, and a chunk of fire out of the kitchen.''
TOM 
TOM Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, please, auntie, don't pull it out. It don't hurt any more. I wish
TOM I may never stir if it does. Please don't, auntie. I don't want to stay
TOM home from school.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, you don't, don't you? So all this row was because you thought
TOM you'd get to stay home from school and go a-fishing? Tom, Tom, I love
TOM you so, and you seem to try every way you can to break my old heart with
TOM your outrageousness.'' By this time the dental instruments were ready.
TOM The old lady made one end of the silk thread fast to Tom's tooth with a
TOM loop and tied the other to the bedpost. Then she seized the chunk of
TOM fire and suddenly thrust it almost into the boy's face. The tooth hung
TOM dangling by the bedpost, now.
TOM 
TOM But all trials bring their compensations. As Tom wended to school after
TOM breakfast, he was the envy of every boy he met because the gap in his
TOM upper row of teeth enabled him to expectorate in a new and admirable
TOM way. He gathered quite a following of lads interested in the exhibition;
TOM and one that had cut his finger and had been a centre of fascination and
TOM homage up to this time, now found himself suddenly without an adherent,
TOM and shorn of his glory. His heart was heavy, and he said with a disdain
TOM which he did not feel that it wasn't anything to spit like Tom Sawyer;
TOM but another boy said, ``Sour grapes!'' and he wandered away a dismantled
TOM hero.
TOM 
TOM Shortly Tom came upon the juvenile pariah of the village, Huckleberry
TOM Finn, son of the town drunkard. Huckleberry was cordially hated and
TOM dreaded by all the mothers of the town, because he was idle and lawless
TOM and vulgar and bad -- and because all their children admired him so, and
TOM delighted in his forbidden society, and wished they dared to be like
TOM him. Tom was like the rest of the respectable boys, in that he envied
TOM Huckleberry his gaudy outcast condition, and was under strict orders not
TOM to play with him. So he played with him every time he got a chance.
TOM Huckleberry was always dressed in the cast-off clothes of full-grown
TOM men, and they were in perennial bloom and fluttering with rags. His hat
TOM was a vast ruin with a wide crescent lopped out of its brim; his coat,
TOM when he wore one, hung nearly to his heels and had the rearward buttons
TOM far down the back; but one suspender supported his trousers; the seat of
TOM the trousers bagged low and contained nothing, the fringed legs dragged
TOM in the dirt when not rolled up.
TOM 
TOM Huckleberry came and went, at his own free will. He slept on doorsteps
TOM in fine weather and in empty hogsheads in wet; he did not have to go to
