TOM all; she never looked. Could it be possible that she was not aware that
TOM he was there? He carried his exploits to her immediate vicinity; came
TOM war-whooping around, snatched a boy's cap, hurled it to the roof of the
TOM schoolhouse, broke through a group of boys, tumbling them in every
TOM direction, and fell sprawling, himself, under Becky's nose, almost
TOM upsetting her -- and she turned, with her nose in the air, and he heard
TOM her say: ``Mf! some people think they're mighty smart -- always showing
TOM off!''
TOM 
TOM Tom's cheeks burned. He gathered himself up and sneaked off, crushed and
TOM crestfallen.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XIII
TOM 
TOM TOM'S mind was made up now. He was gloomy and desperate. He was a
TOM forsaken, friendless boy, he said; nobody loved him; when they found out
TOM what they had driven him to, perhaps they would be sorry; he had tried
TOM to do right and get along, but they would not let him; since nothing
TOM would do them but to be rid of him, let it be so; and let them blame HIM
TOM for the consequences -- why shouldn't they? What right had the
TOM friendless to complain? Yes, they had forced him to it at last: he would
TOM lead a life of crime. There was no choice.
TOM 
TOM By this time he was far down Meadow Lane, and the bell for school to
TOM ``take up'' tinkled faintly upon his ear. He sobbed, now, to think he
TOM should never, never hear that old familiar sound any more -- it was very
TOM hard, but it was forced on him; since he was driven out into the cold
TOM world, he must submit -- but he forgave them. Then the sobs came thick
TOM and fast.
TOM 
TOM Just at this point he met his soul's sworn comrade, Joe Harper --
TOM hard-eyed, and with evidently a great and dismal purpose in his heart.
TOM Plainly here were ``two souls with but a single thought.'' Tom, wiping
TOM his eyes with his sleeve, began to blubber out something about a
TOM resolution to escape from hard usage and lack of sympathy at home by
TOM roaming abroad into the great world never to return; and ended by hoping
TOM that Joe would not forget him.
TOM 
TOM But it transpired that this was a request which Joe had just been going
TOM to make of Tom, and had come to hunt him up for that purpose. His mother
TOM had whipped him for drinking some cream which he had never tasted and
TOM knew nothing about; it was plain that she was tired of him and wished
TOM him to go; if she felt that way, there was nothing for him to do but
TOM succumb; he hoped she would be happy, and never regret having driven her
TOM poor boy out into the unfeeling world to suffer and die.
TOM 
TOM As the two boys walked sorrowing along, they made a new compact to stand
TOM by each other and be brothers and never separate till death relieved
TOM them of their troubles. Then they began to lay their plans. Joe was for
TOM being a hermit, and living on crusts in a remote cave, and dying, some
TOM time, of cold and want and grief; but after listening to Tom, he
TOM conceded that there were some conspicuous advantages about a life of
TOM crime, and so he consented to be a pirate.
TOM 
TOM Three miles below St. Petersburg, at a point where the Mississippi River
TOM was a trifle over a mile wide, there was a long, narrow, wooded island,
TOM with a shallow bar at the head of it, and this offered well as a
TOM rendezvous. It was not inhabited; it lay far over toward the further
TOM shore, abreast a dense and almost wholly unpeopled forest. So Jackson's
TOM Island was chosen. Who were to be the subjects of their piracies was a
TOM matter that did not occur to them. Then they hunted up Huckleberry Finn,
TOM and he joined them promptly, for all careers were one to him; he was
TOM indifferent. They presently separated to meet at a lonely spot on the
TOM river-bank two miles above the village at the favorite hour -- which was
TOM midnight. There was a small log raft there which they meant to capture.
TOM Each would bring hooks and lines, and such provision as he could steal
TOM in the most dark and mysterious way -- as became outlaws. And before the
TOM afternoon was done, they had all managed to enjoy the sweet glory of
TOM spreading the fact that pretty soon the town would ``hear something.''
TOM All who got this vague hint were cautioned to ``be mum and wait.''
TOM 
TOM About midnight Tom arrived with a boiled ham and a few trifles, and
TOM stopped in a dense undergrowth on a small bluff overlooking the
TOM meeting-place. It was starlight, and very still. The mighty river lay
TOM like an ocean at rest. Tom listened a moment, but no sound disturbed the
TOM quiet. Then he gave a low, distinct whistle. It was answered from under
TOM the bluff. Tom whistled twice more; these signals were answered in the
TOM same way. Then a guarded voice said:
TOM 
TOM ``Who goes there?''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom Sawyer, the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main. Name your names.''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck Finn the Red-Handed, and Joe Harper the Terror of the Seas.'' Tom
TOM had furnished these titles, from his favorite literature.
TOM 
TOM ``'Tis well. Give the countersign.''
TOM 
TOM Two hoarse whispers delivered the same awful word simultaneously to the
TOM brooding night:
TOM 
TOM ``BLOOD!''
TOM 
TOM Then Tom tumbled his ham over the bluff and let himself down after it,
TOM tearing both skin and clothes to some extent in the effort. There was an
TOM easy, comfortable path along the shore under the bluff, but it lacked
TOM the advantages of difficulty and danger so valued by a pirate.
TOM 
TOM The Terror of the Seas had brought a side of bacon, and had about worn
TOM himself out with getting it there. Finn the Red-Handed had stolen a
TOM skillet and a quantity of half-cured leaf tobacco, and had also brought
TOM a few corn-cobs to make pipes with. But none of the pirates smoked or
TOM ``chewed'' but himself. The Black Avenger of the Spanish Main said it
TOM would never do to start without some fire. That was a wise thought;
TOM matches were hardly known there in that day. They saw a fire smouldering
TOM upon a great raft a hundred yards above, and they went stealthily
TOM thither and helped themselves to a chunk. They made an imposing
TOM adventure of it, saying, ``Hist!'' every now and then, and suddenly
TOM halting with finger on lip; moving with hands on imaginary dagger-hilts;
TOM and giving orders in dismal whispers that if ``the foe'' stirred, to
TOM ``let him have it to the hilt,'' because ``dead men tell no tales.''
TOM They knew well enough that the raftsmen were all down at the village
TOM laying in stores or having a spree, but still that was no excuse for
TOM their conducting this thing in an unpiratical way.
TOM 
TOM They shoved off, presently, Tom in command, Huck at the after oar and
TOM Joe at the forward. Tom stood amidships, gloomy-browed, and with folded
TOM arms, and gave his orders in a low, stern whisper:
TOM 
TOM ``Luff, and bring her to the wind!''
TOM 
TOM ``Aye-aye, sir!''
TOM 
TOM ``Steady, steady-y-y-y!''
TOM 
TOM ``Steady it is, sir!''
TOM 
TOM ``Let her go off a point!''
TOM 
TOM ``Point it is, sir!''
TOM 
TOM As the boys steadily and monotonously drove the raft toward mid-stream
TOM it was no doubt understood that these orders were given only for
TOM ``style,'' and were not intended to mean anything in particular.
TOM 
TOM ``What sail's she carrying?''
TOM 
TOM ``Courses, tops'ls, and flying-jib, sir.''
TOM 
TOM ``Send the r'yals up! Lay out aloft, there, half a dozen of ye --
TOM foretopmaststuns'l! Lively, now!''
TOM 
TOM ``Aye-aye, sir!''
TOM 
TOM ``Shake out that maintogalans'l! Sheets and braces! NOW my hearties!''
TOM 
TOM ``Aye-aye, sir!''
TOM 
TOM ``Hellum-a-lee -- hard a port! Stand by to meet her when she comes!
TOM Port, port! NOW, men! With a will! Stead-y-y-y!''
TOM 
TOM ``Steady it is, sir!''
TOM 
TOM The raft drew beyond the middle of the river; the boys pointed her head
TOM right, and then lay on their oars. The river was not high, so there was
TOM not more than a two or three mile current. Hardly a word was said during
TOM the next three-quarters of an hour. Now the raft was passing before the
TOM distant town. Two or three glimmering lights showed where it lay,
TOM peacefully sleeping, beyond the vague vast sweep of star-gemmed water,
TOM unconscious of the tremendous event that was happening. The Black
TOM Avenger stood still with folded arms, ``looking his last'' upon the
TOM scene of his former joys and his later sufferings, and wishing ``she''
TOM could see him now, abroad on the wild sea, facing peril and death with
TOM dauntless heart, going to his doom with a grim smile on his lips. It was
TOM but a small strain on his imagination to remove Jackson's Island beyond
TOM eye-shot of the village, and so he ``looked his last'' with a broken and
TOM satisfied heart. The other pirates were looking their last, too; and
TOM they all looked so long that they came near letting the current drift
TOM them out of the range of the island. But they discovered the danger in
TOM time, and made shift to avert it. About two o'clock in the morning the
TOM raft grounded on the bar two hundred yards above the head of the island,
TOM and they waded back and forth until they had landed their freight. Part
TOM of the little raft's belongings consisted of an old sail, and this they
TOM spread over a nook in the bushes for a tent to shelter their provisions;
TOM but they themselves would sleep in the open air in good weather, as
TOM became outlaws.
TOM 
TOM They built a fire against the side of a great log twenty or thirty steps
TOM within the sombre depths of the forest, and then cooked some bacon in
TOM the frying-pan for supper, and used up half of the corn ``pone'' stock
TOM they had brought. It seemed glorious sport to be feasting in that wild,
TOM free way in the virgin forest of an unexplored and uninhabited island,
TOM far from the haunts of men, and they said they never would return to
TOM civilization. The climbing fire lit up their faces and threw its ruddy
TOM glare upon the pillared tree-trunks of their forest temple, and upon the
TOM varnished foliage and festooning vines.
TOM 
TOM When the last crisp slice of bacon was gone, and the last allowance of
TOM corn pone devoured, the boys stretched themselves out on the grass,
TOM filled with contentment. They could have found a cooler place, but they
TOM would not deny themselves such a romantic feature as the roasting
TOM camp-fire.
TOM 
TOM ``AIN'T it gay?'' said Joe.
TOM 
TOM ``It's NUTS!'' said Tom. ``What would the boys say if they could see
TOM us?''
TOM 
TOM ``Say? Well, they'd just die to be here -- hey, Hucky!''
TOM 
TOM ``I reckon so,'' said Huckleberry; ``anyways, I'm suited. I don't want
TOM nothing better'n this. I don't ever get enough to eat, gen'ally -- and
TOM here they can't come and pick at a feller and bullyrag him so.''
TOM 
TOM ``It's just the life for me,'' said Tom. ``You don't have to get up,
TOM mornings, and you don't have to go to school, and wash, and all that
TOM blame foolishness. You see a pirate don't have to do ANYTHING, Joe, when
TOM he's ashore, but a hermit HE has to be praying considerable, and then he
TOM don't have any fun, anyway, all by himself that way.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh yes, that's so,'' said Joe, ``but I hadn't thought much about it,
TOM you know. I'd a good deal rather be a pirate, now that I've tried it.''
TOM 
TOM ``You see,'' said Tom, ``people don't go much on hermits, nowadays, like
TOM they used to in old times, but a pirate's always respected. And a
TOM hermit's got to sleep on the hardest place he can find, and put
TOM sackcloth and ashes on his head, and stand out in the rain, and --''
TOM 
TOM ``What does he put sackcloth and ashes on his head for?'' inquired Huck.
TOM 
TOM ``I dono. But they've GOT to do it. Hermits always do. You'd have to do
TOM that if you was a hermit.''
TOM 
TOM ``Dern'd if I would,'' said Huck.
TOM 
TOM ``Well, what would you do?''
TOM 
TOM ``I dono. But I wouldn't do that.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, Huck, you'd HAVE to. How'd you get around it?''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, I just wouldn't stand it. I'd run away.''
TOM 
TOM ``Run away! Well, you WOULD be a nice old slouch of a hermit. You'd be a
TOM disgrace.''
TOM 
TOM The Red-Handed made no response, being better employed. He had finished
TOM gouging out a cob, and now he fitted a weed stem to it, loaded it with
TOM tobacco, and was pressing a coal to the charge and blowing a cloud of
TOM fragrant smoke -- he was in the full bloom of luxurious contentment. The
TOM other pirates envied him this majestic vice, and secretly resolved to
TOM acquire it shortly. Presently Huck said:
TOM 
TOM ``What does pirates have to do?''
TOM 
TOM Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, they have just a bully time -- take ships and burn them, and get
TOM the money and bury it in awful places in their island where there's
TOM ghosts and things to watch it, and kill everybody in the ships -- make
TOM 'em walk a plank.''
TOM 
TOM ``And they carry the women to the island,'' said Joe; ``they don't kill
TOM the women.''
TOM 
TOM ``No,'' assented Tom, ``they don't kill the women -- they're too noble.
TOM And the women's always beautiful, too.''
TOM 
TOM ``And don't they wear the bulliest clothes! Oh no! All gold and silver
TOM and di'monds,'' said Joe, with enthusiasm.
TOM 
TOM ``Who?'' said Huck.
TOM 
TOM ``Why, the pirates.''
TOM 
TOM Huck scanned his own clothing forlornly.
TOM 
TOM ``I reckon I ain't dressed fitten for a pirate,'' said he, with a
TOM regretful pathos in his voice; ``but I ain't got none but these.''
TOM 
TOM But the other boys told him the fine clothes would come fast enough,
TOM after they should have begun their adventures. They made him understand
TOM that his poor rags would do to begin with, though it was customary for
TOM wealthy pirates to start with a proper wardrobe.
TOM 
TOM Gradually their talk died out and drowsiness began to steal upon the
TOM eyelids of the little waifs. The pipe dropped from the fingers of the
TOM Red-Handed, and he slept the sleep of the conscience-free and the weary.
TOM The Terror of the Seas and the Black Avenger of the Spanish Main had
TOM more difficulty in getting to sleep. They said their prayers inwardly,
TOM and lying down, since there was nobody there with authority to make them
TOM kneel and recite aloud; in truth, they had a mind not to say them at
TOM all, but they were afraid to proceed to such lengths as that, lest they
TOM might call down a sudden and special thunderbolt from heaven. Then at
TOM once they reached and hovered upon the imminent verge of sleep -- but an
TOM intruder came, now, that would not ``down.'' It was conscience. They
TOM began to feel a vague fear that they had been doing wrong to run away;
TOM and next they thought of the stolen meat, and then the real torture
TOM came. They tried to argue it away by reminding conscience that they had
TOM purloined sweetmeats and apples scores of times; but conscience was not
TOM to be appeased by such thin plausibilities; it seemed to them, in the
TOM end, that there was no getting around the stubborn fact that taking
TOM sweetmeats was only ``hooking,'' while taking bacon and hams and such
TOM valuables was plain simple stealing -- and there was a command against
TOM that in the Bible. So they inwardly resolved that so long as they
TOM remained in the business, their piracies should not again be sullied
TOM with the crime of stealing. Then conscience granted a truce, and these
TOM curiously inconsistent pirates fell peacefully to sleep.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XIV
TOM 
TOM WHEN Tom awoke in the morning, he wondered where he was. He sat up and
TOM rubbed his eyes and looked around. Then he comprehended. It was the cool
TOM gray dawn, and there was a delicious sense of repose and peace in the
TOM deep pervading calm and silence of the woods. Not a leaf stirred; not a
TOM sound obtruded upon great Nature's meditation. Beaded dewdrops stood
TOM upon the leaves and grasses. A white layer of ashes covered the fire,
TOM and a thin blue breath of smoke rose straight into the air. Joe and Huck
TOM still slept.
TOM 
TOM Now, far away in the woods a bird called; another answered; presently
TOM the hammering of a woodpecker was heard. Gradually the cool dim gray of
TOM the morning whitened, and as gradually sounds multiplied and life
TOM manifested itself. The marvel of Nature shaking off sleep and going to
TOM work unfolded itself to the musing boy. A little green worm came
TOM crawling over a dewy leaf, lifting two-thirds of his body into the air
TOM from time to time and ``sniffing around,'' then proceeding again -- for
TOM he was measuring, Tom said; and when the worm approached him, of its own
TOM accord, he sat as still as a stone, with his hopes rising and falling,
TOM by turns, as the creature still came toward him or seemed inclined to go
TOM elsewhere; and when at last it considered a painful moment with its
TOM curved body in the air and then came decisively down upon Tom's leg and
TOM began a journey over him, his whole heart was glad -- for that meant
TOM that he was going to have a new suit of clothes -- without the shadow of
TOM a doubt a gaudy piratical uniform. Now a procession of ants appeared,
TOM from nowhere in particular, and went about their labors; one struggled
TOM manfully by with a dead spider five times as big as itself in its arms,
TOM and lugged it straight up a tree-trunk. A brown spotted lady-bug climbed
TOM the dizzy height of a grass blade, and Tom bent down close to it and
TOM said, ``Lady-bug, lady-bug, fly away home, your house is on fire, your
TOM children's alone,'' and she took wing and went off to see about it --
TOM which did not surprise the boy, for he knew of old that this insect was
TOM credulous about conflagrations, and he had practised upon its simplicity
TOM more than once. A tumblebug came next, heaving sturdily at its ball, and
TOM Tom touched the creature, to see it shut its legs against its body and
TOM pretend to be dead. The birds were fairly rioting by this time. A
TOM catbird, the Northern mocker, lit in a tree over Tom's head, and trilled
TOM out her imitations of her neighbors in a rapture of enjoyment; then a
TOM shrill jay swept down, a flash of blue flame, and stopped on a twig
TOM almost within the boy's reach, cocked his head to one side and eyed the
TOM strangers with a consuming curiosity; a gray squirrel and a big fellow
TOM of the ``fox'' kind came skurrying along, sitting up at intervals to
TOM inspect and chatter at the boys, for the wild things had probably never
TOM seen a human being before and scarcely knew whether to be afraid or not.
TOM All Nature was wide awake and stirring, now; long lances of sunlight
TOM pierced down through the dense foliage far and near, and a few
TOM butterflies came fluttering upon the scene.
TOM 
TOM Tom stirred up the other pirates and they all clattered away with a
TOM shout, and in a minute or two were stripped and chasing after and
TOM tumbling over each other in the shallow limpid water of the white
TOM sandbar. They felt no longing for the little village sleeping in the
TOM distance beyond the majestic waste of water. A vagrant current or a
TOM slight rise in the river had carried off their raft, but this only
TOM gratified them, since its going was something like burning the bridge
TOM between them and civilization.
TOM 
TOM They came back to camp wonderfully refreshed, glad-hearted, and
TOM ravenous; and they soon had the camp-fire blazing up again. Huck found a
TOM spring of clear cold water close by, and the boys made cups of broad oak
TOM or hickory leaves, and felt that water, sweetened with such a wildwood
TOM charm as that, would be a good enough substitute for coffee. While Joe
TOM was slicing bacon for breakfast, Tom and Huck asked him to hold on a
TOM minute; they stepped to a promising nook in the river-bank and threw in
TOM their lines; almost immediately they had reward. Joe had not had time to
TOM get impatient before they were back again with some handsome bass, a
TOM couple of sun-perch and a small catfish -- provisions enough for quite a
TOM family. They fried the fish with the bacon, and were astonished; for no
TOM fish had ever seemed so delicious before. They did not know that the
TOM quicker a fresh-water fish is on the fire after he is caught the better
TOM he is; and they reflected little upon what a sauce open-air sleeping,
TOM open-air exercise, bathing, and a large ingredient of hunger make, too.
TOM 
TOM They lay around in the shade, after breakfast, while Huck had a smoke,
TOM and then went off through the woods on an exploring expedition. They
TOM tramped gayly along, over decaying logs, through tangled underbrush,
TOM among solemn monarchs of the forest, hung from their crowns to the
TOM ground with a drooping regalia of grape-vines. Now and then they came
TOM upon snug nooks carpeted with grass and jeweled with flowers.
TOM 
TOM They found plenty of things to be delighted with, but nothing to be
TOM astonished at. They discovered that the island was about three miles
TOM long and a quarter of a mile wide, and that the shore it lay closest to
TOM was only separated from it by a narrow channel hardly two hundred yards
TOM wide. They took a swim about every hour, so it was close upon the middle
TOM of the afternoon when they got back to camp. They were too hungry to
TOM stop to fish, but they fared sumptuously upon cold ham, and then threw
TOM themselves down in the shade to talk. But the talk soon began to drag,
TOM and then died. The stillness, the solemnity that brooded in the woods,
TOM and the sense of loneliness, began to tell upon the spirits of the boys.
TOM They fell to thinking. A sort of undefined longing crept upon them. This
TOM took dim shape, presently -- it was budding homesickness. Even Finn the
TOM Red-Handed was dreaming of his doorsteps and empty hogsheads. But they
TOM were all ashamed of their weakness, and none was brave enough to speak
TOM his thought.
TOM 
TOM For some time, now, the boys had been dully conscious of a peculiar
TOM sound in the distance, just as one sometimes is of the ticking of a
TOM clock which he takes no distinct note of. But now this mysterious sound
TOM became more pronounced, and forced a recognition. The boys started,
TOM glanced at each other, and then each assumed a listening attitude. There
TOM was a long silence, profound and unbroken; then a deep, sullen boom came
TOM floating down out of the distance.
TOM 
TOM ``What is it!'' exclaimed Joe, under his breath.
TOM 
TOM ``I wonder,'' said Tom in a whisper.
TOM 
TOM ``'Tain't thunder,'' said Huckleberry, in an awed tone, ``becuz thunder
TOM --''
TOM 
TOM ``Hark!'' said Tom. ``Listen -- don't talk.''
TOM 
TOM They waited a time that seemed an age, and then the same muffled boom
TOM troubled the solemn hush.
TOM 
TOM ``Let's go and see.''
TOM 
TOM They sprang to their feet and hurried to the shore toward the town. They
TOM parted the bushes on the bank and peered out over the water. The little
TOM steam ferry-boat was about a mile below the village, drifting with the
TOM current. Her broad deck seemed crowded with people. There were a great
TOM many skiffs rowing about or floating with the stream in the neighborhood
TOM of the ferryboat, but the boys could not determine what the men in them
TOM were doing. Presently a great jet of white smoke burst from the
TOM ferryboat's side, and as it expanded and rose in a lazy cloud, that same
TOM dull throb of sound was borne to the listeners again.
TOM 
TOM ``I know now!'' exclaimed Tom; ``somebody's drownded!''
TOM 
TOM ``That's it!'' said Huck; ``they done that last summer, when Bill Turner
TOM got drownded; they shoot a cannon over the water, and that makes him
TOM come up to the top. Yes, and they take loaves of bread and put
TOM quicksilver in 'em and set 'em afloat, and wherever there's anybody
TOM that's drownded, they'll float right there and stop.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, I've heard about that,'' said Joe. ``I wonder what makes the
TOM bread do that.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, it ain't the bread, so much,'' said Tom; ``I reckon it's mostly
TOM what they SAY over it before they start it out.''
TOM 
TOM ``But they don't say anything over it,'' said Huck. ``I've seen 'em and
TOM they don't.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, that's funny,'' said Tom. ``But maybe they say it to themselves.
TOM Of COURSE they do. Anybody might know that.''
TOM 
TOM The other boys agreed that there was reason in what Tom said, because an
TOM ignorant lump of bread, uninstructed by an incantation, could not be
TOM expected to act very intelligently when set upon an errand of such
TOM gravity.
TOM 
TOM ``By jings, I wish I was over there, now,'' said Joe.
TOM 
TOM ``I do too'' said Huck ``I'd give heaps to know who it is.''
TOM 
TOM The boys still listened and watched. Presently a revealing thought
TOM flashed through Tom's mind, and he exclaimed:
TOM 
TOM ``Boys, I know who's drownded -- it's us!''
TOM 
TOM They felt like heroes in an instant. Here was a gorgeous triumph; they
TOM were missed; they were mourned; hearts were breaking on their account;
TOM tears were being shed; accusing memories of unkindness to these poor
TOM lost lads were rising up, and unavailing regrets and remorse were being
TOM indulged; and best of all, the departed were the talk of the whole town,
TOM and the envy of all the boys, as far as this dazzling notoriety was
TOM concerned. This was fine. It was worth while to be a pirate, after all.
TOM 
TOM As twilight drew on, the ferryboat went back to her accustomed business
TOM and the skiffs disappeared. The pirates returned to camp. They were
TOM jubilant with vanity over their new grandeur and the illustrious trouble
TOM they were making. They caught fish, cooked supper and ate it, and then
TOM fell to guessing at what the village was thinking and saying about them;
TOM and the pictures they drew of the public distress on their account were
TOM gratifying to look upon -- from their point of view. But when the
TOM shadows of night closed them in, they gradually ceased to talk, and sat
TOM gazing into the fire, with their minds evidently wandering elsewhere.
TOM The excitement was gone, now, and Tom and Joe could not keep back
TOM thoughts of certain persons at home who were not enjoying this fine
TOM frolic as much as they were. Misgivings came; they grew troubled and
TOM unhappy; a sigh or two escaped, unawares. By and by Joe timidly ventured
TOM upon a roundabout ``feeler'' as to how the others might look upon a
TOM return to civilization -- not right now, but --
TOM 
TOM Tom withered him with derision! Huck, being uncommitted as yet, joined
TOM in with Tom, and the waverer quickly ``explained,'' and was glad to get
TOM out of the scrape with as little taint of chicken-hearted home-sickness
TOM clinging to his garments as he could. Mutiny was effectually laid to
TOM rest for the moment.
TOM 
TOM As the night deepened, Huck began to nod, and presently to snore. Joe
TOM followed next. Tom lay upon his elbow motionless, for some time,
TOM watching the two intently. At last he got up cautiously, on his knees,
TOM and went searching among the grass and the flickering reflections flung
TOM by the camp-fire. He picked up and inspected several large
TOM semi-cylinders of the thin white bark of a sycamore, and finally chose
TOM two which seemed to suit him. Then he knelt by the fire and painfully
TOM wrote something upon each of these with his ``red keel''; one he rolled
TOM up and put in his jacket pocket, and the other he put in Joe's hat and
TOM removed it to a little distance from the owner. And he also put into the
TOM hat certain schoolboy treasures of almost inestimable value -- among
TOM them a lump of chalk, an India-rubber ball, three fishhooks, and one of
TOM that kind of marbles known as a ``sure 'nough crystal.'' Then he tiptoed
TOM his way cautiously among the trees till he felt that he was out of
TOM hearing, and straightway broke into a keen run in the direction of the
TOM sandbar.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XV
TOM 
TOM A FEW minutes later Tom was in the shoal water of the bar, wading toward
TOM the Illinois shore. Before the depth reached his middle he was half-way
TOM over; the current would permit no more wading, now, so he struck out
TOM confidently to swim the remaining hundred yards. He swam quartering
TOM upstream, but still was swept downward rather faster than he had
TOM expected. However, he reached the shore finally, and drifted along till
TOM he found a low place and drew himself out. He put his hand on his jacket
TOM pocket, found his piece of bark safe, and then struck through the woods,
TOM following the shore, with streaming garments. Shortly before ten o'clock
TOM he came out into an open place opposite the village, and saw the
TOM ferryboat lying in the shadow of the trees and the high bank. Everything
TOM was quiet under the blinking stars. He crept down the bank, watching
TOM with all his eyes, slipped into the water, swam three or four strokes
TOM and climbed into the skiff that did ``yawl'' duty at the boat's stern.
TOM He laid himself down under the thwarts and waited, panting.
TOM 
TOM Presently the cracked bell tapped and a voice gave the order to ``cast
TOM off.'' A minute or two later the skiff's head was standing high up,
TOM against the boat's swell, and the voyage was begun. Tom felt happy in
TOM his success, for he knew it was the boat's last trip for the night. At
TOM the end of a long twelve or fifteen minutes the wheels stopped, and Tom
TOM slipped overboard and swam ashore in the dusk, landing fifty yards
TOM downstream, out of danger of possible stragglers.
TOM 
TOM He flew along unfrequented alleys, and shortly found himself at his
TOM aunt's back fence. He climbed over, approached the ``ell,'' and looked
TOM in at the sitting-room window, for a light was burning there. There sat
TOM Aunt Polly, Sid, Mary, and Joe Harper's mother, grouped together,
TOM talking. They were by the bed, and the bed was between them and the
TOM door. Tom went to the door and began to softly lift the latch; then he
TOM pressed gently and the door yielded a crack; he continued pushing
TOM cautiously, and quaking every time it creaked, till he judged he might
TOM squeeze through on his knees; so he put his head through and began,
TOM warily.
TOM 
TOM ``What makes the candle blow so?'' said Aunt Polly. Tom hurried up.
TOM ``Why, that door's open, I believe. Why, of course it is. No end of
TOM strange things now. Go 'long and shut it, Sid.''
TOM 
TOM Tom disappeared under the bed just in time. He lay and ``breathed''
TOM himself for a time, and then crept to where he could almost touch his
TOM aunt's foot.
TOM 
TOM ``But as I was saying,'' said Aunt Polly, ``he warn't BAD, so to say --
TOM only mischEEvous. Only just giddy, and harum-scarum, you know. He warn't
TOM any more responsible than a colt. HE never meant any harm, and he was
TOM the best-hearted boy that ever was'' -- and she began to cry.
TOM 
TOM ``It was just so with my Joe -- always full of his devilment, and up to
TOM every kind of mischief, but he was just as unselfish and kind as he
TOM could be -- and laws bless me, to think I went and whipped him for
TOM taking that cream, never once recollecting that I throwed it out myself
TOM because it was sour, and I never to see him again in this world, never,
TOM never, never, poor abused boy!'' And Mrs. Harper sobbed as if her heart
TOM would break.
TOM 
TOM ``I hope Tom's better off where he is,'' said Sid, ``but if he'd been
TOM better in some ways --''
TOM 
TOM ``SID!'' Tom felt the glare of the old lady's eye, though he could not
TOM see it. ``Not a word against my Tom, now that he's gone! God'll take
TOM care of HIM -- never you trouble YOURself, sir! Oh, Mrs. Harper, I don't
TOM know how to give him up! I don't know how to give him up! He was such a
TOM comfort to me, although he tormented my old heart out of me, 'most.''
TOM 
TOM ``The Lord giveth and the Lord hath taken away -- Blessed be the name of
TOM the Lord! But it's so hard -- Oh, it's so hard! Only last Saturday my
TOM Joe busted a firecracker right under my nose and I knocked him
TOM sprawling. Little did I know then, how soon -- Oh, if it was to do over
TOM again I'd hug him and bless him for it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, yes, yes, I know just how you feel, Mrs. Harper, I know just
TOM exactly how you feel. No longer ago than yesterday noon, my Tom took and
TOM filled the cat full of Pain-killer, and I did think the cretur would
TOM tear the house down. And God forgive me, I cracked Tom's head with my
TOM thimble, poor boy, poor dead boy. But he's out of all his troubles now.
TOM And the last words I ever heard him say was to reproach --''
TOM 
TOM But this memory was too much for the old lady, and she broke entirely
TOM down. Tom was snuffling, now, himself -- and more in pity of himself
TOM than anybody else. He could hear Mary crying, and putting in a kindly
TOM word for him from time to time. He began to have a nobler opinion of
TOM himself than ever before. Still, he was sufficiently touched by his
TOM aunt's grief to long to rush out from under the bed and overwhelm her
TOM with joy -- and the theatrical gorgeousness of the thing appealed
TOM strongly to his nature, too, but he resisted and lay still.
TOM 
TOM He went on listening, and gathered by odds and ends that it was
TOM conjectured at first that the boys had got drowned while taking a swim;
TOM then the small raft had been missed; next, certain boys said the missing
TOM lads had promised that the village should ``hear something'' soon; the
TOM wise-heads had ``put this and that together'' and decided that the lads
TOM had gone off on that raft and would turn up at the next town below,
TOM presently; but toward noon the raft had been found, lodged against the
TOM Missouri shore some five or six miles below the village -- and then hope
TOM perished; they must be drowned, else hunger would have driven them home
TOM by nightfall if not sooner. It was believed that the search for the
TOM bodies had been a fruitless effort merely because the drowning must have
TOM occurred in mid-channel, since the boys, being good swimmers, would
TOM otherwise have escaped to shore. This was Wednesday night. If the bodies
TOM continued missing until Sunday, all hope would be given over, and the
TOM funerals would be preached on that morning. Tom shuddered.
TOM 
TOM Mrs. Harper gave a sobbing good-night and turned to go. Then with a
TOM mutual impulse the two bereaved women flung themselves into each other's
TOM arms and had a good, consoling cry, and then parted. Aunt Polly was
TOM tender far beyond her wont, in her good-night to Sid and Mary. Sid
TOM snuffled a bit and Mary went off crying with all her heart.
TOM 
TOM Aunt Polly knelt down and prayed for Tom so touchingly, so appealingly,
TOM and with such measureless love in her words and her old trembling voice,
TOM that he was weltering in tears again, long before she was through.
TOM 
TOM He had to keep still long after she went to bed, for she kept making
TOM broken-hearted ejaculations from time to time, tossing unrestfully, and
TOM turning over. But at last she was still, only moaning a little in her
TOM sleep. Now the boy stole out, rose gradually by the bedside, shaded the
TOM candle-light with his hand, and stood regarding her. His heart was full
TOM of pity for her. He took out his sycamore scroll and placed it by the
TOM candle. But something occurred to him, and he lingered considering. His
TOM face lighted with a happy solution of his thought; he put the bark
TOM hastily in his pocket. Then he bent over and kissed the faded lips, and
TOM straightway made his stealthy exit, latching the door behind him.
TOM 
TOM He threaded his way back to the ferry landing, found nobody at large
TOM there, and walked boldly on board the boat, for he knew she was
TOM tenantless except that there was a watchman, who always turned in and
TOM slept like a graven image. He untied the skiff at the stern, slipped
TOM into it, and was soon rowing cautiously upstream. When he had pulled a
TOM mile above the village, he started quartering across and bent himself
TOM stoutly to his work. He hit the landing on the other side neatly, for
TOM this was a familiar bit of work to him. He was moved to capture the
TOM skiff, arguing that it might be considered a ship and therefore
TOM legitimate prey for a pirate, but he knew a thorough search would be
TOM made for it and that might end in revelations. So he stepped ashore and
TOM entered the woods.
TOM 
TOM He sat down and took a long rest, torturing himself meanwhile to keep
TOM awake, and then started warily down the home-stretch. The night was far
TOM spent. It was broad daylight before he found himself fairly abreast the
TOM island bar. He rested again until the sun was well up and gilding the
TOM great river with its splendor, and then he plunged into the stream. A
TOM little later he paused, dripping, upon the threshold of the camp, and
TOM heard Joe say:
TOM 
TOM ``No, Tom's true-blue, Huck, and he'll come back. He won't desert. He
TOM knows that would be a disgrace to a pirate, and Tom's too proud for that
TOM sort of thing. He's up to something or other. Now I wonder what?''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, the things is ours, anyway, ain't they?''
TOM 
TOM ``Pretty near, but not yet, Huck. The writing says they are if he ain't
TOM back here to breakfast.''
TOM 
TOM ``Which he is!'' exclaimed Tom, with fine dramatic effect, stepping
TOM grandly into camp.
TOM 
TOM A sumptuous breakfast of bacon and fish was shortly provided, and as the
TOM boys set to work upon it, Tom recounted (and adorned) his adventures.
TOM They were a vain and boastful company of heroes when the tale was done.
TOM Then Tom hid himself away in a shady nook to sleep till noon, and the
TOM other pirates got ready to fish and explore.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XVI
TOM 
TOM AFTER dinner all the gang turned out to hunt for turtle eggs on the bar.
TOM They went about poking sticks into the sand, and when they found a soft
TOM place they went down on their knees and dug with their hands. Sometimes
TOM they would take fifty or sixty eggs out of one hole. They were perfectly
TOM round white things a trifle smaller than an English walnut. They had a
TOM famous fried-egg feast that night, and another on Friday morning.
TOM 
TOM After breakfast they went whooping and prancing out on the bar, and
TOM chased each other round and round, shedding clothes as they went, until
TOM they were naked, and then continued the frolic far away up the shoal
TOM water of the bar, against the stiff current, which latter tripped their
TOM legs from under them from time to time and greatly increased the fun.
TOM And now and then they stooped in a group and splashed water in each
TOM other's faces with their palms, gradually approaching each other, with
TOM averted faces to avoid the strangling sprays, and finally gripping and
TOM struggling till the best man ducked his neighbor, and then they all went
TOM under in a tangle of white legs and arms and came up blowing,
TOM sputtering, laughing, and gasping for breath at one and the same time.
TOM 
TOM When they were well exhausted, they would run out and sprawl on the dry,
TOM hot sand, and lie there and cover themselves up with it, and by and by
TOM break for the water again and go through the original performance once
TOM more. Finally it occurred to them that their naked skin represented
TOM flesh-colored ``tights'' very fairly; so they drew a ring in the sand
TOM and had a circus -- with three clowns in it, for none would yield this
TOM proudest post to his neighbor.
TOM 
TOM Next they got their marbles and played ``knucks'' and ``ring-taw'' and
TOM ``keeps'' till that amusement grew stale. Then Joe and Huck had another
TOM swim, but Tom would not venture, because he found that in kicking off
TOM his trousers he had kicked his string of rattlesnake rattles off his
TOM ankle, and he wondered how he had escaped cramp so long without the
TOM protection of this mysterious charm. He did not venture again until he
TOM had found it, and by that time the other boys were tired and ready to
TOM rest. They gradually wandered apart, dropped into the ``dumps,'' and
TOM fell to gazing longingly across the wide river to where the village lay
TOM drowsing in the sun. Tom found himself writing ``BECKY'' in the sand
TOM with his big toe; he scratched it out, and was angry with himself for
TOM his weakness. But he wrote it again, nevertheless; he could not help it.
TOM He erased it once more and then took himself out of temptation by
TOM driving the other boys together and joining them.
TOM 
TOM But Joe's spirits had gone down almost beyond resurrection. He was so
TOM homesick that he could hardly endure the misery of it. The tears lay
TOM very near the surface. Huck was melancholy, too. Tom was down-hearted,
TOM but tried hard not to show it. He had a secret which he was not ready to
TOM tell, yet, but if this mutinous depression was not broken up soon, he
TOM would have to bring it out. He said, with a great show of cheerfulness:
TOM 
TOM ``I bet there's been pirates on this island before, boys. We'll explore
TOM it again. They've hid treasures here somewhere. How'd you feel to light
TOM on a rotten chest full of gold and silver -- hey?''
TOM 
TOM But it roused only faint enthusiasm, which faded out, with no reply. Tom
TOM tried one or two other seductions; but they failed, too. It was
TOM discouraging work. Joe sat poking up the sand with a stick and looking
TOM very gloomy. Finally he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, boys, let's give it up. I want to go home. It's so lonesome.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh no, Joe, you'll feel better by and by,'' said Tom. ``Just think of
TOM the fishing that's here.''
TOM 
TOM ``I don't care for fishing. I want to go home.''
TOM 
TOM ``But, Joe, there ain't such another swimming-place anywhere.''
TOM 
TOM ``Swimming's no good. I don't seem to care for it, somehow, when there
TOM ain't anybody to say I sha'n't go in. I mean to go home.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, shucks! Baby! You want to see your mother, I reckon.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, I DO want to see my mother -- and you would, too, if you had one.
TOM I ain't any more baby than you are.'' And Joe snuffled a little.
TOM 
TOM ``Well, we'll let the cry-baby go home to his mother, won't we, Huck?
TOM Poor thing -- does it want to see its mother? And so it shall. You like
TOM it here, don't you, Huck? We'll stay, won't we?''
TOM 
TOM Huck said, ``Y-e-s'' -- without any heart in it.
TOM 
TOM ``I'll never speak to you again as long as I live,'' said Joe, rising.
TOM ``There now!'' And he moved moodily away and began to dress himself.
TOM 
TOM ``Who cares!'' said Tom. ``Nobody wants you to. Go 'long home and get
TOM laughed at. Oh, you're a nice pirate. Huck and me ain't cry-babies.
TOM We'll stay, won't we, Huck? Let him go if he wants to. I reckon we can
TOM get along without him, per'aps.''
TOM 
TOM But Tom was uneasy, nevertheless, and was alarmed to see Joe go sullenly
TOM on with his dressing. And then it was discomforting to see Huck eying
TOM Joe's preparations so wistfully, and keeping up such an ominous silence.
TOM Presently, without a parting word, Joe began to wade off toward the
TOM Illinois shore. Tom's heart began to sink. He glanced at Huck. Huck
TOM could not bear the look, and dropped his eyes. Then he said:
TOM 
TOM ``I want to go, too, Tom. It was getting so lonesome anyway, and now
TOM it'll be worse. Let's us go, too, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``I won't! You can all go, if you want to. I mean to stay.''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, I better go.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, go 'long -- who's hendering you.''
TOM 
TOM Huck began to pick up his scattered clothes. He said:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, I wisht you'd come, too. Now you think it over. We'll wait for
TOM you when we get to shore.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, you'll wait a blame long time, that's all.''
TOM 
TOM Huck started sorrowfully away, and Tom stood looking after him, with a
TOM strong desire tugging at his heart to yield his pride and go along too.
TOM He hoped the boys would stop, but they still waded slowly on. It
TOM suddenly dawned on Tom that it was become very lonely and still. He made
TOM one final struggle with his pride, and then darted after his comrades,
TOM yelling:
TOM 
TOM ``Wait! Wait! I want to tell you something!''
TOM 
TOM They presently stopped and turned around. When he got to where they
TOM were, he began unfolding his secret, and they listened moodily till at
TOM last they saw the ``point'' he was driving at, and then they set up a
TOM war-whoop of applause and said it was ``splendid!'' and said if he had
TOM told them at first, they wouldn't have started away. He made a plausible
TOM excuse; but his real reason had been the fear that not even the secret
TOM would keep them with him any very great length of time, and so he had
TOM meant to hold it in reserve as a last seduction.
TOM 
TOM The lads came gayly back and went at their sports again with a will,
TOM chattering all the time about Tom's stupendous plan and admiring the
TOM genius of it. After a dainty egg and fish dinner, Tom said he wanted to
TOM learn to smoke, now. Joe caught at the idea and said he would like to
TOM try, too. So Huck made pipes and filled them. These novices had never
TOM smoked anything before but cigars made of grape-vine, and they ``bit''
TOM the tongue, and were not considered manly anyway.
TOM 
TOM Now they stretched themselves out on their elbows and began to puff,
TOM charily, and with slender confidence. The smoke had an unpleasant taste,
TOM and they gagged a little, but Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Why, it's just as easy! If I'd a knowed this was all, I'd a learnt
TOM long ago.''
TOM 
TOM ``So would I,'' said Joe. ``It's just nothing.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, many a time I've looked at people smoking, and thought well I
TOM wish I could do that; but I never thought I could,'' said Tom.
TOM 
TOM ``That's just the way with me, hain't it, Huck? You've heard me talk
TOM just that way -- haven't you, Huck? I'll leave it to Huck if I
TOM haven't.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes -- heaps of times,'' said Huck.
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I have too,'' said Tom; ``oh, hundreds of times. Once down by
TOM the slaughter-house. Don't you remember, Huck? Bob Tanner was there, and
TOM Johnny Miller, and Jeff Thatcher, when I said it. Don't you remember,
TOM Huck, 'bout me saying that?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, that's so,'' said Huck. ``That was the day after I lost a white
TOM alley. No, 'twas the day before.''
TOM 
TOM ``There -- I told you so,'' said Tom. ``Huck recollects it.''
TOM 
TOM ``I bleeve I could smoke this pipe all day,'' said Joe. ``I don't feel
TOM sick.''
TOM 
TOM ``Neither do I,'' said Tom. ``I could smoke it all day. But I bet you
TOM Jeff Thatcher couldn't.''
TOM 
TOM ``Jeff Thatcher! Why, he'd keel over just with two draws. Just let him
TOM try it once. HE'D see!''
TOM 
TOM ``I bet he would. And Johnny Miller -- I wish could see Johnny Miller
TOM tackle it once.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, don't I!'' said Joe. ``Why, I bet you Johnny Miller couldn't any
TOM more do this than nothing. Just one little snifter would fetch HIM.''
TOM 
TOM ``'Deed it would, Joe. Say -- I wish the boys could see us now.''
TOM 
TOM ``So do I.''
TOM 
TOM ``Say -- boys, don't say anything about it, and some time when they're
TOM around, I'll come up to you and say, 'Joe, got a pipe? I want a smoke.'
TOM And you'll say, kind of careless like, as if it warn't anything, you'll
TOM say, 'Yes, I got my OLD pipe, and another one, but my tobacker ain't
TOM very good.' And I'll say, 'Oh, that's all right, if it's STRONG enough.'
TOM And then you'll out with the pipes, and we'll light up just as ca'm, and
TOM then just see 'em look!''
TOM 
TOM ``By jings, that'll be gay, Tom! I wish it was NOW!''
TOM 
TOM ``So do I! And when we tell 'em we learned when we was off pirating,
TOM won't they wish they'd been along?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, I reckon not! I'll just BET they will!''
TOM 
TOM So the talk ran on. But presently it began to flag a trifle, and grow
TOM disjointed. The silences widened; the expectoration marvellously
TOM increased. Every pore inside the boys' cheeks became a spouting
TOM fountain; they could scarcely bail out the cellars under their tongues
TOM fast enough to prevent an inundation; little overflowings down their
TOM throats occurred in spite of all they could do, and sudden retchings
TOM followed every time. Both boys were looking very pale and miserable,
TOM now. Joe's pipe dropped from his nerveless fingers. Tom's followed. Both
TOM fountains were going furiously and both pumps bailing with might and
TOM main. Joe said feebly:
TOM 
TOM ``I've lost my knife. I reckon I better go and find it.''
TOM 
TOM Tom said, with quivering lips and halting utterance:
TOM 
TOM ``I'll help you. You go over that way and I'll hunt around by the
TOM spring. No, you needn't come, Huck -- we can find it.''
TOM 
TOM So Huck sat down again, and waited an hour. Then he found it lonesome,
TOM and went to find his comrades. They were wide apart in the woods, both
TOM very pale, both fast asleep. But something informed him that if they had
TOM had any trouble they had got rid of it.
TOM 
TOM They were not talkative at supper that night. They had a humble look,
TOM and when Huck prepared his pipe after the meal and was going to prepare
TOM theirs, they said no, they were not feeling very well -- something they
TOM ate at dinner had disagreed with them.
TOM 
TOM About midnight Joe awoke, and called the boys. There was a brooding
TOM oppressiveness in the air that seemed to bode something. The boys
TOM huddled themselves together and sought the friendly companionship of the
TOM fire, though the dull dead heat of the breathless atmosphere was
TOM stifling. They sat still, intent and waiting. The solemn hush continued.
TOM Beyond the light of the fire everything was swallowed up in the
TOM blackness of darkness. Presently there came a quivering glow that
TOM vaguely revealed the foliage for a moment and then vanished. By and by
TOM another came, a little stronger. Then another. Then a faint moan came
TOM sighing through the branches of the forest and the boys felt a fleeting
TOM breath upon their cheeks, and shuddered with the fancy that the Spirit
TOM of the Night had gone by. There was a pause. Now a weird flash turned
TOM night into day and showed every little grass-blade, separate and
TOM distinct, that grew about their feet. And it showed three white,
TOM startled faces, too. A deep peal of thunder went rolling and tumbling
TOM down the heavens and lost itself in sullen rumblings in the distance. A
TOM sweep of chilly air passed by, rustling all the leaves and snowing the
TOM flaky ashes broadcast about the fire. Another fierce glare lit up the
TOM forest and an instant crash followed that seemed to rend the tree-tops
TOM right over the boys' heads. They clung together in terror, in the thick
TOM gloom that followed. A few big rain-drops fell pattering upon the
TOM leaves.
TOM 
TOM ``Quick! boys, go for the tent!'' exclaimed Tom.
TOM 
TOM They sprang away, stumbling over roots and among vines in the dark, no
TOM two plunging in the same direction. A furious blast roared through the
TOM trees, making everything sing as it went. One blinding flash after
TOM another came, and peal on peal of deafening thunder. And now a drenching
TOM rain poured down and the rising hurricane drove it in sheets along the
TOM ground. The boys cried out to each other, but the roaring wind and the
TOM booming thunder-blasts drowned their voices utterly. However, one by one
TOM they straggled in at last and took shelter under the tent, cold, scared,
TOM and streaming with water; but to have company in misery seemed something
TOM to be grateful for. They could not talk, the old sail flapped so
TOM furiously, even if the other noises would have allowed them. The tempest
TOM rose higher and higher, and presently the sail tore loose from its
TOM fastenings and went winging away on the blast. The boys seized each
TOM others' hands and fled, with many tumblings and bruises, to the shelter
TOM of a great oak that stood upon the river-bank. Now the battle was at its
TOM highest. Under the ceaseless conflagration of lightning that flamed in
TOM the skies, everything below stood out in clean-cut and shadowless
TOM distinctness: the bending trees, the billowy river, white with foam, the
TOM driving spray of spume-flakes, the dim outlines of the high bluffs on
TOM the other side, glimpsed through the drifting cloud-rack and the
TOM slanting veil of rain. Every little while some giant tree yielded the
TOM fight and fell crashing through the younger growth; and the unflagging
TOM thunder-peals came now in ear-splitting explosive bursts, keen and
TOM sharp, and unspeakably appalling. The storm culminated in one matchless
TOM effort that seemed likely to tear the island to pieces, burn it up,
TOM drown it to the tree-tops, blow it away, and deafen every creature in
TOM it, all at one and the same moment. It was a wild night for homeless
TOM young heads to be out in.
TOM 
TOM But at last the battle was done, and the forces retired with weaker and
TOM weaker threatenings and grumblings, and peace resumed her sway. The boys
TOM went back to camp, a good deal awed; but they found there was still
TOM something to be thankful for, because the great sycamore, the shelter of
TOM their beds, was a ruin, now, blasted by the lightnings, and they were
TOM not under it when the catastrophe happened.
TOM 
TOM Everything in camp was drenched, the camp-fire as well; for they were
TOM but heedless lads, like their generation, and had made no provision
TOM against rain. Here was matter for dismay, for they were soaked through
TOM and chilled. They were eloquent in their distress; but they presently
TOM discovered that the fire had eaten so far up under the great log it had
TOM been built against (where it curved upward and separated itself from the
TOM ground), that a handbreadth or so of it had escaped wetting; so they
TOM patiently wrought until, with shreds and bark gathered from the under
TOM sides of sheltered logs, they coaxed the fire to burn again. Then they
TOM piled on great dead boughs till they had a roaring furnace, and were
TOM glad-hearted once more. They dried their boiled ham and had a feast, and
TOM after that they sat by the fire and expanded and glorified their
TOM midnight adventure until morning, for there was not a dry spot to sleep
TOM on, anywhere around.
TOM 
TOM As the sun began to steal in upon the boys, drowsiness came over them,
TOM and they went out on the sandbar and lay down to sleep. They got
TOM scorched out by and by, and drearily set about getting breakfast. After
TOM the meal they felt rusty, and stiff-jointed, and a little home-sick once
TOM more. Tom saw the signs, and fell to cheering up the pirates as well as
TOM he could. But they cared nothing for marbles, or circus, or swimming, or
TOM anything. He reminded them of the imposing secret, and raised a ray of
TOM cheer. While it lasted, he got them interested in a new device. This was
TOM to knock off being pirates, for a while, and be Indians for a change.
TOM They were attracted by this idea; so it was not long before they were
TOM stripped, and striped from head to heel with black mud, like so many
TOM zebras -- all of them chiefs, of course -- and then they went tearing
TOM through the woods to attack an English settlement.
TOM 
TOM By and by they separated into three hostile tribes, and darted upon each
TOM other from ambush with dreadful war-whoops, and killed and scalped each
TOM other by thousands. It was a gory day. Consequently it was an extremely
TOM satisfactory one.
TOM 
TOM They assembled in camp toward supper-time, hungry and happy; but now a
TOM difficulty arose -- hostile Indians could not break the bread of
TOM hospitality together without first making peace, and this was a simple
TOM impossibility without smoking a pipe of peace. There was no other
TOM process that ever they had heard of. Two of the savages almost wished
TOM they had remained pirates. However, there was no other way; so with such
TOM show of cheerfulness as they could muster they called for the pipe and
TOM took their whiff as it passed, in due form.
TOM 
TOM And behold, they were glad they had gone into savagery, for they had
TOM gained something; they found that they could now smoke a little without
TOM having to go and hunt for a lost knife; they did not get sick enough to
TOM be seriously uncomfortable. They were not likely to fool away this high
TOM promise for lack of effort. No, they practised cautiously, after supper,
TOM with right fair success, and so they spent a jubilant evening. They were
TOM prouder and happier in their new acquirement than they would have been
TOM in the scalping and skinning of the Six Nations. We will leave them to
TOM smoke and chatter and brag, since we have no further use for them at
TOM present.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XVII
TOM 
TOM BUT there was no hilarity in the little town that same tranquil Saturday
TOM afternoon. The Harpers, and Aunt Polly's family, were being put into
TOM mourning, with great grief and many tears. An unusual quiet possessed
TOM the village, although it was ordinarily quiet enough, in all conscience.
TOM The villagers conducted their concerns with an absent air, and talked
TOM little; but they sighed often. The Saturday holiday seemed a burden to
TOM the children. They had no heart in their sports, and gradually gave them
TOM up.
TOM 
TOM In the afternoon Becky Thatcher found herself moping about the deserted
TOM schoolhouse yard, and feeling very melancholy. But she found nothing
TOM there to comfort her. She soliloquized:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, if I only had a brass andiron-knob again! But I haven't got
TOM anything now to remember him by.'' And she choked back a little sob.
TOM 
TOM Presently she stopped, and said to herself:
TOM 
TOM ``It was right here. Oh, if it was to do over again, I wouldn't say that
TOM -- I wouldn't say it for the whole world. But he's gone now; I'll never,
TOM never, never see him any more.''
TOM 
TOM This thought broke her down, and she wandered away, with tears rolling
TOM down her cheeks. Then quite a group of boys and girls -- playmates of
TOM Tom's and Joe's -- came by, and stood looking over the paling fence and
TOM talking in reverent tones of how Tom did so-and-so the last time they
TOM saw him, and how Joe said this and that small trifle (pregnant with
TOM awful prophecy, as they could easily see now!) -- and each speaker
TOM pointed out the exact spot where the lost lads stood at the time, and
TOM then added something like ``and I was a-standing just so -- just as I am
TOM now, and as if you was him -- I was as close as that -- and he smiled,
TOM just this way -- and then something seemed to go all over me, like --
TOM awful, you know -- and I never thought what it meant, of course, but I
TOM can see now!''
TOM 
TOM Then there was a dispute about who saw the dead boys last in life, and
TOM many claimed that dismal distinction, and offered evidences, more or
TOM less tampered with by the witness; and when it was ultimately decided
TOM who DID see the departed last, and exchanged the last words with them,
TOM the lucky parties took upon themselves a sort of sacred importance, and
TOM were gaped at and envied by all the rest. One poor chap, who had no
TOM other grandeur to offer, said with tolerably manifest pride in the
TOM remembrance:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, Tom Sawyer he licked me once.''
TOM 
TOM But that bid for glory was a failure. Most of the boys could say that,
TOM and so that cheapened the distinction too much. The group loitered away,
TOM still recalling memories of the lost heroes, in awed voices.
TOM 
TOM When the Sunday-school hour was finished, the next morning, the bell
TOM began to toll, instead of ringing in the usual way. It was a very still
TOM Sabbath, and the mournful sound seemed in keeping with the musing hush
TOM that lay upon nature. The villagers began to gather, loitering a moment
TOM in the vestibule to converse in whispers about the sad event. But there
TOM was no whispering in the house; only the funereal rustling of dresses as
TOM the women gathered to their seats disturbed the silence there. None
TOM could remember when the little church had been so full before. There was
TOM finally a waiting pause, an expectant dumbness, and then Aunt Polly
TOM entered, followed by Sid and Mary, and they by the Harper family, all in
TOM deep black, and the whole congregation, the old minister as well, rose
TOM reverently and stood until the mourners were seated in the front pew.
TOM There was another communing silence, broken at intervals by muffled
TOM sobs, and then the minister spread his hands abroad and prayed. A moving
TOM hymn was sung, and the text followed: ``I am the Resurrection and the
TOM Life.''
TOM 
TOM As the service proceeded, the clergyman drew such pictures of the
TOM graces, the winning ways, and the rare promise of the lost lads that
TOM every soul there, thinking he recognized these pictures, felt a pang in
TOM remembering that he had persistently blinded himself to them always
TOM before, and had as persistently seen only faults and flaws in the poor
TOM boys. The minister related many a touching incident in the lives of the
TOM departed, too, which illustrated their sweet, generous natures, and the
TOM people could easily see, now, how noble and beautiful those episodes
TOM were, and remembered with grief that at the time they occurred they had
TOM seemed rank rascalities, well deserving of the cowhide. The congregation
TOM became more and more moved, as the pathetic tale went on, till at last
TOM the whole company broke down and joined the weeping mourners in a chorus
TOM of anguished sobs, the preacher himself giving way to his feelings, and
TOM crying in the pulpit.
TOM 
TOM There was a rustle in the gallery, which nobody noticed; a moment later
TOM the church door creaked; the minister raised his streaming eyes above
TOM his handkerchief, and stood transfixed! First one and then another pair
TOM of eyes followed the minister's, and then almost with one impulse the
TOM congregation rose and stared while the three dead boys came marching up
TOM the aisle, Tom in the lead, Joe next, and Huck, a ruin of drooping rags,
TOM sneaking sheepishly in the rear! They had been hid in the unused gallery
TOM listening to their own funeral sermon!
TOM 
TOM Aunt Polly, Mary, and the Harpers threw themselves upon their restored
TOM ones, smothered them with kisses and poured out thanksgivings, while
TOM poor Huck stood abashed and uncomfortable, not knowing exactly what to
TOM do or where to hide from so many unwelcoming eyes. He wavered, and
TOM started to slink away, but Tom seized him and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Aunt Polly, it ain't fair. Somebody's got to be glad to see Huck.''
TOM 
TOM ``And so they shall. I'm glad to see him, poor motherless thing!'' And
TOM the loving attentions Aunt Polly lavished upon him were the one thing
TOM capable of making him more uncomfortable than he was before.
TOM 
TOM Suddenly the minister shouted at the top of his voice: ``Praise God from
TOM whom all blessings flow -- SING! -- and put your hearts in it!''
TOM 
TOM And they did. Old Hundred swelled up with a triumphant burst, and while
TOM it shook the rafters Tom Sawyer the Pirate looked around upon the
TOM envying juveniles about him and confessed in his heart that this was the
TOM proudest moment of his life.
TOM 
TOM As the ``sold'' congregation trooped out they said they would almost be
TOM willing to be made ridiculous again to hear Old Hundred sung like that
TOM once more.
TOM 
TOM Tom got more cuffs and kisses that day -- according to Aunt Polly's
TOM varying moods -- than he had earned before in a year; and he hardly knew
TOM which expressed the most gratefulness to God and affection for himself.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XVIII
TOM 
TOM THAT was Tom's great secret -- the scheme to return home with his
TOM brother pirates and attend their own funerals. They had paddled over to
TOM the Missouri shore on a log, at dusk on Saturday, landing five or six
TOM miles below the village; they had slept in the woods at the edge of the
TOM town till nearly daylight, and had then crept through back lanes and
TOM alleys and finished their sleep in the gallery of the church among a
TOM chaos of invalided benches.
TOM 
TOM At breakfast, Monday morning, Aunt Polly and Mary were very loving to
TOM Tom, and very attentive to his wants. There was an unusual amount of
TOM talk. In the course of it Aunt Polly said:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I don't say it wasn't a fine joke, Tom, to keep everybody
TOM suffering 'most a week so you boys had a good time, but it is a pity you
TOM could be so hard-hearted as to let me suffer so. If you could come over
TOM on a log to go to your funeral, you could have come over and give me a
TOM hint some way that you warn't dead, but only run off.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, you could have done that, Tom,'' said Mary; ``and I believe you
TOM would if you had thought of it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Would you, Tom?'' said Aunt Polly, her face lighting wistfully. ``Say,
TOM now, would you, if you'd thought of it?''
TOM 
TOM ``I -- well, I don't know. 'Twould 'a' spoiled everything.''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, I hoped you loved me that much,'' said Aunt Polly, with a grieved
TOM tone that discomforted the boy. ``It would have been something if you'd
TOM cared enough to THINK of it, even if you didn't DO it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Now, auntie, that ain't any harm,'' pleaded Mary; ``it's only Tom's
TOM giddy way -- he is always in such a rush that he never thinks of
TOM anything.''
TOM 
TOM ``More's the pity. Sid would have thought. And Sid would have come and
TOM DONE it, too. Tom, you'll look back, some day, when it's too late, and
TOM wish you'd cared a little more for me when it would have cost you so
TOM little.''
TOM 
TOM ``Now, auntie, you know I do care for you,'' said Tom.
TOM 
TOM ``I'd know it better if you acted more like it.''
TOM 
TOM ``I wish now I'd thought,'' said Tom, with a repentant tone; ``but I
TOM dreamt about you, anyway. That's something, ain't it?''
TOM 
TOM ``It ain't much -- a cat does that much -- but it's better than nothing.
TOM What did you dream?''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, Wednesday night I dreamt that you was sitting over there by the
TOM bed, and Sid was sitting by the woodbox, and Mary next to him.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, so we did. So we always do. I'm glad your dreams could take even
TOM that much trouble about us.''
TOM 
TOM ``And I dreamt that Joe Harper's mother was here.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, she was here! Did you dream any more?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, lots. But it's so dim, now.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, try to recollect -- can't you?''
TOM 
TOM ``Somehow it seems to me that the wind -- the wind blowed the -- the
TOM --''
TOM 
TOM ``Try harder, Tom! The wind did blow something. Come!''
TOM 
TOM Tom pressed his fingers on his forehead an anxious minute, and then
TOM said:
TOM 
TOM ``I've got it now! I've got it now! It blowed the candle!''
TOM 
TOM ``Mercy on us! Go on, Tom -- go on!''
TOM 
TOM ``And it seems to me that you said, 'Why, I believe that that door --'''
TOM 
TOM ``Go ON, Tom!''
TOM 
TOM ``Just let me study a moment -- just a moment. Oh, yes -- you said you
TOM believed the door was open.''
TOM 
TOM ``As I'm sitting here, I did! Didn't I, Mary! Go on!''
TOM 
TOM ``And then -- and then -- well I won't be certain, but it seems like as
TOM if you made Sid go and -- and --''
TOM 
TOM ``Well? Well? What did I make him do, Tom? What did I make him do?''
TOM 
TOM ``You made him -- you -- Oh, you made him shut it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, for the land's sake! I never heard the beat of that in all my
TOM days! Don't tell ME there ain't anything in dreams, any more. Sereny
TOM Harper shall know of this before I'm an hour older. I'd like to see her
TOM get around THIS with her rubbage 'bout superstition. Go on, Tom!''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, it's all getting just as bright as day, now. Next you said I
TOM warn't BAD, only mischeevous and harum-scarum, and not any more
TOM responsible than -- than -- I think it was a colt, or something.''
TOM 
TOM ``And so it was! Well, goodness gracious! Go on, Tom!''
TOM 
TOM ``And then you began to cry.''
TOM 
TOM ``So I did. So I did. Not the first time, neither. And then --''
TOM 
TOM ``Then Mrs. Harper she began to cry, and said Joe was just the same, and
TOM she wished she hadn't whipped him for taking cream when she'd throwed it
TOM out her own self --''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom! The sperrit was upon you! You was a prophesying -- that's what
TOM you was doing! Land alive, go on, Tom!''
TOM 
TOM ``Then Sid he said -- he said --''
TOM 
TOM ``I don't think I said anything,'' said Sid.
TOM 
TOM ``Yes you did, Sid,'' said Mary.
TOM 
TOM ``Shut your heads and let Tom go on! What did he say, Tom?''
TOM 
TOM ``He said -- I THINK he said he hoped I was better off where I was gone
TOM to, but if I'd been better sometimes --''
TOM 
TOM ``THERE, d'you hear that! It was his very words!''
TOM 
TOM ``And you shut him up sharp.''
TOM 
TOM ``I lay I did! There must 'a' been an angel there. There WAS an angel
TOM there, somewheres!''
TOM 
TOM ``And Mrs. Harper told about Joe scaring her with a firecracker, and you
TOM told about Peter and the Painkiller --''
TOM 
TOM ``Just as true as I live!''
TOM 
TOM ``And then there was a whole lot of talk 'bout dragging the river for
TOM us, and 'bout having the funeral Sunday, and then you and old Miss
TOM Harper hugged and cried, and she went.''
TOM 
TOM ``It happened just so! It happened just so, as sure as I'm a-sitting in
TOM these very tracks. Tom, you couldn't told it more like if you'd 'a' seen
TOM it! And then what? Go on, Tom!''
TOM 
TOM ``Then I thought you prayed for me -- and I could see you and hear every
TOM word you said. And you went to bed, and I was so sorry that I took and
TOM wrote on a piece of sycamore bark, 'We ain't dead -- we are only off
TOM being pirates,' and put it on the table by the candle; and then you
TOM looked so good, laying there asleep, that I thought I went and leaned
TOM over and kissed you on the lips.''
TOM 
TOM ``Did you, Tom, DID you! I just forgive you everything for that!'' And
TOM she seized the boy in a crushing embrace that made him feel like the
TOM guiltiest of villains.
TOM 
TOM ``It was very kind, even though it was only a -- dream,'' Sid
TOM soliloquized just audibly.
TOM 
TOM ``Shut up, Sid! A body does just the same in a dream as he'd do if he
TOM was awake. Here's a big Milum apple I've been saving for you, Tom, if
TOM you was ever found again -- now go 'long to school. I'm thankful to the
TOM good God and Father of us all I've got you back, that's long-suffering
TOM and merciful to them that believe on Him and keep His word, though
TOM goodness knows I'm unworthy of it, but if only the worthy ones got His
TOM blessings and had His hand to help them over the rough places, there's
TOM few enough would smile here or ever enter into His rest when the long
TOM night comes. Go 'long Sid, Mary, Tom -- take yourselves off -- you've
TOM hendered me long enough.''
TOM 
TOM The children left for school, and the old lady to call on Mrs. Harper
TOM and vanquish her realism with Tom's marvellous dream. Sid had better
TOM judgment than to utter the thought that was in his mind as he left the
TOM house. It was this: ``Pretty thin -- as long a dream as that, without
TOM any mistakes in it!''
TOM 
TOM What a hero Tom was become, now! He did not go skipping and prancing,
TOM but moved with a dignified swagger as became a pirate who felt that the
TOM public eye was on him. And indeed it was; he tried not to seem to see
TOM the looks or hear the remarks as he passed along, but they were food and
TOM drink to him. Smaller boys than himself flocked at his heels, as proud
TOM to be seen with him, and tolerated by him, as if he had been the drummer
TOM at the head of a procession or the elephant leading a menagerie into
TOM town. Boys of his own size pretended not to know he had been away at
TOM all; but they were consuming with envy, nevertheless. They would have
TOM given anything to have that swarthy suntanned skin of his, and his
TOM glittering notoriety; and Tom would not have parted with either for a
TOM circus.
TOM 
TOM At school the children made so much of him and of Joe, and delivered
TOM such eloquent admiration from their eyes, that the two heroes were not
TOM long in becoming insufferably ``stuck-up.'' They began to tell their
TOM adventures to hungry listeners -- but they only began; it was not a
TOM thing likely to have an end, with imaginations like theirs to furnish
TOM material. And finally, when they got out their pipes and went serenely
TOM puffing around, the very summit of glory was reached.
TOM 
TOM Tom decided that he could be independent of Becky Thatcher now. Glory
TOM was sufficient. He would live for glory. Now that he was distinguished,
TOM maybe she would be wanting to ``make up.'' Well, let her -- she should
TOM see that he could be as indifferent as some other people. Presently she
TOM arrived. Tom pretended not to see her. He moved away and joined a group
TOM of boys and girls and began to talk. Soon he observed that she was
TOM tripping gayly back and forth with flushed face and dancing eyes,
TOM pretending to be busy chasing schoolmates, and screaming with laughter
TOM when she made a capture; but he noticed that she always made her
TOM captures in his vicinity, and that she seemed to cast a conscious eye in
TOM his direction at such times, too. It gratified all the vicious vanity
TOM that was in him; and so, instead of winning him, it only ``set him up''
TOM the more and made him the more diligent to avoid betraying that he knew
TOM she was about. Presently she gave over skylarking, and moved
TOM irresolutely about, sighing once or twice and glancing furtively and
TOM wistfully toward Tom. Then she observed that now Tom was talking more
TOM particularly to Amy Lawrence than to any one else. She felt a sharp pang
TOM and grew disturbed and uneasy at once. She tried to go away, but her
TOM feet were treacherous, and carried her to the group instead. She said to
TOM a girl almost at Tom's elbow -- with sham vivacity:
TOM 
TOM ``Why, Mary Austin! you bad girl, why didn't you come to
TOM Sunday-school?''
TOM 
TOM ``I did come -- didn't you see me?''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, no! Did you? Where did you sit?''
TOM 
TOM ``I was in Miss Peters' class, where I always go. I saw YOU.''
TOM 
TOM ``Did you? Why, it's funny I didn't see you. I wanted to tell you about
TOM the picnic.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, that's jolly. Who's going to give it?''
TOM 
TOM ``My ma's going to let me have one.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, goody; I hope she'll let ME come.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, she will. The picnic's for me. She'll let anybody come that I
TOM want, and I want you.''
TOM 
TOM ``That's ever so nice. When is it going to be?''
TOM 
TOM ``By and by. Maybe about vacation.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, won't it be fun! You going to have all the girls and boys?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, every one that's friends to me -- or wants to be''; and she
TOM glanced ever so furtively at Tom, but he talked right along to Amy
TOM Lawrence about the terrible storm on the island, and how the lightning
TOM tore the great sycamore tree ``all to flinders'' while he was ``standing
TOM within three feet of it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, may I come?'' said Grace Miller.
TOM 
TOM ``Yes.''
TOM 
TOM ``And me?'' said Sally Rogers.
TOM 
TOM ``Yes.''
TOM 
TOM ``And me, too?'' said Susy Harper. ``And Joe?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes.''
TOM 
TOM And so on, with clapping of joyful hands till all the group had begged
TOM for invitations but Tom and Amy. Then Tom turned coolly away, still
TOM talking, and took Amy with him. Becky's lips trembled and the tears came
TOM to her eyes; she hid these signs with a forced gayety and went on
TOM chattering, but the life had gone out of the picnic, now, and out of
TOM everything else; she got away as soon as she could and hid herself and
TOM had what her sex call ``a good cry.'' Then she sat moody, with wounded
TOM pride, till the bell rang. She roused up, now, with a vindictive cast in
TOM her eye, and gave her plaited tails a shake and said she knew what SHE'D
TOM do.
TOM 
TOM At recess Tom continued his flirtation with Amy with jubilant
TOM self-satisfaction. And he kept drifting about to find Becky and lacerate
TOM her with the performance. At last he spied her, but there was a sudden
TOM falling of his mercury. She was sitting cosily on a little bench behind
TOM the schoolhouse looking at a picture-book with Alfred Temple -- and so
TOM absorbed were they, and their heads so close together over the book,
TOM that they did not seem to be conscious of anything in the world besides.
TOM Jealousy ran red-hot through Tom's veins. He began to hate himself for
TOM throwing away the chance Becky had offered for a reconciliation. He
TOM called himself a fool, and all the hard names he could think of. He
TOM wanted to cry with vexation. Amy chatted happily along, as they walked,
TOM for her heart was singing, but Tom's tongue had lost its function. He
TOM did not hear what Amy was saying, and whenever she paused expectantly he
TOM could only stammer an awkward assent, which was as often misplaced as
TOM otherwise. He kept drifting to the rear of the school-house, again and
TOM again, to sear his eyeballs with the hateful spectacle there. He could
TOM not help it. And it maddened him to see, as he thought he saw, that
TOM Becky Thatcher never once suspected that he was even in the land of the
TOM living. But she did see, nevertheless; and she knew she was winning her
TOM fight, too, and was glad to see him suffer as she had suffered.
TOM 
TOM Amy's happy prattle became intolerable. Tom hinted at things he had to
TOM attend to; things that must be done; and time was fleeting. But in vain
TOM -- the girl chirped on. Tom thought, ``Oh, hang her, ain't I ever going
TOM to get rid of her?'' At last he must be attending to those things -- and
TOM she said artlessly that she would be ``around'' when school let out. And
TOM he hastened away, hating her for it.
TOM 
TOM ``Any other boy!'' Tom thought, grating his teeth. ``Any boy in the
TOM whole town but that Saint Louis smarty that thinks he dresses so fine
TOM and is aristocracy! Oh, all right, I licked you the first day you ever
TOM saw this town, mister, and I'll lick you again! You just wait till I
TOM catch you out! I'll just take and --''
TOM 
TOM And he went through the motions of thrashing an imaginary boy --
TOM pummelling the air, and kicking and gouging. ``Oh, you do, do you? You
TOM holler 'nough, do you? Now, then, let that learn you!'' And so the
TOM imaginary flogging was finished to his satisfaction.
TOM 
TOM Tom fled home at noon. His conscience could not endure any more of Amy's
TOM grateful happiness, and his jealousy could bear no more of the other
TOM distress. Becky resumed her picture inspections with Alfred, but as the
TOM minutes dragged along and no Tom came to suffer, her triumph began to
TOM cloud and she lost interest; gravity and absent-mindedness followed, and
TOM then melancholy; two or three times she pricked up her ear at a
TOM footstep, but it was a false hope; no Tom came. At last she grew
TOM entirely miserable and wished she hadn't carried it so far. When poor
TOM Alfred, seeing that he was losing her, he did not know how, kept
TOM exclaiming: ``Oh, here's a jolly one! look at this!'' she lost patience
TOM at last, and said, ``Oh, don't bother me! I don't care for them!'' and
TOM burst into tears, and got up and walked away.
TOM
