TOM There was one very strong argument in favor of this idea -- namely, that
TOM the quantity of coin he had seen was too vast to be real. He had never
TOM seen as much as fifty dollars in one mass before, and he was like all
TOM boys of his age and station in life, in that he imagined that all
TOM references to ``hundreds'' and ``thousands'' were mere fanciful forms of
TOM speech, and that no such sums really existed in the world. He never had
TOM supposed for a moment that so large a sum as a hundred dollars was to be
TOM found in actual money in any one's possession. If his notions of hidden
TOM treasure had been analyzed, they would have been found to consist of a
TOM handful of real dimes and a bushel of vague, splendid, ungraspable
TOM dollars.
TOM 
TOM But the incidents of his adventure grew sensibly sharper and clearer
TOM under the attrition of thinking them over, and so he presently found
TOM himself leaning to the impression that the thing might not have been a
TOM dream, after all. This uncertainty must be swept away. He would snatch a
TOM hurried breakfast and go and find Huck. Huck was sitting on the gunwale
TOM of a flatboat, listlessly dangling his feet in the water and looking
TOM very melancholy. Tom concluded to let Huck lead up to the subject. If he
TOM did not do it, then the adventure would be proved to have been only a
TOM dream.
TOM 
TOM ``Hello, Huck!''
TOM 
TOM ``Hello, yourself.''
TOM 
TOM Silence, for a minute.
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, if we'd 'a' left the blame tools at the dead tree, we'd 'a' got
TOM the money. Oh, ain't it awful!''
TOM 
TOM ``'Tain't a dream, then, 'tain't a dream! Somehow I most wish it was.
TOM Dog'd if I don't, Huck.''
TOM 
TOM ``What ain't a dream?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, that thing yesterday. I been half thinking it was.''
TOM 
TOM ``Dream! If them stairs hadn't broke down you'd 'a' seen how much dream
TOM it was! I've had dreams enough all night -- with that patch-eyed Spanish
TOM devil going for me all through 'em -- rot him!''
TOM 
TOM ``No, not rot him. FIND him! Track the money!''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, we'll never find him. A feller don't have only one chance for
TOM such a pile -- and that one's lost. I'd feel mighty shaky if I was to
TOM see him, anyway.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, so'd I; but I'd like to see him, anyway -- and track him out --
TOM to his Number Two.''
TOM 
TOM ``Number Two -- yes, that's it. I been thinking 'bout that. But I can't
TOM make nothing out of it. What do you reckon it is?''
TOM 
TOM ``I dono. It's too deep. Say, Huck -- maybe it's the number of a
TOM house!''
TOM 
TOM ``Goody! ... No, Tom, that ain't it. If it is, it ain't in this
TOM one-horse town. They ain't no numbers here.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, that's so. Lemme think a minute. Here -- it's the number of a
TOM room -- in a tavern, you know!''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, that's the trick! They ain't only two taverns. We can find out
TOM quick.''
TOM 
TOM ``You stay here, Huck, till I come.''
TOM 
TOM Tom was off at once. He did not care to have Huck's company in public
TOM places. He was gone half an hour. He found that in the best tavern, No.
TOM 2 had long been occupied by a young lawyer, and was still so occupied.
TOM In the less ostentatious house, No. 2 was a mystery. The tavern-keeper's
TOM young son said it was kept locked all the time, and he never saw anybody
TOM go into it or come out of it except at night; he did not know any
TOM particular reason for this state of things; had had some little
TOM curiosity, but it was rather feeble; had made the most of the mystery by
TOM entertaining himself with the idea that that room was ``ha'nted''; had
TOM noticed that there was a light in there the night before.
TOM 
TOM ``That's what I've found out, Huck. I reckon that's the very No. 2 we're
TOM after.''
TOM 
TOM ``I reckon it is, Tom. Now what you going to do?''
TOM 
TOM ``Lemme think.''
TOM 
TOM Tom thought a long time. Then he said:
TOM 
TOM ``I'll tell you. The back door of that No. 2 is the door that comes out
TOM into that little close alley between the tavern and the old rattle trap
TOM of a brick store. Now you get hold of all the door-keys you can find,
TOM and I'll nip all of auntie's, and the first dark night we'll go there
TOM and try 'em. And mind you, keep a lookout for Injun Joe, because he said
TOM he was going to drop into town and spy around once more for a chance to
TOM get his revenge. If you see him, you just follow him; and if he don't go
TOM to that No. 2, that ain't the place.''
TOM 
TOM ``Lordy, I don't want to foller him by myself!''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, it'll be night, sure. He mightn't ever see you -- and if he did,
TOM maybe he'd never think anything.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, if it's pretty dark I reckon I'll track him. I dono -- I dono.
TOM I'll try.''
TOM 
TOM ``You bet I'll follow him, if it's dark, Huck. Why, he might 'a' found
TOM out he couldn't get his revenge, and be going right after that money.''
TOM 
TOM ``It's so, Tom, it's so. I'll foller him; I will, by jingoes!''
TOM 
TOM ``Now you're TALKING! Don't you ever weaken, Huck, and I won't.''
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XXVIII
TOM 
TOM THAT night Tom and Huck were ready for their adventure. They hung about
TOM the neighborhood of the tavern until after nine, one watching the alley
TOM at a distance and the other the tavern door. Nobody entered the alley or
TOM left it; nobody resembling the Spaniard entered or left the tavern door.
TOM The night promised to be a fair one; so Tom went home with the
TOM understanding that if a considerable degree of darkness came on, Huck
TOM was to come and ``maow,'' whereupon he would slip out and try the keys.
TOM But the night remained clear, and Huck closed his watch and retired to
TOM bed in an empty sugar hogshead about twelve.
TOM 
TOM Tuesday the boys had the same ill luck. Also Wednesday. But Thursday
TOM night promised better. Tom slipped out in good season with his aunt's
TOM old tin lantern, and a large towel to blindfold it with. He hid the
TOM lantern in Huck's sugar hogshead and the watch began. An hour before
TOM midnight the tavern closed up and its lights (the only ones thereabouts)
TOM were put out. No Spaniard had been seen. Nobody had entered or left the
TOM alley. Everything was auspicious. The blackness of darkness reigned, the
TOM perfect stillness was interrupted only by occasional mutterings of
TOM distant thunder.
TOM 
TOM Tom got his lantern, lit it in the hogshead, wrapped it closely in the
TOM towel, and the two adventurers crept in the gloom toward the tavern.
TOM Huck stood sentry and Tom felt his way into the alley. Then there was a
TOM season of waiting anxiety that weighed upon Huck's spirits like a
TOM mountain. He began to wish he could see a flash from the lantern -- it
TOM would frighten him, but it would at least tell him that Tom was alive
TOM yet. It seemed hours since Tom had disappeared. Surely he must have
TOM fainted; maybe he was dead; maybe his heart had burst under terror and
TOM excitement. In his uneasiness Huck found himself drawing closer and
TOM closer to the alley; fearing all sorts of dreadful things, and
TOM momentarily expecting some catastrophe to happen that would take away
TOM his breath. There was not much to take away, for he seemed only able to
TOM inhale it by thimblefuls, and his heart would soon wear itself out, the
TOM way it was beating. Suddenly there was a flash of light and Tom came
TOM tearing by him: . ``Run!'' said he; ``run, for your life!''
TOM 
TOM He needn't have repeated it; once was enough; Huck was making thirty or
TOM forty miles an hour before the repetition was uttered. The boys never
TOM stopped till they reached the shed of a deserted slaughter-house at the
TOM lower end of the village. Just as they got within its shelter the storm
TOM burst and the rain poured down. As soon as Tom got his breath he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, it was awful! I tried two of the keys, just as soft as I could;
TOM but they seemed to make such a power of racket that I couldn't hardly
TOM get my breath I was so scared. They wouldn't turn in the lock, either.
TOM Well, without noticing what I was doing, I took hold of the knob, and
TOM open comes the door! It warn't locked! I hopped in, and shook off the
TOM towel, and, GREAT CAESAR'S GHOST!''
TOM 
TOM ``What! -- what'd you see, Tom?''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, I most stepped onto Injun Joe's hand!''
TOM 
TOM ``No!''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes! He was lying there, sound asleep on the floor, with his old patch
TOM on his eye and his arms spread out.''
TOM 
TOM ``Lordy, what did you do? Did he wake up?''
TOM 
TOM ``No, never budged. Drunk, I reckon. I just grabbed that towel and
TOM started!''
TOM 
TOM ``I'd never 'a' thought of the towel, I bet!''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I would. My aunt would make me mighty sick if I lost it.''
TOM 
TOM ``Say, Tom, did you see that box?''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, I didn't wait to look around. I didn't see the box, I didn't see
TOM the cross. I didn't see anything but a bottle and a tin cup on the floor
TOM by Injun Joe; yes, I saw two barrels and lots more bottles in the room.
TOM Don't you see, now, what's the matter with that ha'nted room?''
TOM 
TOM ``How?''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, it's ha'nted with whiskey! Maybe ALL the Temperance Taverns have
TOM got a ha'nted room, hey, Huck?''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I reckon maybe that's so. Who'd 'a' thought such a thing? But
TOM say, Tom, now's a mighty good time to get that box, if Injun Joe's
TOM drunk.''
TOM 
TOM ``It is, that! You try it!''
TOM 
TOM Huck shuddered.
TOM 
TOM ``Well, no -- I reckon not.''
TOM 
TOM ``And I reckon not, Huck. Only one bottle along-side of Injun Joe ain't
TOM enough. If there'd been three, he'd be drunk enough and I'd do it.''
TOM 
TOM There was a long pause for reflection, and then Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Lookyhere, Huck, less not try that thing any more till we know Injun
TOM Joe's not in there. It's too scary. Now, if we watch every night, we'll
TOM be dead sure to see him go out, some time or other, and then we'll
TOM snatch that box quicker'n lightning.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I'm agreed. I'll watch the whole night long, and I'll do it
TOM every night, too, if you'll do the other part of the job.''
TOM 
TOM ``All right, I will. All you got to do is to trot up Hooper Street a
TOM block and maow -- and if I'm asleep, you throw some gravel at the window
TOM and that'll fetch me.''
TOM 
TOM ``Agreed, and good as wheat!''
TOM 
TOM ``Now, Huck, the storm's over, and I'll go home. It'll begin to be
TOM daylight in a couple of hours. You go back and watch that long, will
TOM you?''
TOM 
TOM ``I said I would, Tom, and I will. I'll ha'nt that tavern every night
TOM for a year! I'll sleep all day and I'll stand watch all night.''
TOM 
TOM ``That's all right. Now, where you going to sleep?''
TOM 
TOM ``In Ben Rogers' hayloft. He lets me, and so does his pap's nigger man,
TOM Uncle Jake. I tote water for Uncle Jake whenever he wants me to, and any
TOM time I ask him he gives me a little something to eat if he can spare it.
TOM That's a mighty good nigger, Tom. He likes me, becuz I don't ever act as
TOM if I was above him. Sometime I've set right down and eat WITH him. But
TOM you needn't tell that. A body's got to do things when he's awful hungry
TOM he wouldn't want to do as a steady thing.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, if I don't want you in the daytime, I'll let you sleep. I won't
TOM come bothering around. Any time you see something's up, in the night,
TOM just skip right around and maow.''
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XXIX
TOM 
TOM THE first thing Tom heard on Friday morning was a glad piece of news --
TOM Judge Thatcher's family had come back to town the night before. Both
TOM Injun Joe and the treasure sunk into secondary importance for a moment,
TOM and Becky took the chief place in the boy's interest. He saw her and
TOM they had an exhausting good time playing ``hispy'' and ``gully-keeper''
TOM with a crowd of their school-mates. The day was completed and crowned in
TOM a peculiarly satisfactory way: Becky teased her mother to appoint the
TOM next day for the long-promised and long-delayed picnic, and she
TOM consented. The child's delight was boundless; and Tom's not more
TOM moderate. The invitations were sent out before sunset, and straightway
TOM the young folks of the village were thrown into a fever of preparation
TOM and pleasurable anticipation. Tom's excitement enabled him to keep awake
TOM until a pretty late hour, and he had good hopes of hearing Huck's
TOM ``maow,'' and of having his treasure to astonish Becky and the
TOM picnickers with, next day; but he was disappointed. No signal came that
TOM night.
TOM 
TOM Morning came, eventually, and by ten or eleven o'clock a giddy and
TOM rollicking company were gathered at Judge Thatcher's, and everything was
TOM ready for a start. It was not the custom for elderly people to mar the
TOM picnics with their presence. The children were considered safe enough
TOM under the wings of a few young ladies of eighteen and a few young
TOM gentlemen of twenty-three or thereabouts. The old steam ferry-boat was
TOM chartered for the occasion; presently the gay throng filed up the main
TOM street laden with provision-baskets. Sid was sick and had to miss the
TOM fun; Mary remained at home to entertain him. The last thing Mrs.
TOM Thatcher said to Becky, was:
TOM 
TOM ``You'll not get back till late. Perhaps you'd better stay all night
TOM with some of the girls that live near the ferry-landing, child.''
TOM 
TOM ``Then I'll stay with Susy Harper, mamma.''
TOM 
TOM ``Very well. And mind and behave yourself and don't be any trouble.''
TOM 
TOM Presently, as they tripped along, Tom said to Becky:
TOM 
TOM ``Say -- I'll tell you what we'll do. 'Stead of going to Joe Harper's
TOM we'll climb right up the hill and stop at the Widow Douglas'. She'll
TOM have ice-cream! She has it most every day -- dead loads of it. And
TOM she'll be awful glad to have us.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, that will be fun!''
TOM 
TOM Then Becky reflected a moment and said:
TOM 
TOM ``But what will mamma say?''
TOM 
TOM ``How'll she ever know?''
TOM 
TOM The girl turned the idea over in her mind, and said reluctantly:
TOM 
TOM ``I reckon it's wrong -- but --''
TOM 
TOM ``But shucks! Your mother won't know, and so what's the harm? All she
TOM wants is that you'll be safe; and I bet you she'd 'a' said go there if
TOM she'd 'a' thought of it. I know she would!''
TOM 
TOM The Widow Douglas' splendid hospitality was a tempting bait. It and
TOM Tom's persuasions presently carried the day. So it was decided to say
TOM nothing anybody about the night's programme. Presently it occurred to
TOM Tom that maybe Huck might come this very night and give the signal. The
TOM thought took a deal of the spirit out of his anticipations. Still he
TOM could not bear to give up the fun at Widow Douglas'. And why should he
TOM give it up, he reasoned -- the signal did not come the night before, so
TOM why should it be any more likely to come to-night? The sure fun of the
TOM evening outweighed the uncertain treasure; and, boy-like, he determined
TOM to yield to the stronger inclination and not allow himself to think of
TOM the box of money another time that day.
TOM 
TOM Three miles below town the ferryboat stopped at the mouth of a woody
TOM hollow and tied up. The crowd swarmed ashore and soon the forest
TOM distances and craggy heights echoed far and near with shoutings and
TOM laughter. All the different ways of getting hot and tired were gone
TOM through with, and by-and-by the rovers straggled back to camp fortified
TOM with responsible appetites, and then the destruction of the good things
TOM began. After the feast there was a refreshing season of rest and chat in
TOM the shade of spreading oaks. By-and-by somebody shouted:
TOM 
TOM ``Who's ready for the cave?''
TOM 
TOM Everybody was. Bundles of candles were procured, and straightway there
TOM was a general scamper up the hill. The mouth of the cave was up the
TOM hillside -- an opening shaped like a letter A. Its massive oaken door
TOM stood unbarred. Within was a small chamber, chilly as an ice-house, and
TOM walled by Nature with solid limestone that was dewy with a cold sweat.
TOM It was romantic and mysterious to stand here in the deep gloom and look
TOM out upon the green valley shining in the sun. But the impressiveness of
TOM the situation quickly wore off, and the romping began again. The moment
TOM a candle was lighted there was a general rush upon the owner of it; a
TOM struggle and a gallant defence followed, but the candle was soon knocked
TOM down or blown out, and then there was a glad clamor of laughter and a
TOM new chase. But all things have an end. By-and-by the procession went
TOM filing down the steep descent of the main avenue, the flickering rank of
TOM lights dimly revealing the lofty walls of rock almost to their point of
TOM junction sixty feet overhead. This main avenue was not more than eight
TOM or ten feet wide. Every few steps other lofty and still narrower
TOM crevices branched from it on either hand -- for McDougal's cave was but
TOM a vast labyrinth of crooked aisles that ran into each other and out
TOM again and led nowhere. It was said that one might wander days and nights
TOM together through its intricate tangle of rifts and chasms, and never
TOM find the end of the cave; and that he might go down, and down, and still
TOM down, into the earth, and it was just the same -- labyrinth under
TOM labyrinth, and no end to any of them. No man ``knew'' the cave. That was
TOM an impossible thing. Most of the young men knew a portion of it, and it
TOM was not customary to venture much beyond this known portion. Tom Sawyer
TOM knew as much of the cave as any one.
TOM 
TOM The procession moved along the main avenue some three-quarters of a
TOM mile, and then groups and couples began to slip aside into branch
TOM avenues, fly along the dismal corridors, and take each other by surprise
TOM at points where the corridors joined again. Parties were able to elude
TOM each other for the space of half an hour without going beyond the
TOM ``known'' ground.
TOM 
TOM By-and-by, one group after another came straggling back to the mouth of
TOM the cave, panting, hilarious, smeared from head to foot with tallow
TOM drippings, daubed with clay, and entirely delighted with the success of
TOM the day. Then they were astonished to find that they had been taking no
TOM note of time and that night was about at hand. The clanging bell had
TOM been calling for half an hour. However, this sort of close to the day's
TOM adventures was romantic and therefore satisfactory. When the ferryboat
TOM with her wild freight pushed into the stream, nobody cared sixpence for
TOM the wasted time but the captain of the craft.
TOM 
TOM Huck was already upon his watch when the ferry-boat's lights went
TOM glinting past the wharf. He heard no noise on board, for the young
TOM people were as subdued and still as people usually are who are nearly
TOM tired to death. He wondered what boat it was, and why she did not stop
TOM at the wharf -- and then he dropped her out of his mind and put his
TOM attention upon his business. The night was growing cloudy and dark. Ten
TOM o'clock came, and the noise of vehicles ceased, scattered lights began
TOM to wink out, all straggling foot-passengers disappeared, the village
TOM betook itself to its slumbers and left the small watcher alone with the
TOM silence and the ghosts. Eleven o'clock came, and the tavern lights were
TOM put out; darkness everywhere, now. Huck waited what seemed a weary long
TOM time, but nothing happened. His faith was weakening. Was there any use?
TOM Was there really any use? Why not give it up and turn in?
TOM 
TOM A noise fell upon his ear. He was all attention in an instant. The alley
TOM door closed softly. He sprang to the corner of the brick store. The next
TOM moment two men brushed by him, and one seemed to have something under
TOM his arm. It must be that box! So they were going to remove the treasure.
TOM Why call Tom now? It would be absurd -- the men would get away with the
TOM box and never be found again. No, he would stick to their wake and
TOM follow them; he would trust to the darkness for security from discovery.
TOM So communing with himself, Huck stepped out and glided along behind the
TOM men, cat-like, with bare feet, allowing them to keep just far enough
TOM ahead not to be invisible.
TOM 
TOM They moved up the river street three blocks, then turned to the left up
TOM a cross-street. They went straight ahead, then, until they came to the
TOM path that led up Cardiff Hill; this they took. They passed by the old
TOM Welshman's house, half-way up the hill, without hesitating, and still
TOM climbed upward. Good, thought Huck, they will bury it in the old quarry.
TOM But they never stopped at the quarry. They passed on, up the summit.
TOM They plunged into the narrow path between the tall sumach bushes, and
TOM were at once hidden in the gloom. Huck closed up and shortened his
TOM distance, now, for they would never be able to see him. He trotted along
TOM awhile; then slackened his pace, fearing he was gaining too fast; moved
TOM on a piece, then stopped altogether; listened; no sound; none, save that
TOM he seemed to hear the beating of his own heart. The hooting of an owl
TOM came over the hill -- ominous sound! But no footsteps. Heavens, was
TOM everything lost! He was about to spring with winged feet, when a man
TOM cleared his throat not four feet from him! Huck's heart shot into his
TOM throat, but he swallowed it again; and then he stood there shaking as if
TOM a dozen agues had taken charge of him at once, and so weak that he
TOM thought he must surely fall to the ground. He knew where he was. He knew
TOM he was within five steps of the stile leading into Widow Douglas'
TOM grounds. Very well, he thought, let them bury it there; it won't be hard
TOM to find.
TOM 
TOM Now there was a voice -- a very low voice -- Injun Joe's:
TOM 
TOM ``Damn her, maybe she's got company -- there's lights, late as it is.''
TOM 
TOM ``I can't see any.''
TOM 
TOM This was that stranger's voice -- the stranger of the haunted house. A
TOM deadly chill went to Huck's heart -- this, then, was the ``revenge''
TOM job! His thought was, to fly. Then he remembered that the Widow Douglas
TOM had been kind to him more than once, and maybe these men were going to
TOM murder her. He wished he dared venture to warn her; but he knew he
TOM didn't dare -- they might come and catch him. He thought all this and
TOM more in the moment that elapsed between the stranger's remark and Injun
TOM Joe's next -- which was --
TOM 
TOM ``Because the bush is in your way. Now -- this way -- now you see, don't
TOM you?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes. Well, there IS company there, I reckon. Better give it up.''
TOM 
TOM ``Give it up, and I just leaving this country forever! Give it up and
TOM maybe never have another chance. I tell you again, as I've told you
TOM before, I don't care for her swag -- you may have it. But her husband
TOM was rough on me -- many times he was rough on me -- and mainly he was
TOM the justice of the peace that jugged me for a vagrant. And that ain't
TOM all. It ain't a millionth part of it! He had me HORSEWHIPPED! --
TOM horsewhipped in front of the jail, like a nigger! -- with all the town
TOM looking on! HORSEWHIPPED! -- do you understand? He took advantage of me
TOM and died. But I'll take it out of HER.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, don't kill her! Don't do that!''
TOM 
TOM ``Kill? Who said anything about killing? I would kill HIM if he was
TOM here; but not her. When you want to get revenge on a woman you don't
TOM kill her -- bosh! you go for her looks. You slit her nostrils -- you
TOM notch her ears like a sow!''
TOM 
TOM ``By God, that's --''
TOM 
TOM ``Keep your opinion to yourself! It will be safest for you. I'll tie her
TOM to the bed. If she bleeds to death, is that my fault? I'll not cry, if
TOM she does. My friend, you'll help me in this thing -- for MY sake --
TOM that's why you're here -- I mightn't be able alone. If you flinch, I'll
TOM kill you. Do you understand that? And if I have to kill you, I'll kill
TOM her -- and then I reckon nobody'll ever know much about who done this
TOM business.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, if it's got to be done, let's get at it. The quicker the better
TOM -- I'm all in a shiver.''
TOM 
TOM ``Do it NOW? And company there? Look here -- I'll get suspicious of you,
TOM first thing you know. No -- we'll wait till the lights are out --
TOM there's no hurry.''
TOM 
TOM Huck felt that a silence was going to ensue -- a thing still more awful
TOM than any amount of murderous talk; so he held his breath and stepped
TOM gingerly back; planted his foot carefully and firmly, after balancing,
TOM one-legged, in a precarious way and almost toppling over, first on one
TOM side and then on the other. He took another step back, with the same
TOM elaboration and the same risks; then another and another, and -- a twig
TOM snapped under his foot! His breath stopped and he listened. There was no
TOM sound -- the stillness was perfect. His gratitude was measureless. Now
TOM he turned in his tracks, between the walls of sumach bushes -- turned
TOM himself as carefully as if he were a ship -- and then stepped quickly
TOM but cautiously along. When he emerged at the quarry he felt secure, and
TOM so he picked up his nimble heels and flew. Down, down he sped, till he
TOM reached the Welshman's. He banged at the door, and presently the heads
TOM of the old man and his two stalwart sons were thrust from windows.
TOM 
TOM ``What's the row there? Who's banging? What do you want?''
TOM 
TOM ``Let me in -- quick! I'll tell everything.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, who are you?''
TOM 
TOM ``Huckleberry Finn -- quick, let me in!''
TOM 
TOM ``Huckleberry Finn, indeed! It ain't a name to open many doors, I judge!
TOM But let him in, lads, and let's see what's the trouble.''
TOM 
TOM ``Please don't ever tell I told you,'' were Huck's first words when he
TOM got in. ``Please don't -- I'd be killed, sure -- but the widow's been
TOM good friends to me sometimes, and I want to tell -- I WILL tell if
TOM you'll promise you won't ever say it was me.''
TOM 
TOM ``By George, he HAS got something to tell, or he wouldn't act so!''
TOM exclaimed the old man; ``out with it and nobody here'll ever tell,
TOM lad.''
TOM 
TOM Three minutes later the old man and his sons, well armed, were up the
TOM hill, and just entering the sumach path on tiptoe, their weapons in
TOM their hands. Huck accompanied them no further. He hid behind a great
TOM bowlder and fell to listening. There was a lagging, anxious silence, and
TOM then all of a sudden there was an explosion of firearms and a cry.
TOM 
TOM Huck waited for no particulars. He sprang away and sped down the hill as
TOM fast as his legs could carry him.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XXX
TOM 
TOM AS the earliest suspicion of dawn appeared on Sunday morning, Huck came
TOM groping up the hill and rapped gently at the old Welshman's door. The
TOM inmates were asleep, but it was a sleep that was set on a hair-trigger,
TOM on account of the exciting episode of the night. A call came from a
TOM window:
TOM 
TOM ``Who's there!''
TOM 
TOM Huck's scared voice answered in a low tone:
TOM 
TOM ``Please let me in! It's only Huck Finn!''
TOM 
TOM ``It's a name that can open this door night or day, lad! -- and
TOM welcome!''
TOM 
TOM These were strange words to the vagabond boy's ears, and the pleasantest
TOM he had ever heard. He could not recollect that the closing word had ever
TOM been applied in his case before. The door was quickly unlocked, and he
TOM entered. Huck was given a seat and the old man and his brace of tall
TOM sons speedily dressed themselves.
TOM 
TOM ``Now, my boy, I hope you're good and hungry, because breakfast will be
TOM ready as soon as the sun's up, and we'll have a piping hot one, too --
TOM make yourself easy about that! I and the boys hoped you'd turn up and
TOM stop here last night.''
TOM 
TOM ``I was awful scared,'' said Huck, ``and I run. I took out when the
TOM pistols went off, and I didn't stop for three mile. I've come now becuz
TOM I wanted to know about it, you know; and I come before daylight becuz I
TOM didn't want to run across them devils, even if they was dead.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, poor chap, you do look as if you'd had a hard night of it -- but
TOM there's a bed here for you when you've had your breakfast. No, they
TOM ain't dead, lad -- we are sorry enough for that. You see we knew right
TOM where to put our hands on them, by your description; so we crept along
TOM on tiptoe till we got within fifteen feet of them -- dark as a cellar
TOM that sumach path was -- and just then I found I was going to sneeze. It
TOM was the meanest kind of luck! I tried to keep it back, but no use --
TOM 'twas bound to come, and it did come! I was in the lead with my pistol
TOM raised, and when the sneeze started those scoundrels a-rustling to get
TOM out of the path, I sung out, 'Fire boys!' and blazed away at the place
TOM where the rustling was. So did the boys. But they were off in a jiffy,
TOM those villains, and we after them, down through the woods. I judge we
TOM never touched them. They fired a shot apiece as they started, but their
TOM bullets whizzed by and didn't do us any harm. As soon as we lost the
TOM sound of their feet we quit chasing, and went down and stirred up the
TOM constables. They got a posse together, and went off to guard the river
TOM bank, and as soon as it is light the sheriff and a gang are going to
TOM beat up the woods. My boys will be with them presently. I wish we had
TOM some sort of description of those rascals -- 'twould help a good deal.
TOM But you couldn't see what they were like, in the dark, lad, I suppose?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh yes; I saw them down-town and follered them.''
TOM 
TOM ``Splendid! Describe them -- describe them, my boy!''
TOM 
TOM ``One's the old deaf and dumb Spaniard that's ben around here once or
TOM twice, and t'other's a mean-looking, ragged --''
TOM 
TOM ``That's enough, lad, we know the men! Happened on them in the woods
TOM back of the widow's one day, and they slunk away. Off with you, boys,
TOM and tell the sheriff -- get your breakfast to-morrow morning!''
TOM 
TOM The Welshman's sons departed at once. As they were leaving the room Huck
TOM sprang up and exclaimed:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, please don't tell ANYbody it was me that blowed on them! Oh,
TOM please!''
TOM 
TOM ``All right if you say it, Huck, but you ought to have the credit of
TOM what you did.''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh no, no! Please don't tell!''
TOM 
TOM When the young men were gone, the old Welshman said:
TOM 
TOM ``They won't tell -- and I won't. But why don't you want it known?''
TOM 
TOM Huck would not explain, further than to say that he already knew too
TOM much about one of those men and would not have the man know that he knew
TOM anything against him for the whole world -- he would be killed for
TOM knowing it, sure.
TOM 
TOM The old man promised secrecy once more, and said:
TOM 
TOM ``How did you come to follow these fellows, lad? Were they looking
TOM suspicious?''
TOM 
TOM Huck was silent while he framed a duly cautious reply. Then he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, you see, I'm a kind of a hard lot, -- least everybody says so,
TOM and I don't see nothing agin it -- and sometimes I can't sleep much, on
TOM account of thinking about it and sort of trying to strike out a new way
TOM of doing. That was the way of it last night. I couldn't sleep, and so I
TOM come along up-street 'bout midnight, a-turning it all over, and when I
TOM got to that old shackly brick store by the Temperance Tavern, I backed
TOM up agin the wall to have another think. Well, just then along comes
TOM these two chaps slipping along close by me, with something under their
TOM arm, and I reckoned they'd stole it. One was a-smoking, and t'other one
TOM wanted a light; so they stopped right before me and the cigars lit up
TOM their faces and I see that the big one was the deaf and dumb Spaniard,
TOM by his white whiskers and the patch on his eye, and t'other one was a
TOM rusty, ragged-looking devil.''
TOM 
TOM ``Could you see the rags by the light of the cigars?''
TOM 
TOM This staggered Huck for a moment. Then he said:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, I don't know -- but somehow it seems as if I did.''
TOM 
TOM ``Then they went on, and you --''
TOM 
TOM ``Follered 'em -- yes. That was it. I wanted to see what was up -- they
TOM sneaked along so. I dogged 'em to the widder's stile, and stood in the
TOM dark and heard the ragged one beg for the widder, and the Spaniard swear
TOM he'd spile her looks just as I told you and your two --''
TOM 
TOM ``What! The DEAF AND DUMB man said all that!''
TOM 
TOM Huck had made another terrible mistake! He was trying his best to keep
TOM the old man from getting the faintest hint of who the Spaniard might be,
TOM and yet his tongue seemed determined to get him into trouble in spite of
TOM all he could do. He made several efforts to creep out of his scrape, but
TOM the old man's eye was upon him and he made blunder after blunder.
TOM Presently the Welshman said:
TOM 
TOM ``My boy, don't be afraid of me. I wouldn't hurt a hair of your head for
TOM all the world. No -- I'd protect you -- I'd protect you. This Spaniard
TOM is not deaf and dumb; you've let that slip without intending it; you
TOM can't cover that up now. You know something about that Spaniard that you
TOM want to keep dark. Now trust me -- tell me what it is, and trust me -- I
TOM won't betray you.''
TOM 
TOM Huck looked into the old man's honest eyes a moment, then bent over and
TOM whispered in his ear:
TOM 
TOM ``'Tain't a Spaniard -- it's Injun Joe!''
TOM 
TOM The Welshman almost jumped out of his chair. In a moment he said:
TOM 
TOM ``It's all plain enough, now. When you talked about notching ears and
TOM slitting noses I judged that that was your own embellishment, because
TOM white men don't take that sort of revenge. But an Injun! That's a
TOM different matter altogether.''
TOM 
TOM During breakfast the talk went on, and in the course of it the old man
TOM said that the last thing which he and his sons had done, before going to
TOM bed, was to get a lantern and examine the stile and its vicinity for
TOM marks of blood. They found none, but captured a bulky bundle of --
TOM 
TOM ``Of WHAT?''
TOM 
TOM If the words had been lightning they could not have leaped with a more
TOM stunning suddenness from Huck's blanched lips. His eyes were staring
TOM wide, now, and his breath suspended -- waiting for the answer. The
TOM Welshman started -- stared in return -- three seconds -- five seconds --
TOM ten -- then replied:
TOM 
TOM ``Of burglar's tools. Why, what's the MATTER with you?''
TOM 
TOM Huck sank back, panting gently, but deeply, unutterably grateful. The
TOM Welshman eyed him gravely, curiously -- and presently said:
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, burglar's tools. That appears to relieve you a good deal. But
TOM what did give you that turn? What were YOU expecting we'd found?''
TOM 
TOM Huck was in a close place -- the inquiring eye was upon him -- he would
TOM have given anything for material for a plausible answer -- nothing
TOM suggested itself -- the inquiring eye was boring deeper and deeper -- a
TOM senseless reply offered -- there was no time to weigh it, so at a
TOM venture he uttered it -- feebly:
TOM 
TOM ``Sunday-school books, maybe.''
TOM 
TOM Poor Huck was too distressed to smile, but the old man laughed loud and
TOM joyously, shook up the details of his anatomy from head to foot, and
TOM ended by saying that such a laugh was money in a-man's pocket, because
TOM it cut down the doctor's bill like everything. Then he added:
TOM 
TOM ``Poor old chap, you're white and jaded -- you ain't well a bit -- no
TOM wonder you're a little flighty and off your balance. But you'll come out
TOM of it. Rest and sleep will fetch you out all right, I hope.''
TOM 
TOM Huck was irritated to think he had been such a goose and betrayed such a
TOM suspicious excitement, for he had dropped the idea that the parcel
TOM brought from the tavern was the treasure, as soon as he had heard the
TOM talk at the widow's stile. He had only thought it was not the treasure,
TOM however -- he had not known that it wasn't -- and so the suggestion of a
TOM captured bundle was too much for his self-possession. But on the whole
TOM he felt glad the little episode had happened, for now he knew beyond all
TOM question that that bundle was not THE bundle, and so his mind was at
TOM rest and exceedingly comfortable. In fact, everything seemed to be
TOM drifting just in the right direction, now; the treasure must be still in
TOM No. 2, the men would be captured and jailed that day, and he and Tom
TOM could seize the gold that night without any trouble or any fear of
TOM interruption.
TOM 
TOM Just as breakfast was completed there was a knock at the door. Huck
TOM jumped for a hiding-place, for he had no mind to be connected even
TOM remotely with the late event. The Welshman admitted several ladies and
TOM gentlemen, among them the Widow Douglas, and noticed that groups of
TOM citizens were climbing up the hill -- to stare at the stile. So the news
TOM had spread. The Welshman had to tell the story of the night to the
TOM visitors. The widow's gratitude for her preservation was outspoken.
TOM 
TOM ``Don't say a word about it, madam. There's another that you're more
TOM beholden to than you are to me and my boys, maybe, but he don't allow me
TOM to tell his name. We wouldn't have been there but for him.''
TOM 
TOM Of course this excited a curiosity so vast that it almost belittled the
TOM main matter -- but the Welshman allowed it to eat into the vitals of his
TOM visitors, and through them be transmitted to the whole town, for he
TOM refused to part with his secret. When all else had been learned, the
TOM widow said:
TOM 
TOM ``I went to sleep reading in bed and slept straight through all that
TOM noise. Why didn't you come and wake me?''
TOM 
TOM ``We judged it warn't worth while. Those fellows warn't likely to come
TOM again -- they hadn't any tools left to work with, and what was the use
TOM of waking you up and scaring you to death? My three negro men stood
TOM guard at your house all the rest of the night. They've just come back.''
TOM 
TOM More visitors came, and the story had to be told and retold for a couple
TOM of hours more.
TOM 
TOM There was no Sabbath-school during day-school vacation, but everybody
TOM was early at church. The stirring event was well canvassed. News came
TOM that not a sign of the two villains had been yet discovered. When the
TOM sermon was finished, Judge Thatcher's wife dropped alongside of Mrs.
TOM Harper as she moved down the aisle with the crowd and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Is my Becky going to sleep all day? I just expected she would be tired
TOM to death.''
TOM 
TOM ``Your Becky?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes,'' with a startled look -- ``didn't she stay with you last
TOM night?''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, no.''
TOM 
TOM Mrs. Thatcher turned pale, and sank into a pew, just as Aunt Polly,
TOM talking briskly with a friend, passed by. Aunt Polly said:
TOM 
TOM ``Good-morning, Mrs. Thatcher. Good-morning, Mrs. Harper. I've got a boy
TOM that's turned up missing. I reckon my Tom stayed at your house last
TOM night -- one of you. And now he's afraid to come to church. I've got to
TOM settle with him.''
TOM 
TOM Mrs. Thatcher shook her head feebly and turned paler than ever.
TOM 
TOM ``He didn't stay with us,'' said Mrs. Harper, beginning to look uneasy.
TOM A marked anxiety came into Aunt Polly's face.
TOM 
TOM ``Joe Harper, have you seen my Tom this morning?''
TOM 
TOM ``No'm.''
TOM 
TOM ``When did you see him last?''
TOM 
TOM Joe tried to remember, but was not sure he could say. The people had
TOM stopped moving out of church. Whispers passed along, and a boding
TOM uneasiness took possession of every countenance. Children were anxiously
TOM questioned, and young teachers. They all said they had not noticed
TOM whether Tom and Becky were on board the ferryboat on the homeward trip;
TOM it was dark; no one thought of inquiring if any one was missing. One
TOM young man finally blurted out his fear that they were still in the cave!
TOM Mrs. Thatcher swooned away. Aunt Polly fell to crying and wringing her
TOM hands.
TOM 
TOM The alarm swept from lip to lip, from group to group, from street to
TOM street, and within five minutes the bells were wildly clanging and the
TOM whole town was up! The Cardiff Hill episode sank into instant
TOM insignificance, the burglars were forgotten, horses were saddled, skiffs
TOM were manned, the ferryboat ordered out, and before the horror was half
TOM an hour old, two hundred men were pouring down highroad and river toward
TOM the cave.
TOM 
TOM All the long afternoon the village seemed empty and dead. Many women
TOM visited Aunt Polly and Mrs. Thatcher and tried to comfort them. They
TOM cried with them, too, and that was still better than words. All the
TOM tedious night the town waited for news; but when the morning dawned at
TOM last, all the word that came was, ``Send more candles -- and send
TOM food.'' Mrs. Thatcher was almost crazed; and Aunt Polly, also. Judge
TOM Thatcher sent messages of hope and encouragement from the cave, but they
TOM conveyed no real cheer.
TOM 
TOM The old Welshman came home toward daylight, spattered with
TOM candle-grease, smeared with clay, and almost worn out. He found Huck
TOM still in the bed that had been provided for him, and delirious with
TOM fever. The physicians were all at the cave, so the Widow Douglas came
TOM and took charge of the patient. She said she would do her best by him,
TOM because, whether he was good, bad, or indifferent, he was the Lord's,
TOM and nothing that was the Lord's was a thing to be neglected. The
TOM Welshman said Huck had good spots in him, and the widow said:
TOM 
TOM ``You can depend on it. That's the Lord's mark. He don't leave it off.
TOM He never does. Puts it somewhere on every creature that comes from his
TOM hands.''
TOM 
TOM Early in the forenoon parties of jaded men began to straggle into the
TOM village, but the strongest of the citizens continued searching. All the
TOM news that could be gained was that remotenesses of the cavern were being
TOM ransacked that had never been visited before; that every corner and
TOM crevice was going to be thoroughly searched; that wherever one wandered
TOM through the maze of passages, lights were to be seen flitting hither and
TOM thither in the distance, and shoutings and pistol-shots sent their
TOM hollow reverberations to the ear down the sombre aisles. In one place,
TOM far from the section usually traversed by tourists, the names ``BECKY &
TOM TOM'' had been found traced upon the rocky wall with candle-smoke, and
TOM near at hand a grease-soiled bit of ribbon. Mrs. Thatcher recognized the
TOM ribbon and cried over it. She said it was the last relic she should ever
TOM have of her child; and that no other memorial of her could ever be so
TOM precious, because this one parted latest from the living body before the
TOM awful death came. Some said that now and then, in the cave, a far-away
TOM speck of light would glimmer, and then a glorious shout would burst
TOM forth and a score of men go trooping down the echoing aisle -- and then
TOM a sickening disappointment always followed; the children were not there;
TOM it was only a searcher's light.
TOM 
TOM Three dreadful days and nights dragged their tedious hours along, and
TOM the village sank into a hopeless stupor. No one had heart for anything.
TOM The accidental discovery, just made, that the proprietor of the
TOM Temperance Tavern kept liquor on his premises, scarcely fluttered the
TOM public pulse, tremendous as the fact was. In a lucid interval, Huck
TOM feebly led up to the subject of taverns, and finally asked -- dimly
TOM dreading the worst -- if anything had been discovered at the Temperance
TOM Tavern since he had been ill.
TOM 
TOM ``Yes,'' said the widow.
TOM 
TOM Huck started up in bed, wild-eyed:
TOM 
TOM ``What? What was it?''
TOM 
TOM ``Liquor! -- and the place has been shut up. Lie down, child -- what a
TOM turn you did give me!''
TOM 
TOM ``Only tell me just one thing -- only just one -- please! Was it Tom
TOM Sawyer that found it?''
TOM 
TOM The widow burst into tears. ``Hush, hush, child, hush! I've told you
TOM before, you must NOT talk. You are very, very sick!''
TOM 
TOM Then nothing but liquor had been found; there would have been a great
TOM powwow if it had been the gold. So the treasure was gone forever -- gone
TOM forever! But what could she be crying about? Curious that she should
TOM cry.
TOM 
TOM These thoughts worked their dim way through Huck's mind, and under the
TOM weariness they gave him he fell asleep. The widow said to herself:
TOM 
TOM ``There -- he's asleep, poor wreck. Tom Sawyer find it! Pity but
TOM somebody could find Tom Sawyer! Ah, there ain't many left, now, that's
TOM got hope enough, or strength enough, either, to go on searching.''
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XXXI
TOM 
TOM NOW to return to Tom and Becky's share in the picnic. They tripped along
TOM the murky aisles with the rest of the company, visiting the familiar
TOM wonders of the cave -- wonders dubbed with rather over-descriptive
TOM names, such as ``The Drawing-Room,'' ``The Cathedral,'' ``Aladdin's
TOM Palace,'' and so on. Presently the hide-and-seek frolicking began, and
TOM Tom and Becky engaged in it with zeal until the exertion began to grow a
TOM trifle wearisome; then they wandered down a sinuous avenue holding their
TOM candles aloft and reading the tangled web-work of names, dates,
TOM post-office addresses, and mottoes with which the rocky walls had been
TOM frescoed (in candle-smoke). Still drifting along and talking, they
TOM scarcely noticed that they were now in a part of the cave whose walls
TOM were not frescoed. They smoked their own names under an overhanging
TOM shelf and moved on. Presently they came to a place where a little stream
TOM of water, trickling over a ledge and carrying a limestone sediment with
TOM it, had, in the slow-dragging ages, formed a laced and ruffled Niagara
TOM in gleaming and imperishable stone. Tom squeezed his small body behind
TOM it in order to illuminate it for Becky's gratification. He found that it
TOM curtained a sort of steep natural stairway which was enclosed between
TOM narrow walls, and at once the ambition to be a discoverer seized him.
TOM Becky responded to his call, and they made a smoke-mark for future
TOM guidance, and started upon their quest. They wound this way and that,
TOM far down into the secret depths of the cave, made another mark, and
TOM branched off in search of novelties to tell the upper world about. In
TOM one place they found a spacious cavern, from whose ceiling depended a
TOM multitude of shining stalactites of the length and circumference of a
TOM man's leg; they walked all about it, wondering and admiring, and
TOM presently left it by one of the numerous passages that opened into it.
TOM This shortly brought them to a bewitching spring, whose basin was
TOM incrusted with a frostwork of glittering crystals; it was in the midst
TOM of a cavern whose walls were supported by many fantastic pillars which
TOM had been formed by the joining of great stalactites and stalagmites
TOM together, the result of the ceaseless water-drip of centuries. Under the
TOM roof vast knots of bats had packed themselves together, thousands in a
TOM bunch; the lights disturbed the creatures and they came flocking down by
TOM hundreds, squeaking and darting furiously at the candles. Tom knew their
TOM ways and the danger of this sort of conduct. He seized Becky's hand and
TOM hurried her into the first corridor that offered; and none too soon, for
TOM a bat struck Becky's light out with its wing while she was passing out
TOM of the cavern. The bats chased the children a good distance; but the
TOM fugitives plunged into every new passage that offered, and at last got
TOM rid of the perilous things. Tom found a subterranean lake, shortly,
TOM which stretched its dim length away until its shape was lost in the
TOM shadows. He wanted to explore its borders, but concluded that it would
TOM be best to sit down and rest awhile, first. Now, for the first time, the
TOM deep stillness of the place laid a clammy hand upon the spirits of the
TOM children. Becky said:
TOM 
TOM ``Why, I didn't notice, but it seems ever so long since I heard any of
TOM the others.''
TOM 
TOM ``Come to think, Becky, we are away down below them -- and I don't know
TOM how far away north, or south, or east, or whichever it is. We couldn't
TOM hear them here.''
TOM 
TOM Becky grew apprehensive.
TOM 
TOM ``I wonder how long we've been down here, Tom? We better start back.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, I reckon we better. P'raps we better.''
TOM 
TOM ``Can you find the way, Tom? It's all a mixed-up crookedness to me.''
TOM 
TOM ``I reckon I could find it -- but then the bats. If they put our candles
TOM out it will be an awful fix. Let's try some other way, so as not to go
TOM through there.''
TOM 
TOM ``Well. But I hope we won't get lost. It would be so awful!'' and the
TOM girl shuddered at the thought of the dreadful possibilities.
TOM 
TOM They started through a corridor, and traversed it in silence a long way,
TOM glancing at each new opening, to see if there was anything familiar
TOM about the look of it; but they were all strange. Every time Tom made an
TOM examination, Becky would watch his face for an encouraging sign, and he
TOM would say cheerily:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, it's all right. This ain't the one, but we'll come to it right
TOM away!''
TOM 
TOM But he felt less and less hopeful with each failure, and presently began
TOM to turn off into diverging avenues at sheer random, in desperate hope of
TOM finding the one that was wanted. He still said it was ``all right,'' but
TOM there was such a leaden dread at his heart that the words had lost their
TOM ring and sounded just as if he had said, ``All is lost!'' Becky clung to
TOM his side in an anguish of fear, and tried hard to keep back the tears,
TOM but they would come. At last she said:
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, Tom, never mind the bats, let's go back that way! We seem to get
TOM worse and worse off all the time.''
TOM 
TOM ``Listen!'' said he.
TOM 
TOM Profound silence; silence so deep that even their breathings were
TOM conspicuous in the hush. Tom shouted. The call went echoing down the
TOM empty aisles and died out in the distance in a faint sound that
TOM resembled a ripple of mocking laughter.
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, don't do it again, Tom, it is too horrid,'' said Becky.
TOM 
TOM ``It is horrid, but I better, Becky; they might hear us, you know,'' and
TOM he shouted again.
TOM 
TOM The ``might'' was even a chillier horror than the ghostly laughter, it
TOM so confessed a perishing hope. The children stood still and listened;
TOM but there was no result. Tom turned upon the back track at once, and
TOM hurried his steps. It was but a little while before a certain indecision
TOM in his manner revealed another fearful fact to Becky -- he could not
TOM find his way back!
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, Tom, you didn't make any marks!''
TOM 
TOM ``Becky, I was such a fool! Such a fool! I never thought we might want
TOM to come back! No -- I can't find the way. It's all mixed up.''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, Tom, we're lost! we're lost! We never can get out of this awful
TOM place! Oh, why DID we ever leave the others!''
TOM 
TOM She sank to the ground and burst into such a frenzy of crying that Tom
TOM was appalled with the idea that she might die, or lose her reason. He
TOM sat down by her and put his arms around her; she buried her face in his
TOM bosom, she clung to him, she poured out her terrors, her unavailing
TOM regrets, and the far echoes turned them all to jeering laughter. Tom
TOM begged her to pluck up hope again, and she said she could not. He fell
TOM to blaming and abusing himself for getting her into this miserable
TOM situation; this had a better effect. She said she would try to hope
TOM again, she would get up and follow wherever he might lead if only he
TOM would not talk like that any more. For he was no more to blame than she,
TOM she said.
TOM 
TOM So they moved on again -- aimlessly -- simply at random -- all they
TOM could do was to move, keep moving. For a little while, hope made a show
TOM of reviving -- not with any reason to back it, but only because it is
TOM its nature to revive when the spring has not been taken out of it by age
TOM and familiarity with failure.
TOM 
TOM By-and-by Tom took Becky's candle and blew it out. This economy meant so
TOM much! Words were not needed. Becky understood, and her hope died again.
TOM She knew that Tom had a whole candle and three or four pieces in his
TOM pockets -- yet he must economize.
TOM 
TOM By-and-by, fatigue began to assert its claims; the children tried to pay
TOM attention, for it was dreadful to think of sitting down when time was
TOM grown to be so precious, moving, in some direction, in any direction,
TOM was at least progress and might bear fruit; but to sit down was to
TOM invite death and shorten its pursuit.
TOM 
TOM At last Becky's frail limbs refused to carry her farther. She sat down.
TOM Tom rested with her, and they talked of home, and the friends there, and
TOM the comfortable beds and, above all, the light! Becky cried, and Tom
TOM tried to think of some way of comforting her, but all his encouragements
TOM were grown threadbare with use, and sounded like sarcasms. Fatigue bore
TOM so heavily upon Becky that she drowsed off to sleep. Tom was grateful.
TOM He sat looking into her drawn face and saw it grow smooth and natural
TOM under the influence of pleasant dreams; and by-and-by a smile dawned and
TOM rested there. The peaceful face reflected somewhat of peace and healing
TOM into his own spirit, and his thoughts wandered away to bygone times and
TOM dreamy memories. While he was deep in his musings, Becky woke up with a
TOM breezy little laugh -- but it was stricken dead upon her lips, and a
TOM groan followed it.
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, how COULD I sleep! I wish I never, never had waked! No! No, I
TOM don't, Tom! Don't look so! I won't say it again.''
TOM 
TOM ``I'm glad you've slept, Becky; you'll feel rested, now, and we'll find
TOM the way out.''
TOM 
TOM ``We can try, Tom; but I've seen such a beautiful country in my dream. I
TOM reckon we are going there.''
TOM 
TOM ``Maybe not, maybe not. Cheer up, Becky, and let's go on trying.''
TOM 
TOM They rose up and wandered along, hand in hand and hopeless. They tried
TOM to estimate how long they had been in the cave, but all they knew was
TOM that it seemed days and weeks, and yet it was plain that this could not
TOM be, for their candles were not gone yet. A long time after this -- they
TOM could not tell how long -- Tom said they must go softly and listen for
TOM dripping water -- they must find a spring. They found one presently, and
TOM Tom said it was time to rest again. Both were cruelly tired, yet Becky
TOM said she thought she could go a little farther. She was surprised to
TOM hear Tom dissent. She could not understand it. They sat down, and Tom
TOM fastened his candle to the wall in front of them with some clay. Thought
TOM was soon busy; nothing was said for some time. Then Becky broke the
TOM silence:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, I am so hungry!''
TOM 
TOM Tom took something out of his pocket.
TOM 
TOM ``Do you remember this?'' said he.
TOM 
TOM Becky almost smiled.
TOM 
TOM ``It's our wedding-cake, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes -- I wish it was as big as a barrel, for it's all we've got.''
TOM 
TOM ``I saved it from the picnic for us to dream on, Tom, the way grown-up
TOM people do with wedding-cake -- but it'll be our --''
TOM 
TOM She dropped the sentence where it was. Tom divided the cake and Becky
TOM ate with good appetite, while Tom nibbled at his moiety. There was
TOM abundance of cold water to finish the feast with. By-and-by Becky
TOM suggested that they move on again. Tom was silent a moment. Then he
TOM said:
TOM 
TOM ``Becky, can you bear it if I tell you something?''
TOM 
TOM Becky's face paled, but she thought she could.
TOM 
TOM ``Well, then, Becky, we must stay here, where there's water to drink.
TOM That little piece is our last candle!''
TOM 
TOM Becky gave loose to tears and wailings. Tom did what he could to comfort
TOM her, but with little effect. At length Becky said:
TOM 
TOM ``Tom!''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, Becky?''
TOM 
TOM ``They'll miss us and hunt for us!''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, they will! Certainly they will!''
TOM 
TOM ``Maybe they're hunting for us now, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, I reckon maybe they are. I hope they are.''
TOM 
TOM ``When would they miss us, Tom?''
TOM 
TOM ``When they get back to the boat, I reckon.''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom, it might be dark then -- would they notice we hadn't come?''
TOM 
TOM ``I don't know. But anyway, your mother would miss you as soon as they
TOM got home.''
TOM 
TOM A frightened look in Becky's face brought Tom to his senses and he saw
TOM that he had made a blunder. Becky was not to have gone home that night!
TOM The children became silent and thoughtful. In a moment a new burst of
TOM grief from Becky showed Tom that the thing in his mind had struck hers
TOM also -- that the Sabbath morning might be half spent before Mrs.
TOM Thatcher discovered that Becky was not at Mrs. Harper's.
TOM 
TOM The children fastened their eyes upon their bit of candle and watched it
TOM melt slowly and pitilessly away; saw the half inch of wick stand alone
TOM at last; saw the feeble flame rise and fall, climb the thin column of
TOM smoke, linger at its top a moment, and then -- the horror of utter
TOM darkness reigned!
TOM 
TOM How long afterward it was that Becky came to a slow consciousness that
TOM she was crying in Tom's arms, neither could tell. All that they knew
TOM was, that after what seemed a mighty stretch of time, both awoke out of
TOM a dead stupor of sleep and resumed their miseries once more. Tom said it
TOM might be Sunday, now -- maybe Monday. He tried to get Becky to talk, but
TOM her sorrows were too oppressive, all her hopes were gone. Tom said that
TOM they must have been missed long ago, and no doubt the search was going
TOM on. He would shout and maybe some one would come. He tried it; but in
TOM the darkness the distant echoes sounded so hideously that he tried it no
TOM more.
TOM 
TOM The hours wasted away, and hunger came to torment the captives again. A
TOM portion of Tom's half of the cake was left; they divided and ate it. But
TOM they seemed hungrier than before. The poor morsel of food only whetted
TOM desire.
TOM 
TOM By-and-by Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``SH! Did you hear that?''
TOM 
TOM Both held their breath and listened. There was a sound like the
TOM faintest, far-off shout. Instantly Tom answered it, and leading Becky by
TOM the hand, started groping down the corridor in its direction. Presently
TOM he listened again; again the sound was heard, and apparently a little
TOM nearer.
TOM 
TOM ``It's them!'' said Tom; ``they're coming! Come along, Becky -- we're
TOM all right now!''
TOM 
TOM The joy of the prisoners was almost overwhelming. Their speed was slow,
TOM however, because pitfalls were somewhat common, and had to be guarded
TOM against. They shortly came to one and had to stop. It might be three
TOM feet deep, it might be a hundred -- there was no passing it at any rate.
TOM Tom got down on his breast and reached as far down as he could. No
TOM bottom. They must stay there and wait until the searchers came. They
TOM listened; evidently the distant shoutings were growing more distant! a
TOM moment or two more and they had gone altogether. The heart-sinking
TOM misery of it! Tom whooped until he was hoarse, but it was of no use. He
TOM talked hopefully to Becky; but an age of anxious waiting passed and no
TOM sounds came again.
TOM 
TOM The children groped their way back to the spring. The weary time dragged
TOM on; they slept again, and awoke famished and woe-stricken. Tom believed
TOM it must be Tuesday by this time.
TOM 
TOM Now an idea struck him. There were some side passages near at hand. It
TOM would be better to explore some of these than bear the weight of the
TOM heavy time in idleness. He took a kite-line from his pocket, tied it to
TOM a projection, and he and Becky started, Tom in the lead, unwinding the
TOM line as he groped along. At the end of twenty steps the corridor ended
TOM in a ``jumping-off place.'' Tom got down on his knees and felt below,
TOM and then as far around the corner as he could reach with his hands
TOM conveniently; he made an effort to stretch yet a little farther to the
TOM right, and at that moment, not twenty yards away, a human hand, holding
TOM a candle, appeared from behind a rock! Tom lifted up a glorious shout,
TOM and instantly that hand was followed by the body it belonged to -- Injun
TOM Joe's! Tom was paralyzed; he could not move. He was vastly gratified the
TOM next moment, to see the ``Spaniard'' take to his heels and get himself
TOM out of sight. Tom wondered that Joe had not recognized his voice and
TOM come over and killed him for testifying in court. But the echoes must
TOM have disguised the voice. Without doubt, that was it, he reasoned. Tom's
TOM fright weakened every muscle in his body. He said to himself that if he
TOM had strength enough to get back to the spring he would stay there, and
TOM nothing should tempt him to run the risk of meeting Injun Joe again. He
TOM was careful to keep from Becky what it was he had seen. He told her he
TOM had only shouted ``for luck.''
TOM 
TOM But hunger and wretchedness rise superior to fears in the long run.
TOM Another tedious wait at the spring and another long sleep brought
TOM changes. The children awoke tortured with a raging hunger. Tom believed
TOM that it must be Wednesday or Thursday or even Friday or Saturday, now,
TOM and that the search had been given over. He proposed to explore another
TOM passage. He felt willing to risk Injun Joe and all other terrors. But
TOM Becky was very weak. She had sunk into a dreary apathy and would not be
TOM roused. She said she would wait, now, where she was, and die -- it would
TOM not be long. She told Tom to go with the kite-line and explore if he
TOM chose; but she implored him to come back every little while and speak to
TOM her; and she made him promise that when the awful time came, he would
TOM stay by her and hold her hand until all was over.
TOM 
TOM Tom kissed her, with a choking sensation in his throat, and made a show
TOM of being confident of finding the searchers or an escape from the cave;
TOM then he took the kite-line in his hand and went groping down one of the
TOM passages on his hands and knees, distressed with hunger and sick with
TOM bodings of coming doom.
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XXXII
TOM 
TOM TUESDAY afternoon came, and waned to the twilight. The village of St.
TOM Petersburg still mourned. The lost children had not been found. Public
TOM prayers had been offered up for them, and many and many a private prayer
TOM that had the petitioner's whole heart in it; but still no good news came
TOM from the cave. The majority of the searchers had given up the quest and
TOM gone back to their daily avocations, saying that it was plain the
TOM children could never be found. Mrs. Thatcher was very ill, and a great
TOM part of the time delirious. People said it was heartbreaking to hear her
TOM call her child, and raise her head and listen a whole minute at a time,
TOM then lay it wearily down again with a moan. Aunt Polly had drooped into
TOM a settled melancholy, and her gray hair had grown almost white. The
TOM village went to its rest on Tuesday night, sad and forlorn.
TOM 
TOM Away in the middle of the night a wild peal burst from the village
TOM bells, and in a moment the streets were swarming with frantic half-clad
TOM people, who shouted, ``Turn out! turn out! they're found! they're
TOM found!'' Tin pans and horns were added to the din, the population massed
TOM itself and moved toward the river, met the children coming in an open
TOM carriage drawn by shouting citizens, thronged around it, joined its
TOM homeward march, and swept magnificently up the main street roaring
TOM huzzah after huzzah!
TOM 
TOM The village was illuminated; nobody went to bed again; it was the
TOM greatest night the little town had ever seen. During the first half-hour
TOM a procession of villagers filed through Judge Thatcher's house, seized
TOM the saved ones and kissed them, squeezed Mrs. Thatcher's hand, tried to
TOM speak but couldn't -- and drifted out raining tears all over the place.
TOM 
TOM Aunt Polly's happiness was complete, and Mrs. Thatcher's nearly so. It
TOM would be complete, however, as soon as the messenger dispatched with the
TOM great news to the cave should get the word to her husband. Tom lay upon
TOM a sofa with an eager auditory about him and told the history of the
TOM wonderful adventure, putting in many striking additions to adorn it
TOM withal; and closed with a description of how he left Becky and went on
TOM an exploring expedition; how he followed two avenues as far as his
TOM kite-line would reach; how he followed a third to the fullest stretch of
TOM the kite-line, and was about to turn back when he glimpsed a far-off
TOM speck that looked like daylight; dropped the line and groped toward it,
TOM pushed his head and shoulders through a small hole, and saw the broad
TOM Mississippi rolling by! And if it had only happened to be night he would
TOM not have seen that speck of daylight and would not have explored that
TOM passage any more! He told how he went back for Becky and broke the good
TOM news and she told him not to fret her with such stuff, for she was
TOM tired, and knew she was going to die, and wanted to. He described how he
TOM labored with her and convinced her; and how she almost died for joy when
TOM she had groped to where she actually saw the blue speck of daylight; how
TOM he pushed his way out at the hole and then helped her out; how they sat
TOM there and cried for gladness; how some men came along in a skiff and Tom
TOM hailed them and told them their situation and their famished condition;
TOM how the men didn't believe the wild tale at first, ``because,'' said
TOM they, ``you are five miles down the river below the valley the cave is
TOM in'' -- then took them aboard, rowed to a house, gave them supper, made
TOM them rest till two or three hours after dark and then brought them home.
TOM 
TOM Before day-dawn, Judge Thatcher and the handful of searchers with him
TOM were tracked out, in the cave, by the twine clews they had strung behind
TOM them, and informed of the great news.
TOM 
TOM Three days and nights of toil and hunger in the cave were not to be
TOM shaken off at once, as Tom and Becky soon discovered. They were
TOM bedridden all of Wednesday and Thursday, and seemed to grow more and
TOM more tired and worn, all the time. Tom got about, a little, on Thursday,
TOM was down-town Friday, and nearly as whole as ever Saturday; but Becky
TOM did not leave her room until Sunday, and then she looked as if she had
TOM passed through a wasting illness.
TOM 
TOM Tom learned of Huck's sickness and went to see him on Friday, but could
TOM not be admitted to the bedroom; neither could he on Saturday or Sunday.
TOM He was admitted daily after that, but was warned to keep still about his
TOM adventure and introduce no exciting topic. The Widow Douglas stayed by
TOM to see that he obeyed. At home Tom learned of the Cardiff Hill event;
TOM also that the ``ragged man's'' body had eventually been found in the
TOM river near the ferry-landing; he had been drowned while trying to
TOM escape, perhaps.
TOM 
TOM About a fortnight after Tom's rescue from the cave, he started off to
TOM visit Huck, who had grown plenty strong enough, now, to hear exciting
TOM talk, and Tom had some that would interest him, he thought. Judge
TOM Thatcher's house was on Tom's way, and he stopped to see Becky. The
TOM Judge and some friends set Tom to talking, and some one asked him
TOM ironically if he wouldn't like to go to the cave again. Tom said he
TOM thought he wouldn't mind it. The Judge said:
TOM 
TOM ``Well, there are others just like you, Tom, I've not the least doubt.
TOM But we have taken care of that. Nobody will get lost in that cave any
TOM more.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why?''
TOM 
TOM ``Because I had its big door sheathed with boiler iron two weeks ago,
TOM and triple-locked -- and I've got the keys.''
TOM 
TOM Tom turned as white as a sheet.
TOM 
TOM ``What's the matter, boy! Here, run, somebody! Fetch a glass of water!''
TOM 
TOM The water was brought and thrown into Tom's face.
TOM 
TOM ``Ah, now you're all right. What was the matter with you, Tom?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, Judge, Injun Joe's in the cave!''
TOM 
TOM 
TOM Chapter XXXIII
TOM 
TOM WITHIN a few minutes the news had spread, and a dozen skiff-loads of men
TOM were on their way to McDougal's cave, and the ferryboat, well filled
TOM with passengers, soon followed. Tom Sawyer was in the skiff that bore
TOM Judge Thatcher.
TOM 
TOM When the cave door was unlocked, a sorrowful sight presented itself in
TOM the dim twilight of the place. Injun Joe lay stretched upon the ground,
TOM dead, with his face close to the crack of the door, as if his longing
TOM eyes had been fixed, to the latest moment, upon the light and the cheer
TOM of the free world outside. Tom was touched, for he knew by his own
TOM experience how this wretch had suffered. His pity was moved, but
TOM nevertheless he felt an abounding sense of relief and security, now,
TOM which revealed to him in a degree which he had not fully appreciated
TOM before how vast a weight of dread had been lying upon him since the day
TOM he lifted his voice against this bloody-minded outcast.
TOM 
TOM Injun Joe's bowie-knife lay close by, its blade broken in two. The great
TOM foundation-beam of the door had been chipped and hacked through, with
TOM tedious labor; useless labor, too, it was, for the native rock formed a
TOM sill outside it, and upon that stubborn material the knife had wrought
TOM no effect; the only damage done was to the knife itself. But if there
TOM had been no stony obstruction there the labor would have been useless
TOM still, for if the beam had been wholly cut away Injun Joe could not have
TOM squeezed his body under the door, and he knew it. So he had only hacked
TOM that place in order to be doing something -- in order to pass the weary
TOM time -- in order to employ his tortured faculties. Ordinarily one could
TOM find half a dozen bits of candle stuck around in the crevices of this
TOM vestibule, left there by tourists; but there were none now. The prisoner
TOM had searched them out and eaten them. He had also contrived to catch a
TOM few bats, and these, also, he had eaten, leaving only their claws. The
TOM poor unfortunate had starved to death. In one place, near at hand, a
TOM stalagmite had been slowly growing up from the ground for ages, builded
TOM by the water-drip from a stalactite overhead. The captive had broken off
TOM the stalagmite, and upon the stump had placed a stone, wherein he had
TOM scooped a shallow hollow to catch the precious drop that fell once in
TOM every three minutes with the dreary regularity of a clock-tick -- a
TOM dessertspoonful once in four and twenty hours. That drop was falling
TOM when the Pyramids were new; when Troy fell; when the foundations of Rome
TOM were laid when Christ was crucified; when the Conqueror created the
TOM British empire; when Columbus sailed; when the massacre at Lexington was
TOM ``news.'' It is falling now; it will still be falling when all these
TOM things shall have sunk down the afternoon of history, and the twilight
TOM of tradition, and been swallowed up in the thick night of oblivion. Has
TOM everything a purpose and a mission? Did this drop fall patiently during
TOM five thousand years to be ready for this flitting human insect's need?
TOM and has it another important object to accomplish ten thousand years to
TOM come? No matter. It is many and many a year since the hapless half-breed
TOM scooped out the stone to catch the priceless drops, but to this day the
TOM tourist stares longest at that pathetic stone and that slow-dropping
TOM water when he comes to see the wonders of McDougal's cave. Injun Joe's
TOM cup stands first in the list of the cavern's marvels; even ``Aladdin's
TOM Palace'' cannot rival it.
TOM 
TOM Injun Joe was buried near the mouth of the cave; and people flocked
TOM there in boats and wagons from the towns and from all the farms and
TOM hamlets for seven miles around; they brought their children, and all
TOM sorts of provisions, and confessed that they had had almost as
TOM satisfactory a time at the funeral as they could have had at the
TOM hanging.
TOM 
TOM This funeral stopped the further growth of one thing -- the petition to
TOM the governor for Injun Joe's pardon. The petition had been largely
TOM signed; many tearful and eloquent meetings had been held, and a
TOM committee of sappy women been appointed to go in deep mourning and wail
TOM around the governor, and implore him to be a merciful ass and trample
TOM his duty under foot. Injun Joe was believed to have killed five citizens
TOM of the village, but what of that? If he had been Satan himself there
TOM would have been plenty of weaklings ready to scribble their names to a
TOM pardon-petition, and drip a tear on it from their permanently impaired
TOM and leaky water-works.
TOM 
TOM The morning after the funeral Tom took Huck to a private place to have
TOM an important talk. Huck had learned all about Tom's adventure from the
TOM Welshman and the Widow Douglas, by this time, but Tom said he reckoned
TOM there was one thing they had not told him; that thing was what he wanted
TOM to talk about now. Huck's face saddened. He said:
TOM 
TOM ``I know what it is. You got into No. 2 and never found anything but
TOM whiskey. Nobody told me it was you; but I just knowed it must 'a' ben
TOM you, soon as I heard 'bout that whiskey business; and I knowed you
TOM hadn't got the money becuz you'd 'a' got at me some way or other and
TOM told me even if you was mum to everybody else. Tom, something's always
TOM told me we'd never get holt of that swag.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, Huck, I never told on that tavern-keeper. YOU know his tavern was
TOM all right the Saturday I went to the picnic. Don't you remember you was
TOM to watch there that night?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh yes! Why, it seems 'bout a year ago. It was that very night that I
TOM follered Injun Joe to the widder's.''
TOM 
TOM ``YOU followed him?''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes -- but you keep mum. I reckon Injun Joe's left friends behind him,
TOM and I don't want 'em souring on me and doing me mean tricks. If it
TOM hadn't ben for me he'd be down in Texas now, all right.''
TOM 
TOM Then Huck told his entire adventure in confidence to Tom, who had only
TOM heard of the Welshman's part of it before.
TOM 
TOM ``Well,'' said Huck, presently, coming back to the main question,
TOM ``whoever nipped the whiskey in No. 2, nipped the money, too, I reckon
TOM -- anyways it's a goner for us, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, that money wasn't ever in No. 2!''
TOM 
TOM ``What!'' Huck searched his comrade's face keenly. ``Tom, have you got
TOM on the track of that money again?''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, it's in the cave!''
TOM 
TOM Huck's eyes blazed.
TOM 
TOM ``Say it again, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``The money's in the cave!''
TOM 
TOM ``Tom -- honest injun, now -- is it fun, or earnest?''
TOM 
TOM ``Earnest, Huck -- just as earnest as ever I was in my life. Will you go
TOM in there with me and help get it out?''
TOM 
TOM ``I bet I will! I will if it's where we can blaze our way to it and not
TOM get lost.''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, we can do that without the least little bit of trouble in the
TOM world.''
TOM 
TOM ``Good as wheat! What makes you think the money's --''
TOM 
TOM ``Huck, you just wait till we get in there. If we don't find it I'll
TOM agree to give you my drum and every thing I've got in the world. I will,
TOM by jings.''
TOM 
TOM ``All right -- it's a whiz. When do you say?''
TOM 
TOM ``Right now, if you say it. Are you strong enough?''
TOM 
TOM ``Is it far in the cave? I ben on my pins a little, three or four days,
TOM now, but I can't walk more'n a mile, Tom -- least I don't think I
TOM could.''
TOM 
TOM ``It's about five mile into there the way anybody but me would go, Huck,
TOM but there's a mighty short cut that they don't anybody but me know
TOM about. Huck, I'll take you right to it in a skiff. I'll float the skiff
TOM down there, and I'll pull it back again all by myself. You needn't ever
TOM turn your hand over.''
TOM 
TOM ``Less start right off, Tom.''
TOM 
TOM ``All right. We want some bread and meat, and our pipes, and a little
TOM bag or two, and two or three kite-strings, and some of these new-fangled
TOM things they call lucifer matches. I tell you, many's the time I wished I
TOM had some when I was in there before.''
TOM 
TOM A trifle after noon the boys borrowed a small skiff from a citizen who
TOM was absent, and got under way at once. When they were several miles
TOM below ``Cave Hollow,'' Tom said:
TOM 
TOM ``Now you see this bluff here looks all alike all the way down from the
TOM cave hollow -- no houses, no wood-yards, bushes all alike. But do you
TOM see that white place up yonder where there's been a landslide? Well,
TOM that's one of my marks. We'll get ashore, now.''
TOM 
TOM They landed.
TOM 
TOM ``Now, Huck, where we're a-standing you could touch that hole I got out
TOM of with a fishing-pole. See if you can find it.''
TOM 
TOM Huck searched all the place about, and found nothing. Tom proudly
TOM marched into a thick clump of sumach bushes and said:
TOM 
TOM ``Here you are! Look at it, Huck; it's the snuggest hole in this
TOM country. You just keep mum about it. All along I've been wanting to be a
TOM robber, but I knew I'd got to have a thing like this, and where to run
TOM across it was the bother. We've got it now, and we'll keep it quiet,
TOM only we'll let Joe Harper and Ben Rogers in -- because of course there's
TOM got to be a Gang, or else there wouldn't be any style about it. Tom
TOM Sawyer's Gang -- it sounds splendid, don't it, Huck?''
TOM 
TOM ``Well, it just does, Tom. And who'll we rob?''
TOM 
TOM ``Oh, most anybody. Waylay people -- that's mostly the way.''
TOM 
TOM ``And kill them?''
TOM 
TOM ``No, not always. Hive them in the cave till they raise a ransom.''
TOM 
TOM ``What's a ransom?''
TOM 
TOM ``Money. You make them raise all they can, off'n their friends; and
TOM after you've kept them a year, if it ain't raised then you kill them.
TOM That's the general way. Only you don't kill the women. You shut up the
TOM women, but you don't kill them. They're always beautiful and rich, and
TOM awfully scared. You take their watches and things, but you always take
TOM your hat off and talk polite. They ain't anybody as polite as robbers --
TOM you'll see that in any book. Well, the women get to loving you, and
TOM after they've been in the cave a week or two weeks they stop crying and
TOM after that you couldn't get them to leave. If you drove them out they'd
TOM turn right around and come back. It's so in all the books.''
TOM 
TOM ``Why, it's real bully, Tom. I believe it's better'n to be a pirate.''
TOM 
TOM ``Yes, it's better in some ways, because it's close to home and circuses
TOM and all that.''
TOM 
TOM By this time everything was ready and the boys entered the hole, Tom in
